الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
الوسط أن هذه الأمور التي يقال لها المتولّدات حاصلة بسبب فعل العبد، وبالأسباب الأخرى التي يخلقها الله. فالشبع يحصل بأكل العبد وابتلاعه، وبما جعله الله في الإنسان، وفي الغذاء من القوى المعينة على حصول الشبع (١). إذن فإن القول بالسببية أمر يؤكده الإيمان أو الوحي من غير نشوب مفتعل لثنائية الخالق أو الفاعل وقدرة المخلوق وفاعليته على نحو من الندية والمنازعة. ذلك أن المسلّمة الأساس هنا تنسجم مع خالقية الله – تعالى – وفاعليته المطلقة، وأمره - سبحانه - لنا بالسير وفق منطق السنن المبثوثة في عالمي الآفاق والأنفس، وفي ضوء قانون السير والنظر:
وَقُلْ سِيرُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ فَانظُرُوا كَيْفَ بَدَأَ الْخَلْق ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٢٠/٢٩]. وهذه الآية تشير بوضوح إلى أن بداية الخلق ليست خاصة بعالم الأنفس فقط، كما قد يتبادر إلى الذهن السطحي، بل إن السير في الأرض يتحقق بتتبع صنع الله وآياته في الخلق والإنشاء، في الجمادات والكائنات الحية على السواء (٣). وفي ذلك ما يشير إلى أن لا تعارض بين حركة العبد النسبية وقدرة الله المطلقة. ولكون الإنسان أرقى مخلوق لاستخلافه دون سواه، فإن الخطاب القرآني يشير الله الجامعة بين قدرة الله المطلقة وحركة العبد النسبية المحدودة. ولكن لا بد أن يكون ذلك وفق قراءة كلية تجمع بين الآيات في مواضعها المختلفة، حتى لا نقع في النظرة التجزيئية للنص القرآني. فإذا كان الله تعالى قد قال:
وَنُرِيدُ أَن لَمُنَّ عَلَى الَّذِينَ اسْتُضْعِفُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَنَجْعَلَهُمْ أَئِمَّةً وَنَجْعَلَهُمُ الْوَارِثِينَ، وَتُمَكِّنَ لَهُمْ فِي الأَرْضِ وَنُرِيَ فِرْعَوْنَ وَهَامَانَ وَجُنُودَهُما مِنْهُمْ ما كانُوا يَحْذَرُونَ﴾ [القصص: ٥/٢٨-٦].
وإنَّ الْأَرْضَ لِلَّهِ يُورِثُهَا مَنْ يَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ وَالْعَاقِبَةُ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٢٨/٧].
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
وَإِذا أَرَدْنا أَنْ نُهْلِكَ قَرْيَةً أَمَرْنَا مُتْرَفِيها فَفَسَقُوا فِيهَا فَحَقَّ عَلَيْهَا الْقَوْلُ فَدَمَّرْناها تدميرا (١) [الإسراء: ١٦/١٧].
فلا بد أن تفهم تلك الآيات في ضوء ما تقرره آيات أخرى تصرح بمسؤولية الإنسان:
وَكُلَّ إنسان أَلْزَمْنَاهُ طَائِرَهُ فِي عُنُقِهِ... [الإسراء: ١٣/١٧].
وَأَن لَيْسَ لِلإِنسان إلا ما سعى... [النجم: ٣٩/٥٣].
فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْراً يَرَهُ، وَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًا يَرَهُ [الزلزلة: ٧/٩٩-٨].
و نفهمها كذلك في ضوء تلك الآيات المقررة لحرية الإنسان واختياره وإرادته:
وَهَدَيْنَاهُ النَّجْدَيْنِ﴾ [البلد: ١٠/٩٠].
وإنا هَدَيْناهُ السَّبِيلَ إمّا شاكِراً وَإِما كَفُوراً) [الإنسان: ٣/٧٦].
وإلى جانب تأكيد الوحي على حتمية منطق السننية ممثلة في مظهر السببية وقانونها معا ؛ فإن منطق العلم هو الآخر يرفض فكرة التلقائية والمصادفة والظروف الطارئة، بل يعتمد على قانون السبب والمسبب (السببية). وذلك ما يعبر عنه منهج البحث العلمي اليوم بمصطلح المتغيرين المستقل (٢) والتابع (٣). ولذلك فالحتمية السببية مفهوم أساسي يقوم عليه العلم، وفي ضوئها يتم تفسير الظواهر المختلفة. وذلك ما ينبغي أن تتبناه وتشدد على التزامه التربية الإسلامية، وأن تعكس ذلك عبر عناصر المنهج. وأن يعزز ذلك قيام المعلم بتفسير الظواهر المختلفة أثناء تدريسه وفق قانون السببية، كي يتحقق الأمر ذاته في المتعلم.

The middle [position] is that these things called generated effects occur due to the action of the servant and due to the other causes that God creates. For satiety occurs by the servant's eating and swallowing, and by what God has placed in humans and in food of powers that assist in achieving satiety (1). "And when We intend to destroy a city, We command its affluent, and they commit wickedness therein, so the word is justified against it, and We destroy it utterly" [al-Isra 16/17].

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument for the law of causality (sababiyya) from both revelation and science. The author begins by stating the middle position (al-wasat) regarding generated effects (al-mutawalladāt): they occur due to the action of the servant (fi‘l al-‘abd) and due to other causes created by God. The example of satiety (shib‘) is given: it results from the servant's eating and swallowing, but also from the powers God placed in the human body and in food. This shows that causality does not imply a dualistic rivalry between Creator and creature; rather, it is affirmed by faith and revelation without such a conflict. The author then quotes the Quranic command to travel and see how creation began, interpreting it as an invitation to observe causality in both the physical world and the human soul. This verse, he argues, refutes a superficial understanding that limits creation to the inner world—it includes inanimate objects and living beings alike. The passage then emphasizes that there is no contradiction between the relative movement of the servant and God's absolute power. The Quranic discourse, particularly verses on divine will and human responsibility, must be read holistically to avoid a fragmented view. Verses such as 'And We intended to confer favor upon those who were oppressed' and 'Indeed, the earth belongs to Allah' are cited alongside verses affirming human responsibility and free will: 'Every human being We have bound his fate to his neck,' 'Man has only what he strives for,' and the atom's weight of good and evil. Thus, causal determinism (al-ḥatmiyya al-sababiyya) is a foundational concept of science, and Islamic education should adopt and emphasize it, with teachers explaining phenomena through the lens of causality so that students internalize this principle.

The author argues that the command 'Travel throughout the earth' is not limited to inner reflection but includes:
A) Only observing human souls.

Scientific Affirmation of Causality and Its Educational Implications
Author argues that science affirms causality, and Islamic education should embody this.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to connect the scientific principle of causality to Islamic education and curriculum design.

Core Idea
Science and revelation both affirm causality; Islamic education must reflect this.

The author extends his argument from revelation to science, noting that modern scientific methodology is built on causality. This has direct implications for how we teach. Let's explore the scientific side and its application to Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the author's claim about science
The author states that the logic of science (manṭiq al-‘ilm) rejects spontaneity and coincidence, and relies on the law of cause and effect.
This is a key bridge between revelation and modern science.
2
Understand the terms 'independent variable' and 'dependent variable'
The author mentions these as the contemporary scientific expression of causality. The independent variable is the cause, the dependent variable is the effect.
These are standard terms in scientific methodology.
3
Explain why causal determinism is fundamental to science
The passage asserts that causal determinism (al-ḥatmiyya al-sababiyya) is a foundational concept of science; phenomena are interpreted in light of it.
Without causality, scientific explanation and prediction would be impossible.
4
Discuss the implication for Islamic education
The author argues that Islamic education should adopt and emphasize causality in its curriculum. Teachers should explain phenomena according to the law of causality, so that students internalize this principle.
This aligns the Islamic worldview with scientific rationality.

الوسط أن هذه الأمور التي يقال لها المتولّدات حاصلة بسبب فعل العبد، وبالأسباب الأخرى التي يخلقها الله. فالشبع يحصل بأكل العبد وابتلاعه، وبما جعله الله في الإنسان، وفي الغذاء من القوى المعينة على حصول الشبع (١). إذن فإن القول بالسببية أمر يؤكده الإيمان أو الوحي من غير نشوب مفتعل لثنائية الخالق أو الفاعل وقدرة المخلوق وفاعليته على نحو من الندية والمنازعة. ذلك أن المسلّمة الأساس هنا تنسجم مع خالقية الله – تعالى – وفاعليته المطلقة، وأمره - سبحانه - لنا بالسير وفق منطق السنن المبثوثة في عالمي الآفاق والأنفس، وفي ضوء قانون السير والنظر:
وَقُلْ سِيرُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ فَانظُرُوا كَيْفَ بَدَأَ الْخَلْق ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٢٠/٢٩]. وهذه الآية تشير بوضوح إلى أن بداية الخلق ليست خاصة بعالم الأنفس فقط، كما قد يتبادر إلى الذهن السطحي، بل إن السير في الأرض يتحقق بتتبع صنع الله وآياته في الخلق والإنشاء، في الجمادات والكائنات الحية على السواء (٣). وفي ذلك ما يشير إلى أن لا تعارض بين حركة العبد النسبية وقدرة الله المطلقة. ولكون الإنسان أرقى مخلوق لاستخلافه دون سواه، فإن الخطاب القرآني يشير الله الجامعة بين قدرة الله المطلقة وحركة العبد النسبية المحدودة. ولكن لا بد أن يكون ذلك وفق قراءة كلية تجمع بين الآيات في مواضعها المختلفة، حتى لا نقع في النظرة التجزيئية للنص القرآني. فإذا كان الله تعالى قد قال:
وَنُرِيدُ أَن لَمُنَّ عَلَى الَّذِينَ اسْتُضْعِفُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَنَجْعَلَهُمْ أَئِمَّةً وَنَجْعَلَهُمُ الْوَارِثِينَ، وَتُمَكِّنَ لَهُمْ فِي الأَرْضِ وَنُرِيَ فِرْعَوْنَ وَهَامَانَ وَجُنُودَهُما مِنْهُمْ ما كانُوا يَحْذَرُونَ﴾ [القصص: ٥/٢٨-٦].
وإنَّ الْأَرْضَ لِلَّهِ يُورِثُهَا مَنْ يَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ وَالْعَاقِبَةُ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٢٨/٧].
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
وَإِذا أَرَدْنا أَنْ نُهْلِكَ قَرْيَةً أَمَرْنَا مُتْرَفِيها فَفَسَقُوا فِيهَا فَحَقَّ عَلَيْهَا الْقَوْلُ فَدَمَّرْناها تدميرا (١) [الإسراء: ١٦/١٧].
فلا بد أن تفهم تلك الآيات في ضوء ما تقرره آيات أخرى تصرح بمسؤولية الإنسان:
وَكُلَّ إنسان أَلْزَمْنَاهُ طَائِرَهُ فِي عُنُقِهِ... [الإسراء: ١٣/١٧].
وَأَن لَيْسَ لِلإِنسان إلا ما سعى... [النجم: ٣٩/٥٣].
فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْراً يَرَهُ، وَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًا يَرَهُ [الزلزلة: ٧/٩٩-٨].
و نفهمها كذلك في ضوء تلك الآيات المقررة لحرية الإنسان واختياره وإرادته:
وَهَدَيْنَاهُ النَّجْدَيْنِ﴾ [البلد: ١٠/٩٠].
وإنا هَدَيْناهُ السَّبِيلَ إمّا شاكِراً وَإِما كَفُوراً) [الإنسان: ٣/٧٦].
وإلى جانب تأكيد الوحي على حتمية منطق السننية ممثلة في مظهر السببية وقانونها معا ؛ فإن منطق العلم هو الآخر يرفض فكرة التلقائية والمصادفة والظروف الطارئة، بل يعتمد على قانون السبب والمسبب (السببية). وذلك ما يعبر عنه منهج البحث العلمي اليوم بمصطلح المتغيرين المستقل (٢) والتابع (٣). ولذلك فالحتمية السببية مفهوم أساسي يقوم عليه العلم، وفي ضوئها يتم تفسير الظواهر المختلفة. وذلك ما ينبغي أن تتبناه وتشدد على التزامه التربية الإسلامية، وأن تعكس ذلك عبر عناصر المنهج. وأن يعزز ذلك قيام المعلم بتفسير الظواهر المختلفة أثناء تدريسه وفق قانون السببية، كي يتحقق الأمر ذاته في المتعلم.
Chapter Three, Section Two: The Intellect
The middle [position] is that these things called generated effects occur due to the action of the servant and due to the other causes that God creates. For satiety occurs by the servant's eating and swallowing, and by what God has placed in humans and in food of powers that assist in achieving satiety (1). Therefore, the statement of causality is a matter affirmed by faith or revelation, without an artificial emergence of a duality of the Creator or the agent and the creature's ability and efficacy in a manner of parity and contention. That is because the basic premise here harmonizes with God's creatorship and His absolute efficacy, and His command for us to proceed according to the logic of the laws spread in the worlds of horizons and souls, and in light of the law of travel and contemplation:
"And say, 'Travel throughout the earth and see how He began creation'" [al-Ankabut 20/29]. This verse clearly indicates that the beginning of creation is not specific to the world of souls only, as might come to a superficial mind, but rather travel in the earth is achieved by tracing God's making and His signs in creation and origination, in inanimate objects and living beings alike (3). In that is an indication that there is no contradiction between the relative movement of the servant and God's absolute power. And because man is the most noble creature due to his vicegerency uniquely, the Quranic discourse indicates the comprehensive [relationship] between God's absolute power and the relative limited movement of the servant. But this must be according to a holistic reading that brings together the verses in their different places, so that we do not fall into a fragmentary view of the Quranic text. For if Allah has said:
"And We intended to confer favor upon those who were oppressed in the land and make them leaders and make them the inheritors, and establish them in the land and show Pharaoh and Haman and their soldiers that which they feared" [al-Qasas 5/28-6].
"And indeed, the earth belongs to Allah; He causes to inherit it whom He wills of His servants, and the [best] outcome is for the righteous" [al-A'raf 128/7].
Chapter Three, Section Two: The Intellect
"And when We intend to destroy a city, We command its affluent, and they commit wickedness therein, so the word is justified against it, and We destroy it utterly" [al-Isra 16/17].
So it is necessary to understand those verses in light of what other verses establish that explicitly state human responsibility:
"And every human being We have bound his fate to his neck..." [al-Isra 13/17].
"And that man has only what he strives for..." [al-Najm 39/53].
"So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it" [al-Zalzala 7/99-8].
And we understand them also in light of those verses that establish human freedom, choice, and will:
"And We guided him to the two paths" [al-Balad 10/90].
"Indeed, We guided him to the way, either grateful or ungrateful" [al-Insan 3/76].
And alongside revelation's affirmation of the inevitability of the logic of the laws (sunan) represented in the appearance of causality and its law together, the logic of science also rejects the idea of spontaneity, coincidence, and emergent circumstances, but rather relies on the law of cause and effect (causality). That is what is expressed today by scientific research methodology in the term independent variable (2) and dependent variable (3). Therefore, causal determinism is a fundamental concept upon which science is built, and in its light various phenomena are interpreted. That is what Islamic education should adopt and emphasize its commitment, and reflect that through the elements of the curriculum. And that should be reinforced by the teacher explaining various phenomena during his teaching according to the law of causality, so that the same thing is realized in the learner.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument for the law of causality (sababiyya) from both revelation and science. The author begins by stating the middle position (al-wasat) regarding generated effects (al-mutawalladāt): they occur due to the action of the servant (fi‘l al-‘abd) and due to other causes created by God. The example of satiety (shib‘) is given: it results from the servant's eating and swallowing, but also from the powers God placed in the human body and in food. This shows that causality does not imply a dualistic rivalry between Creator and creature; rather, it is affirmed by faith and revelation without such a conflict. The author then quotes the Quranic command to travel and see how creation began, interpreting it as an invitation to observe causality in both the physical world and the human soul. This verse, he argues, refutes a superficial understanding that limits creation to the inner world—it includes inanimate objects and living beings alike. The passage then emphasizes that there is no contradiction between the relative movement of the servant and God's absolute power. The Quranic discourse, particularly verses on divine will and human responsibility, must be read holistically to avoid a fragmented view. Verses such as 'And We intended to confer favor upon those who were oppressed' and 'Indeed, the earth belongs to Allah' are cited alongside verses affirming human responsibility and free will: 'Every human being We have bound his fate to his neck,' 'Man has only what he strives for,' and the atom's weight of good and evil. These are reconciled with verses on free will: 'We guided him to the two paths.' The author then turns to science, noting that alongside revelation's affirmation of the law of causality, the logic of science also rejects spontaneity and coincidence, relying on cause and effect. Modern scientific methodology expresses this with the terms independent variable (al-mutaghayyir al-mustaqill) and dependent variable (al-tābi‘). Thus, causal determinism (al-ḥatmiyya al-sababiyya) is a foundational concept of science, and Islamic education should adopt and emphasize it, with teachers explaining phenomena through the lens of causality so that students internalize this principle.

Key Terms
الحتمية السببية
المتغير المستقل
المتغير التابع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a fundamental concept upon which science is built?
A) Spontaneity and coincidence.
B) Causal determinism.
C) The idea that phenomena have no cause.
D) Random chance.

Key Takeaway
The law of causality is a shared foundation between revelation and science, and Islamic education should embody this principle in its curriculum and teaching methods.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Suppose you are an Islamic school teacher. Design a short presentation that uses the verse 'And say, Travel throughout the earth...' (29:20) to introduce the concept of variables in a science class. Identify an independent and dependent variable in a natural phenomenon (e.g., sunlight and plant growth) and explain the causal relationship while acknowledging Allah as the ultimate cause.

Reconciling Divine Causality with Human Responsibility in the Quran
Author explains Quranic verses on destruction as consistent with human free will and causal determinism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Quranic verses on divine punishment are consistent with human free will and causal determinism using the author's hermeneutical principle.

Core Idea
Quranic causality does not negate human responsibility; it operates through it.

This passage tackles a foundational epistemological challenge: how to reconcile verses that describe God's direct destruction of cities with those that stress human accountability and free choice. The author argues that these must be understood together, not in isolation. He further connects this Quranic principle of causality (al-sunaniyya) to the scientific law of cause and effect, asserting that Islamic education should instill this integrated worldview.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent tension
Read the opening verse: 'When We intend to destroy a city...' This seems to describe purely divine action. Now note the author's immediate response: such verses must be understood in light of other verses. What is the tension?
The tension is between divine control and human freedom.
2
Extract the verses on human responsibility
The author cites three sets: (1) 'Every person We have imposed his fate upon his neck' (al-Isra 17:13), (2) 'Man has only that for which he strives' (al-Najm 53:39), (3) 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' (al-Zalzalah 99:7-8). List what each affirms about human agency.
These verses establish that humans are accountable for their own deeds.
3
Extract the verses on free will
The author then quotes: 'We guided him to the two paths' (al-Balad 90:10) and 'We guided him to the way, whether grateful or ungrateful' (al-Insan 76:3). What do these add to the picture?
They explicitly affirm that humans have a choice between alternatives.
4
Understand the link to scientific causality
The author asserts that the logic of the sunna (divine pattern) manifests as causality, and that science also rejects randomness, relying on cause and effect. How does this bridge the Quranic worldview with modern scientific thinking?
Both see a deterministic framework, but within it human choices are real causes.
5
Grasp the pedagogical conclusion
The author argues that Islamic education should adopt this causal determinism and teachers should explain phenomena through causality. Why is this important for the learner?
It trains the student to see order and responsibility, not fatalism.

وَإِذا أَرَدْنا أَنْ نُهْلِكَ قَرْيَةً أَمَرْنَا مُتْرَفِيها فَفَسَقُوا فِيهَا فَحَقَّ عَلَيْهَا الْقَوْلُ فَدَمَّرْناها تدميرا. فلا بد أن تفهم تلك الآيات في ضوء ما تقرره آيات أخرى تصرح بمسؤولية الإنسان: ﴿وَكُلَّ إنسان أَلْزَمْنَاهُ طَائِرَهُ فِي عُنُقِهِ... ﴿وَأَن لَيْسَ لِلإِنسان إلا ما سعى... ﴿فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْراً يَرَهُ، وَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًا يَرَهُ ﴾. و نفهمها كذلك في ضوء تلك الآيات المقررة لحرية الإنسان واختياره وإرادته: ﴿وَهَدَيْنَاهُ النَّجْدَيْنِ﴾. ﴿إنا هَدَيْناهُ السَّبِيلَ إمّا شاكِراً وَإِما كَفُوراً﴾. وإلى جانب تأكيد الوحي على حتمية منطق السننية ممثلة في مظهر السببية وقانونها معا ؛ فإن منطق العلم هو الآخر يرفض فكرة التلقائية والمصادفة والظروف الطارئة، بل يعتمد على قانون السبب والمسبب (السببية). وذلك ما يعبر عنه منهج البحث العلمي اليوم بمصطلح المتغيرين المستقل والتابع. ولذلك فالحتمية السببية مفهوم أساسي يقوم عليه العلم، وفي ضوئها يتم تفسير الظواهر المختلفة. وذلك ما ينبغي أن تتبناه وتشدد على التزامه التربية الإسلامية، وأن تعكس ذلك عبر عناصر المنهج. وأن يعزز ذلك قيام المعلم بتفسير الظواهر المختلفة أثناء تدريسه وفق قانون السببية، كي يتحقق الأمر ذاته في المتعلم.
And when We intend to destroy a city, We command its affluent ones, and they commit wickedness therein, so the word is justified against it, and We destroy it completely. Commentary
This passage begins by citing a Quranic verse about the destruction of a city, then immediately cautions that such verses must be understood alongside other Quranic verses that affirm human responsibility and free will. The author quotes verses about personal accountability (each soul bears its own burden), the principle that man gets only what he strives for, and the precise weighing of deeds. Then verses on guidance of the two paths and free choice are cited. The author then links this Quranic emphasis on causality (sunna) to the scientific method, which also rejects randomness and relies on cause and effect. He states that causal determinism is foundational to science, and therefore Islamic education must instill this principle. The teacher should explain phenomena through causality so that students internalize it.

Key Takeaway
Quranic verses on divine action and human responsibility must be interpreted together; this integration aligns with the scientific principle of causality and should guide Islamic education.

The Relativity of the Intellect and Its Limitations
The author argues that the intellect's judgments are not absolute due to temporal-spatial confinement and sensory dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two key limitations of the human intellect—temporal-spatial confinement and the inability to conceive infinitude—as argued in the passage.

Core Idea
The intellect is bounded by time and space, unable to grasp the infinite.

The Quran elevates reason, but this passage warns against absolutizing its judgments. The author shows that the intellect is confined by time, space, and sensory data, and is incapable of resolving fundamental dilemmas such as the finitude or infinitude of the universe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two limitations
The author states the intellect is confined between time and space (mahsur bayn al-zaman wa al-makan) and cannot conceive of things that transcend them, like great truths that have no time or place. Also, it cannot settle the finite/infinite dilemma for the universe.
These are presented as inherent boundaries.
2
Examine the finite/infinite dilemma
The intellect hesitates between the universe being finite or infinite. If finite, the question 'what is after the end?' arises; if infinite, the intellect cannot conceive of something without end. This indecision proves its limits.
The author uses this as a concrete example of intellectual limitation.
3
Connect to sensory dependence
The passage then argues that the intellect only works with sensory data, reinforcing its relativity. Without senses, no judgment is possible.
This is further developed in subsequent sections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
نسبية العقل
تلك الأهمية التي يوليها القرآن للعقل، ومع تلك الخصائص التي يتميز بها ؛ فإن ذلك لا يعني إطلاقية الأحكام الناتجة عنه. وقد سبق القول: إن أحكامه ليست على مستوى واحد من حيث دلالتها على اليقين، فهي تبدأ من الحق بيقين وتنتهي إلى الباطل بيقين. ولأن العقل محصور بين الزمان والمكان؛ فإن السؤال الذي يُطرح دائماً متى؟ وأين؟ . في حين أن الحقائق الكبرى لا زمان لها ولا مكان بيد أن العقل يعجز عن تصور ذلك، فتراه يعلن عجزه عن التسليم بواحد من احتمالين لا ثالث لهما هل الكون متناهي الحدود؟ أو غير متناهي الحدود؟ فهو في تسلسل تصوراته يصل إلى حد فوق عوالم المجرات عاجزا عن التفكير لا يستطيع أن يقتنع باللانهاية، أو أن يسلم بالنهاية، فيحتار بين سؤالين هل انتهى الكون؟ فإذا قبل قفز وهمه ليسأل: وماذا بعد النهاية؟ وإذا قال لنفسه الكون لا نهاية له قفز منطقة المشدود إلى المحسوسات للسؤال: كيف يكون شيء لا نهاية له؟. وهذا التردد بين الاحتمالين وعدم استطاعة العقل الاقتناع بواحد منهما دليل على حدوده.
إن هذا يؤكد أن العقل لا يعمل - إذن - إلا بموجب معطيات الحواس. فالقوة العاقلة في الإنسان هي التي تجمع بين المصوِّرة والذاكرة والمخيلة والذكاء فتقوم بعملها تحليلاً وتركيباً وجمعاً وتفريقاً واستنتاجاً للقواعد العامة والكليات. وبناء على ذلك فإن وظيفة الحواس نقل مشاهدتها في الكون مرئياً كان أم مسموعاً أم مشموماً أم ملموساً أم متذوقاً إلى العقل (المصورة)، فيصدر أحكامه بموجب بياناتها. ومن دون عرض أشرطة الحواس تلك يتعذر على العقل إصدار أي حكم، ولذلك تقول القاعدة الثابتة: الحكم على الشيء فرع عن تصوره.
ومن خبرات الحياة اليومية - في مجال التعليم - التي تزيد من توضيح هذه النسبية في العقل ما يشير إليه أحد الباحثين من كون المدرس قد لا يستطيع استرجاع اسم تلميذ سابق، أو عنوان كتاب قرره في العام الماضي، أو المكان الذي أوقف فيه سيارته كما قد لا يستطيع استرجاع أشياء كثيرة مرت بخبرته سابقاً، ولذلك فإن الفرد قد لا يسترجع غالباً إلا الأشياء التي يرغب في استرجاعها. ومن الأمثلة على ذلك يقول هذا الباحث : إن الطفل يتذكر بقوة أن أمه وعدته بأنها ستصحبه إلى السيرك يوم السبت، لكنه ينسى بسرعة أنها قد طلبت منه أن يشذب الحديقة، تماماً كما أن العالم قد يتذكر الأشياء التي تدعم معتقداته أكثر من غيرها. والأمر ذاته قد يحصل في التفكير والاستدلال حتى عند الأفراد شديدي الذكاء، وذلك إما لخطأ في التفكير والاستدلال، أو نتيجة لاستخدام لوسائل إحصائية وتجريبية غير مناسبة. وقد ينتج ذلك أيضاً لتحيّز انفعالي، كما هو الحاصل عند ذلك الطفل الذي تذکر بشدّة حقه في موعد أمه له، في حين نسى واجبه في تشذيب الحديقة، أو حتى لدى العالم الذي يتذكر ما يدعم معتقداته دون أن يولي الاهتمام ذاته لما يخالفها. وهذا ما كشفت عنه بعض الدراسات التجريبية الحديثة في علم النفس. فقد قدمت بعض البراهين القياسية إلى مجموعة من الطلبة، وطلب منهم تبيين ما إذا كانت النتيجة منطقية من المقدمتين المستخدمتين في القياس. فتبين أن نصف البراهين القياسية -وهي متعلقة بأمور الحياة العادية - أقل خطأ لدى جميع الطلبة، في حين وقعوا جميعاً في أخطاء في النصف المتعلق بالأمور التي من شأنها أن تثير الانفعال. وصدق الله: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَجِيبُوا لَكَ فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّمَا يَتَّبِعُونَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنِ اتَّبَعَ هَوَاهُ بِغَيْرِ هُدَى مِنْ اللَّهِ... [القصص: ٥٠/٢٨]. ريا داوُودُ إِنا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ فَاحْكُمْ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ بِالْحَقِّ وَلَا
Chapter 3, Section 2 - The Intellect. Relativity of the Intellect. That importance which the Quran gives to the intellect, and with those characteristics by which it is distinguished, does not mean the absoluteness of the judgments resulting from it. And it has been said previously: Its judgments are not at one level in terms of their indication of certainty; they begin from truth with certainty and end with falsehood with certainty. And because the intellect is confined between time and space, the question that is always asked is: When? And Where? While the great truths have no time and no place, but the intellect is incapable of conceiving that, so you see it declaring its inability to accept one of two possibilities with no third: Is the universe finite in boundaries? Or infinite in boundaries? So in the sequence of its conceptions, it reaches a limit beyond the worlds of galaxies, incapable of thinking, unable to be convinced of infinity, or to accept finitude, so it hesitates between two questions: Did the universe end? If it accepts, its imagination jumps to ask: And what is after the end? And if it tells itself the universe has no end, it jumps to the realm of the attached to the sensible to ask: How can there be a thing with no end? And this hesitation between the two possibilities and the inability of the intellect to be convinced of either is evidence of its limits. This confirms that the intellect does not work except according to the data of the senses. The rational faculty in man is that which combines the representative faculty, memory, imagination, and intelligence, and performs its work of analysis, synthesis, combination, differentiation, and deduction of general rules and universals. And accordingly, the function of the senses is to transmit their observations in the universe, whether seen, heard, smelled, touched, or tasted, to the intellect (the representative faculty), and it issues its judgments according to their data. Without presenting those sensory tapes, it is impossible for the intellect to issue any judgment, and therefore the established rule says: Judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception. And from the experiences of daily life - in the field of education - that further clarify this relativity in the intellect is what one researcher points to: that a teacher may not be able to recall the name of a former student, or the title of a book he decided last year, or the place where he parked his car, and he may not be able to recall many things that passed through his experience previously. Therefore, the individual often does not retrieve except the things he desires to retrieve. And among the examples of that, this researcher says: The child strongly remembers that his mother promised to take him to the circus on Saturday, but he quickly forgets that she asked him to trim the garden, just as the scientist may remember things that support his beliefs more than others. And the same thing can happen in thinking and reasoning even among highly intelligent individuals, either due to error in thinking and reasoning, or as a result of using inappropriate statistical and experimental methods. And that may also result from emotional bias, as is the case with that child who strongly remembers his right to his mother's appointment, while forgetting his duty to trim the garden, or even with the scientist who remembers what supports his beliefs without giving the same attention to what contradicts them. And this is what some modern experimental studies in psychology have revealed. Some syllogistic proofs were presented to a group of students, and they were asked to indicate whether the conclusion was logical from the two premises used in the syllogism. It became clear that half of the syllogistic proofs - which were related to ordinary life matters - had less error among all students, while they all made errors in the half related to matters that would arouse emotion. And God speaks the truth: {But if they do not respond to you, then know that they only follow their desires. And who is more astray than one who follows his desire without guidance from Allah...} [Al-Qasas 28:50]. O Dawud, indeed We have made you a successor upon the earth, so judge between the people with truth and do not...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument about the nature and limits of the human intellect from an Islamic perspective. The author begins by acknowledging the high status the Quran gives to the intellect, but immediately clarifies that this does not mean the judgments of the intellect are absolute. On the contrary, intellectual judgments vary in their degree of certainty, ranging from certain truth to certain falsehood. The author then identifies a key limitation: the intellect is bounded by time and space, and thus constantly asks 'when?' and 'where?' for everything. However, ultimate realities (al-haqa'iq al-kubra) transcend time and space, and the intellect is incapable of conceiving them. To illustrate, the author presents the dilemma of whether the universe is finite or infinite. The intellect cannot settle either possibility; accepting finitude leads immediately to the question 'what is beyond the end?', and accepting infinity defies the intellect's dependence on the sensible world. This hesitation is presented as proof of the intellect's limits. The author then argues that the intellect operates solely based on sensory data. The rational faculty (al-quwwa al-'aqila) integrates the functions of the representative faculty (musawwira), memory, imagination, and intelligence, performing analysis, synthesis, and deduction of general rules. The senses transmit their observations to the intellect, and without such sensory input, the intellect cannot make any judgment. This is encapsulated in the principle: 'Judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' (al-hukm 'ala al-shay' far'un 'an tasawwurih). To further demonstrate the relativity of the intellect, the author provides examples from daily life and educational experience. A teacher may forget a student's name or where he parked his car; a child vividly remembers a promise of a circus trip but forgets a chore; a scientist recalls evidence that supports his theory while ignoring contradictory data. The same bias occurs in reasoning and inference, even among highly intelligent people, due to errors in thinking, inappropriate statistical methods, or emotional bias. The author cites experimental psychological studies where students made fewer errors on neutral syllogisms but more errors on emotionally charged ones. The passage concludes with two Quranic verses: one from Surah Al-Qasas (28:50) warning against following desires, and a partial verse from Surah Sad (38:26) about judging with truth, emphasizing that emotional bias leads away from truth.

Key Terms
العقل
نسبية العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the intellect's inability to settle whether the universe is finite or infinite prove?
A) That the universe is infinite.
B) That the intellect has limits.
C) That the senses are unreliable.
D) That the Quran contradicts reason.

Key Takeaway
The intellect is bounded by time, space, and sensory experience, and is incapable of conceiving of the infinite or of truths that transcend these categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a contemporary scientific or theological issue where the intellect's limitation (as described in this passage) becomes apparent. Explain how the finite/infinite dilemma or temporal confinement applies.

intermediate
5 min
Sensory Dependence and the Principle of Conception
The author presents the rule 'judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' to emphasize sensory dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the principle 'judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' and demonstrate its role in the intellect's reliance on sensory data.

Core Idea
No judgment without prior conception, and no conception without sensory input.

The author states a foundational rule: you cannot judge something you haven't conceived. Since conception itself depends on the senses, all intellectual judgments ultimately rest on sensory experience.

Guided Path
1
Locate the principle in Arabic
Find the sentence: 'الحكم على الشيء فرع عن تصوره' (Judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception). Recognize that this is presented as an established rule (qā‘ida thābita).
2
Define tasawwur and hukm
Tasawwur (conception) is the mental representation of a thing. Hukm (judgment) is an assertion about that thing. The principle states that without first having a conception, no judgment can be made.
In classical logic, tasawwur and tasdiq (assent) are the two main mental acts.
3
Explain the dependency chain
The author argues that the intellect relies on sensory data to form conceptions. The senses transmit observations to the intellect (musawwira), which then forms conceptions. Without sensory input, no conception is possible, and thus no judgment.
This ties the principle to empiricism.
4
Apply the principle to an Islamic example
Consider the ruling on riba (usury). A jurist must first have a correct conception of what riba is (based on Quran and Sunnah) before issuing a judgment (hukm) about it. The judgment is 'branched' on the conception.
This shows the practical importance in usul al-fiqh.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
نسبية العقل
تلك الأهمية التي يوليها القرآن للعقل، ومع تلك الخصائص التي يتميز بها ؛ فإن ذلك لا يعني إطلاقية الأحكام الناتجة عنه. وقد سبق القول: إن أحكامه ليست على مستوى واحد من حيث دلالتها على اليقين، فهي تبدأ من الحق بيقين وتنتهي إلى الباطل بيقين. ولأن العقل محصور بين الزمان والمكان؛ فإن السؤال الذي يُطرح دائماً متى؟ وأين؟ . في حين أن الحقائق الكبرى لا زمان لها ولا مكان بيد أن العقل يعجز عن تصور ذلك، فتراه يعلن عجزه عن التسليم بواحد من احتمالين لا ثالث لهما هل الكون متناهي الحدود؟ أو غير متناهي الحدود؟ فهو في تسلسل تصوراته يصل إلى حد فوق عوالم المجرات عاجزا عن التفكير لا يستطيع أن يقتنع باللانهاية، أو أن يسلم بالنهاية، فيحتار بين سؤالين هل انتهى الكون؟ فإذا قبل قفز وهمه ليسأل: وماذا بعد النهاية؟ وإذا قال لنفسه الكون لا نهاية له قفز منطقة المشدود إلى المحسوسات للسؤال: كيف يكون شيء لا نهاية له؟. وهذا التردد بين الاحتمالين وعدم استطاعة العقل الاقتناع بواحد منهما دليل على حدوده.

Chapter 3, Section 2 - The Intellect. Relativity of the Intellect. That importance which the Quran gives to the intellect, and with those characteristics by which it is distinguished, does not mean the absoluteness of the judgments resulting from it. And it has been said previously: Its judgments are not at one level in terms of their indication of certainty; they begin from truth with certainty and end with falsehood with certainty. And because the intellect is confined between time and space, the question that is always asked is: When? And Where? Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument about the nature and limits of the human intellect from an Islamic perspective. The author begins by acknowledging the high status the Quran gives to the intellect, but immediately clarifies that this does not mean the judgments of the intellect are absolute. On the contrary, intellectual judgments vary in their degree of certainty, ranging from certain truth to certain falsehood. The author then identifies a key limitation: the intellect is bounded by time and space, and thus constantly asks 'when?' and 'where?' for everything. However, ultimate realities (al-haqa'iq al-kubra) transcend time and space, and the intellect is incapable of conceiving them. To illustrate, the author presents the dilemma of whether the universe is finite or infinite. The intellect cannot settle either possibility; accepting finitude leads immediately to the question 'what is beyond the end?', and accepting infinity defies the intellect's dependence on the sensible world. This hesitation is presented as proof of the intellect's limits. The author then argues that the intellect operates solely based on sensory data. The rational faculty (al-quwwa al-'aqila) integrates the functions of the representative faculty (musawwira), memory, imagination, and intelligence, performing analysis, synthesis, and deduction of general rules. The senses transmit their observations to the intellect, and without such sensory input, the intellect cannot make any judgment. This is encapsulated in the principle: 'Judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' (al-hukm 'ala al-shay' far'un 'an tasawwurih). To further demonstrate the relativity of the intellect, the author provides examples from daily life and educational experience. A teacher may forget a student's name or where he parked his car; a child vividly remembers a promise of a circus trip but forgets a chore; a scientist recalls evidence that supports his theory while ignoring contradictory data. The same bias occurs in reasoning and inference, even among highly intelligent people, due to errors in thinking, inappropriate statistical methods, or emotional bias. The author cites experimental psychological studies where students made fewer errors on neutral syllogisms but more errors on emotionally charged ones. The passage concludes with two Quranic verses: one from Surah Al-Qasas (28:50) warning against following desires, and a partial verse from Surah Sad (38:26) about judging with truth, emphasizing that emotional bias leads away from truth.

Checkpoint
What does the author mean by 'judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' (الحكم على الشيء فرع عن تصوره)?
A) A judgment can be made without any conception.
B) Conception is derived from judgment.
C) Conception must precede judgment.
D) Judgment and conception are independent.

Key Takeaway
All intellectual judgments depend on prior conception, which itself relies on sensory data—the intellect is fundamentally empirical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Explain how the principle 'judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' applies to the ruling on intoxication (khamr). What must be conceived before ruling it as haram?

Emotional Bias and Its Impact on Reasoning
The author uses examples and psychological research to show that emotional bias distorts reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how emotional bias (infi'al) leads to errors in logical reasoning, using the examples and psychological study from the passage.

Core Idea
Emotions hijack reason, causing selective recall and flawed logic.

The passage shows that even intelligent people make logical errors when emotions are involved. Drawing on daily examples and psychological experiments, the author demonstrates that emotional bias distorts memory and reasoning, and concludes with a Quranic warning against following desires.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of bias mentioned
The author mentions memory bias (e.g., teacher forgetting, child remembering only what benefits him) and confirmation bias (scientist remembering evidence supporting his beliefs). These are both driven by emotional preference.
The term 'infi'al' (emotional arousal) is used.
2
Analyze the child and scientist examples
The child vividly remembers the circus promise (positive emotion) but forgets the chore (duty). The scientist selectively recalls supporting evidence. This shows bias in what is stored and retrieved.
These examples illustrate that desire affects memory.
3
Understand the psychological study
Students were given syllogisms. Half about neutral daily matters, half about emotionally charged topics. Errors were higher on the emotional ones. This proves that emotion impairs logical inference.
The study is used as empirical evidence.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
The author quotes 'But if they do not respond to you, then know that they only follow their desires' (Al-Qasas 28:50). This links emotional bias to following hawa (desire), which is condemned as leading to error.
Thus, the argument has both empirical and scriptural grounding.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
نسبية العقل
تلك الأهمية التي يوليها القرآن للعقل، ومع تلك الخصائص التي يتميز بها ؛ فإن ذلك لا يعني إطلاقية الأحكام الناتجة عنه. وقد سبق القول: إن أحكامه ليست على مستوى واحد من حيث دلالتها على اليقين، فهي تبدأ من الحق بيقين وتنتهي إلى الباطل بيقين. ولأن العقل محصور بين الزمان والمكان؛ فإن السؤال الذي يُطرح دائماً متى؟ وأين؟ . في حين أن الحقائق الكبرى لا زمان لها ولا مكان بيد أن العقل يعجز عن تصور ذلك، فتراه يعلن عجزه عن التسليم بواحد من احتمالين لا ثالث لهما هل الكون متناهي الحدود؟ أو غير متناهي الحدود؟ فهو في تسلسل تصوراته يصل إلى حد فوق عوالم المجرات عاجزا عن التفكير لا يستطيع أن يقتنع باللانهاية، أو أن يسلم بالنهاية، فيحتار بين سؤالين هل انتهى الكون؟ فإذا قبل قفز وهمه ليسأل: وماذا بعد النهاية؟ وإذا قال لنفسه الكون لا نهاية له قفز منطقة المشدود إلى المحسوسات للسؤال: كيف يكون شيء لا نهاية له؟. وهذا التردد بين الاحتمالين وعدم استطاعة العقل الاقتناع بواحد منهما دليل على حدوده.
إن هذا يؤكد أن العقل لا يعمل - إذن - إلا بموجب معطيات الحواس. فالقوة العاقلة في الإنسان هي التي تجمع بين المصوِّرة والذاكرة والمخيلة والذكاء فتقوم بعملها تحليلاً وتركيباً وجمعاً وتفريقاً واستنتاجاً للقواعد العامة والكليات. وبناء على ذلك فإن وظيفة الحواس نقل مشاهدتها في الكون مرئياً كان أم مسموعاً أم مشموماً أم ملموساً أم متذوقاً إلى العقل (المصورة)، فيصدر أحكامه بموجب بياناتها. ومن دون عرض أشرطة الحواس تلك يتعذر على العقل إصدار أي حكم، ولذلك تقول القاعدة الثابتة: الحكم على الشيء فرع عن تصوره.
ومن خبرات الحياة اليومية - في مجال التعليم - التي تزيد من توضيح هذه النسبية في العقل ما يشير إليه أحد الباحثين من كون المدرس قد لا يستطيع استرجاع اسم تلميذ سابق، أو عنوان كتاب قرره في العام الماضي، أو المكان الذي أوقف فيه سيارته كما قد لا يستطيع استرجاع أشياء كثيرة مرت بخبرته سابقاً، ولذلك فإن الفرد قد لا يسترجع غالباً إلا الأشياء التي يرغب في استرجاعها. ومن الأمثلة على ذلك يقول هذا الباحث : إن الطفل يتذكر بقوة أن أمه وعدته بأنها ستصحبه إلى السيرك يوم السبت، لكنه ينسى بسرعة أنها قد طلبت منه أن يشذب الحديقة، تماماً كما أن العالم قد يتذكر الأشياء التي تدعم معتقداته أكثر من غيرها. والأمر ذاته قد يحصل في التفكير والاستدلال حتى عند الأفراد شديدي الذكاء، وذلك إما لخطأ في التفكير والاستدلال، أو نتيجة لاستخدام لوسائل إحصائية وتجريبية غير مناسبة. وقد ينتج ذلك أيضاً لتحيّز انفعالي، كما هو الحاصل عند ذلك الطفل الذي تذکر بشدّة حقه في موعد أمه له، في حين نسى واجبه في تشذيب الحديقة، أو حتى لدى العالم الذي يتذكر ما يدعم معتقداته دون أن يولي الاهتمام ذاته لما يخالفها. وهذا ما كشفت عنه بعض الدراسات التجريبية الحديثة في علم النفس. فقد قدمت بعض البراهين القياسية إلى مجموعة من الطلبة، وطلب منهم تبيين ما إذا كانت النتيجة منطقية من المقدمتين المستخدمتين في القياس. فتبين أن نصف البراهين القياسية -وهي متعلقة بأمور الحياة العادية - أقل خطأ لدى جميع الطلبة، في حين وقعوا جميعاً في أخطاء في النصف المتعلق بالأمور التي من شأنها أن تثير الانفعال. وصدق الله: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَجِيبُوا لَكَ فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّمَا يَتَّبِعُونَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنِ اتَّبَعَ هَوَاهُ بِغَيْرِ هُدَى مِنْ اللَّهِ... [القصص: ٥٠/٢٨]. ريا داوُودُ إِنا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ فَاحْكُمْ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ بِالْحَقِّ وَلَا
Chapter 3, Section 2 - The Intellect. Relativity of the Intellect. That importance which the Quran gives to the intellect, and with those characteristics by which it is distinguished, does not mean the absoluteness of the judgments resulting from it. And it has been said previously: Its judgments are not at one level in terms of their indication of certainty; they begin from truth with certainty and end with falsehood with certainty. And because the intellect is confined between time and space, the question that is always asked is: When? And Where? While the great truths have no time and no place, but the intellect is incapable of conceiving that, so you see it declaring its inability to accept one of two possibilities with no third: Is the universe finite in boundaries? Or infinite in boundaries? So in the sequence of its conceptions, it reaches a limit beyond the worlds of galaxies, incapable of thinking, unable to be convinced of infinity, or to accept finitude, so it hesitates between two questions: Did the universe end? If it accepts, its imagination jumps to ask: And what is after the end? And if it tells itself the universe has no end, it jumps to the realm of the attached to the sensible to ask: How can there be a thing with no end? And this hesitation between the two possibilities and the inability of the intellect to be convinced of either is evidence of its limits. This confirms that the intellect does not work except according to the data of the senses. The rational faculty in man is that which combines the representative faculty, memory, imagination, and intelligence, and performs its work of analysis, synthesis, combination, differentiation, and deduction of general rules and universals. And accordingly, the function of the senses is to transmit their observations in the universe, whether seen, heard, smelled, touched, or tasted, to the intellect (the representative faculty), and it issues its judgments according to their data. Without presenting those sensory tapes, it is impossible for the intellect to issue any judgment, and therefore the established rule says: Judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception. And from the experiences of daily life - in the field of education - that further clarify this relativity in the intellect is what one researcher points to: that a teacher may not be able to recall the name of a former student, or the title of a book he decided last year, or the place where he parked his car, and he may not be able to recall many things that passed through his experience previously. Therefore, the individual often does not retrieve except the things he desires to retrieve. And among the examples of that, this researcher says: The child strongly remembers that his mother promised to take him to the circus on Saturday, but he quickly forgets that she asked him to trim the garden, just as the scientist may remember things that support his beliefs more than others. And the same thing can happen in thinking and reasoning even among highly intelligent individuals, either due to error in thinking and reasoning, or as a result of using inappropriate statistical and experimental methods. And that may also result from emotional bias, as is the case with that child who strongly remembers his right to his mother's appointment, while forgetting his duty to trim the garden, or even with the scientist who remembers what supports his beliefs without giving the same attention to what contradicts them. And this is what some modern experimental studies in psychology have revealed. Some syllogistic proofs were presented to a group of students, and they were asked to indicate whether the conclusion was logical from the two premises used in the syllogism. It became clear that half of the syllogistic proofs - which were related to ordinary life matters - had less error among all students, while they all made errors in the half related to matters that would arouse emotion. And God speaks the truth: {But if they do not respond to you, then know that they only follow their desires. And who is more astray than one who follows his desire without guidance from Allah...} [Al-Qasas 28:50]. O Dawud, indeed We have made you a successor upon the earth, so judge between the people with truth and do not...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument about the nature and limits of the human intellect from an Islamic perspective. The author begins by acknowledging the high status the Quran gives to the intellect, but immediately clarifies that this does not mean the judgments of the intellect are absolute. On the contrary, intellectual judgments vary in their degree of certainty, ranging from certain truth to certain falsehood. The author then identifies a key limitation: the intellect is bounded by time and space, and thus constantly asks 'when?' and 'where?' for everything. However, ultimate realities (al-haqa'iq al-kubra) transcend time and space, and the intellect is incapable of conceiving them. To illustrate, the author presents the dilemma of whether the universe is finite or infinite. The intellect cannot settle either possibility; accepting finitude leads immediately to the question 'what is beyond the end?', and accepting infinity defies the intellect's dependence on the sensible world. This hesitation is presented as proof of the intellect's limits. The author then argues that the intellect operates solely based on sensory data. The rational faculty (al-quwwa al-'aqila) integrates the functions of the representative faculty (musawwira), memory, imagination, and intelligence, performing analysis, synthesis, and deduction of general rules. The senses transmit their observations to the intellect, and without such sensory input, the intellect cannot make any judgment. This is encapsulated in the principle: 'Judgment of a thing is a branch of its conception' (al-hukm 'ala al-shay' far'un 'an tasawwurih). To further demonstrate the relativity of the intellect, the author provides examples from daily life and educational experience. A teacher may forget a student's name or where he parked his car; a child vividly remembers a promise of a circus trip but forgets a chore; a scientist recalls evidence that supports his theory while ignoring contradictory data. The same bias occurs in reasoning and inference, even among highly intelligent people, due to errors in thinking, inappropriate statistical methods, or emotional bias. The author cites experimental psychological studies where students made fewer errors on neutral syllogisms but more errors on emotionally charged ones. The passage concludes with two Quranic verses: one from Surah Al-Qasas (28:50) warning against following desires, and a partial verse from Surah Sad (38:26) about judging with truth, emphasizing that emotional bias leads away from truth.

التحيز الانفعالي
الهوى

Key Takeaway
Emotional bias distorts reasoning by affecting memory and judgment, a fact confirmed by modern psychology and warned against in the Quran.

The Quranic Foundation for Senses and Intellect
Author discusses Quranic basis for senses and intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic terms for intellect and senses and explain the process by which senses contribute to the formation of intuitive sciences.

Core Idea
The Quran integrates senses and heart (intellect) as the twin channels of human knowledge.

In this section, the author grounds Islamic epistemology in Quranic verses that mention hearing, sight, and the heart (fu'ad). He interprets the heart as the intellect, the seat of perception to which the senses convey their data. Understanding this process is crucial for grasping how knowledge is built in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Quranic verses
Find the verses cited (An-Nahl 16:78, Al-Mu'minun 23:78, As-Sajdah 32:9, Al-Isra 17:36). Note that each mentions hearing, sight, and the heart (fu'ad).
2
Identify the meaning of 'fu'ad'
The author states that 'fu'ad' refers to the intellect ('aql) because it is the seat of all perception (qarr al-idrak kulli). Recognize that this is a key epistemological term.
3
Trace the epistemological chain
The senses convey their perceptions to the intellect. The intellect forms simple conceptions (tasawwurat). These conceptions are the basis for intuitive sciences (ulum badihiyya), which in turn ground acquired sciences (ulum kasbiyya).
Note the dependency: senses → intellect → conceptions → intuitive sciences → acquired sciences.
4
Assess the role of hearing and sight
The passage states that hearing and sight are the first and most important senses for acquiring conceptions. Reflect on why these two might be prioritized.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
وقد خلق الله الإنسان مزوّداً بالحواس والعقل معاً، ولذلك فإن مسؤوليته مناطة بهما معاً: ﴿وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُون أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئاً وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصَارَ وَالأَفْئِدَةَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [النحل: ٧٨/١٦]. ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي أَنْشَأَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصارَ وَالْأَفْئِدَةَ قَلِيلاً ما تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون: ٧٨/٢٣]. ﴿ثُمَّ سَوَاهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِهِ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصَارَ وَالأَفْئِدَةَ قَلِيلاً ما تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [السجدة: ٩/٣٢]. ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كان عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً﴾ [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧]. ومن الجدير ملاحظته في هذه الآيات أن ذكر الأفئدة يشير إلى معنى العقل، لأنه مقر الإدراك كله فهو الذي تنقل إليه الحواس مدركاتها، وهي العلم بالتصورات المفردة. والإشارة بينة إلى أنه لا يمكن اكتساب العلوم الكسبية إلا بواسطة العلوم البديهية النظري والضروري. وحصول العلوم البديهية يتحقق عند تصور موضوعاتها ومجالاتها. وحدوث هذه التصورات إنما يكون بسبب إعانة الحواس على جزئياتها. وبذلك تصير الحواس الخمس السبب الأصلي لحدوث هذه العلوم. ويكون السمع والبصر أول الحواس تحصيلاً للتصورات وأهمها.

صحيح أن الآيات ميّزت الإنسان عن الحيوان بالعقل إذ لا فؤاد عند الأخير رغم امتلاكه للحواس، ولكن لربما كان من غير الدقيق ما ذهب إليه أحد الباحثين - استنتاجاً من هذه الحقيقة - أن الدور الحقيقي الفاعل إنما هو للعقل الذي يقف وراء الحواس، ويجعل من إحساساتها إدراكات ومعارف حقيقية تنقلها من الغرائز والانعكاسات التي تشترك فيها سائر الحيوانات المزودة بمثل تلك الحواس، بيد أنها لا تتعدى الاهتداء الغريزي. كما أن من غير المفهوم ما حاول به باحث آخر أن يردّ على هذا الرأي فراح يستشهد بقول الله تعالى: ﴿لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ﴾ [الشورى: ١١/٤٢] ليستدل من خلاله على أن وسيلتي السمع والبصر من الكمال، ولذلك فالمعارف الآتية من قبلهما بالنسبة للإنسان معارف يقينية مؤكدة. ولست أدري كيف تكون يقينية مؤكدة لمجرد أنها من صفات الكمال عند الإنسان؟ فهل يرفع هذا التشريف معارفها إلى مقام المعارف اليقينية المؤكدة؟ وأين نذهب - إذن - بحقيقة خداع الحواس الذي قد يحصل أحياناً؟ وهل كانت ترقى هذه المعارف إلى اليقين - أحياناً - إن لم يكن العقل قد استقبلها وتفاعل معها؟

والقول بمنح العقل مزية جوهرية على الحواس إلى الحد الذي يشعرك بالميل نحو المذهب العقلاني لا يخلو من غلو. ذلك أن الوظيفة تكاملية بينهما، والعلاقة عضوية تبادلية بحيث نقول: إنه وإن صح تميّز الإنسان عن غيره بالعقل، لكنه لن يحيل أي معرفة يدركها العقل بقوانينه الأولية - عدا ما سواها - إلى معارف حقيقية ذات قيمة لو لم تكن الحواس ومعطياتها قد منحت له منافذ الإدراك وإحداث عمليات التعقل العليا.
Chapter Three, Section Two: The Intellect
And Allah created man equipped with both senses and intellect, therefore his responsibility is contingent upon both: {And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers not knowing anything, and He made for you hearing, sight, and hearts that you might be grateful} [An-Nahl 16:78]. {And He it is who produced for you hearing, sight, and hearts; little do you give thanks} [Al-Mu'minun 23:78]. {Then He proportioned him and breathed into him of His spirit and made for you hearing, sight, and hearts; little do you give thanks} [As-Sajdah 32:9]. {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge; indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart – all of those will be questioned} [Al-Isra 17:36]. It is worth noting in these verses that mentioning the hearts (af'idah) refers to the meaning of intellect, because it is the seat of all perception, to which the senses convey their perceptions, and it is knowledge of simple conceptions. And the indication is clear that acquired sciences cannot be obtained except through primary and necessary intuitive sciences. And the attainment of intuitive sciences is realized upon conceiving their subjects and fields. And the occurrence of these conceptions is only due to the assistance of the senses regarding their particulars. Thus the five senses become the original cause of the occurrence of these sciences. And hearing and sight are the first of the senses in acquiring conceptions and the most important of them.

It is true that the verses distinguished man from animal by intellect, since the latter has no heart despite possessing senses, but perhaps it is imprecise what one researcher concluded from this fact – that the real active role belongs only to the intellect which stands behind the senses and makes of their sensations true perceptions and knowledge, transferring them from the instincts and reflexes shared by all animals equipped with such senses, except that they do not exceed instinctual guidance. Likewise, it is incomprehensible what another researcher attempted in refuting this opinion, as he cited the saying of Allah the Exalted: {There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing} [Ash-Shura 42:11] to deduce from it that the two means of hearing and sight are perfections, and therefore the knowledge coming from them for man is certain and confirmed knowledge. And I do not know how they can be certain and confirmed merely because they are attributes of perfection in man? Does this honor elevate their knowledge to the rank of certain and confirmed knowledge? Where then do we go with the reality of sensory deception that may sometimes occur? And would this knowledge reach certainty – sometimes – if the intellect had not received it and interacted with it?

And the claim of granting the intellect an essential superiority over the senses to the extent that it makes you incline toward the rationalist school is not without exaggeration. That is because the function is complementary between them, and the relationship is organic and reciprocal such that we say: Even if it is correct that man is distinguished from others by intellect, it will not convert any knowledge that the intellect grasps by its primary laws – except what is beyond that – into true knowledge of value unless the senses and their data have granted him the channels of perception and the initiation of higher intellectual processes.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a modern Quranic study, examining the relationship between the senses and the intellect in the acquisition of knowledge. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that mention hearing, sight, and the heart (fu'ad), noting that the heart refers to the intellect as the seat of all perception. The senses convey their perceptions to the intellect, which then forms simple conceptions (tasawwurat). The author then explains that acquired sciences (ulum kasbiyya) depend on intuitive sciences (ulum badihiyya), which themselves become actualized only when their subjects are conceived—and these conceptions arise with the assistance of the senses regarding particulars. Thus the five senses are the original cause of these sciences, with hearing and sight being the most important. 

Next, the author critiques two extreme positions. The first researcher claims that the intellect is the real active agent behind the senses, turning raw sensations into true knowledge and distinguishing human knowledge from animal instinct. The author finds this imprecise. The second researcher argues that since hearing and sight are attributes of perfection in Allah, their knowledge in humans is certain and confirmed. The author rejects this as incomprehensible, questioning how sensory certainty can be guaranteed when sensory deception occurs, and whether such knowledge would attain certainty without the intellect's reception and interaction. 

Finally, the author concludes that granting the intellect a fundamental superiority over the senses is an exaggeration characteristic of rationalism. The relationship is complementary and organic: even if the intellect distinguishes humans, it cannot convert any knowledge into true valuable knowledge without the senses providing the channels of perception and initiating higher intellectual processes. Thus, both senses and intellect are necessary and work together.

According to the passage, what is the role of the heart (fu'ad) mentioned in the Quranic verses?
A) It is the seat of emotions and passions.
B) It is the seat of intellect that receives sensory perceptions and forms knowledge.
C) It is the source of divine revelation without sensory input.
D) It is irrelevant to the process of knowledge acquisition.

Key Takeaway
The Quran presents hearing, sight, and the heart (intellect) as integrated faculties for acquiring knowledge, with the senses providing raw data and the intellect processing it into conceptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find the verse in Surat an-Nahl 16:78. Explain in your own words how the heart (fu'ad) functions as the seat of intellect according to the passage.
?
Draw a diagram showing the flow from senses to acquired sciences as described in the passage.

Critiquing Two Extreme Epistemological Positions
Author critiques two extreme views on senses and intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two flawed epistemological positions critiqued by the author and articulate the complementary model between senses and intellect.

Core Idea
Overemphasizing either intellect or senses produces an incomplete epistemology; the true relationship is complementary.

After establishing the Quranic basis, the author critiques two extreme views: one that grants the intellect exclusive active role, and another that claims sensory knowledge is certain because the senses are divine perfections. The author finds both inadequate and proposes an organic, reciprocal relationship between senses and intellect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first extreme position
A researcher claimed that the real active role belongs solely to the intellect behind the senses, turning sensations into true knowledge and distinguishing humans from animals. The author calls this 'imprecise' (ghayr daqiq).
This is a form of rationalism.
2
Identify the second extreme position
Another researcher argued that because hearing and sight are attributes of perfection in Allah, human sensory knowledge is certain and confirmed. The author finds this incomprehensible.
This is a naïve claim of sensory certainty based on divine attributes.
3
Analyze the author's objections
For the first: the author implies that it underplays the essential contribution of the senses. For the second: the author questions how sensory deception can be ignored, and whether certainty would be attained without intellectual processing.
Note the use of rhetorical questions to challenge the second view.
4
Extract the author's positive thesis
The author concludes that the function is complementary (takamuliyya) and the relationship is organic and reciprocal (udwiyya tabaduliyya). The intellect cannot produce valuable knowledge without sensory input.
This is the key corrective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
وقد خلق الله الإنسان مزوّداً بالحواس والعقل معاً، ولذلك فإن مسؤوليته مناطة بهما معاً: ﴿وَاللهُ أَخْرَجَكُمْ مِنْ بُطُون أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ لا تَعْلَمُونَ شَيْئاً وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصَارَ وَالأَفْئِدَةَ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [النحل: ٧٨/١٦]. ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي أَنْشَأَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصارَ وَالْأَفْئِدَةَ قَلِيلاً ما تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون: ٧٨/٢٣]. ﴿ثُمَّ سَوَاهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِهِ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ السَّمْعَ وَالأَبْصَارَ وَالأَفْئِدَةَ قَلِيلاً ما تَشْكُرُونَ﴾ [السجدة: ٩/٣٢]. ﴿وَلا تَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمٌ إِنَّ السَّمْعَ وَالْبَصَرَ وَالْفُؤادَ كُلُّ أُولَئِكَ كان عَنْهُ مَسْؤُولاً﴾ [الإسراء: ٣٦/١٧]. ومن الجدير ملاحظته في هذه الآيات أن ذكر الأفئدة يشير إلى معنى العقل، لأنه مقر الإدراك كله فهو الذي تنقل إليه الحواس مدركاتها، وهي العلم بالتصورات المفردة. والإشارة بينة إلى أنه لا يمكن اكتساب العلوم الكسبية إلا بواسطة العلوم البديهية النظري والضروري. وحصول العلوم البديهية يتحقق عند تصور موضوعاتها ومجالاتها. وحدوث هذه التصورات إنما يكون بسبب إعانة الحواس على جزئياتها. وبذلك تصير الحواس الخمس السبب الأصلي لحدوث هذه العلوم. ويكون السمع والبصر أول الحواس تحصيلاً للتصورات وأهمها.

صحيح أن الآيات ميّزت الإنسان عن الحيوان بالعقل إذ لا فؤاد عند الأخير رغم امتلاكه للحواس، ولكن لربما كان من غير الدقيق ما ذهب إليه أحد الباحثين - استنتاجاً من هذه الحقيقة - أن الدور الحقيقي الفاعل إنما هو للعقل الذي يقف وراء الحواس، ويجعل من إحساساتها إدراكات ومعارف حقيقية تنقلها من الغرائز والانعكاسات التي تشترك فيها سائر الحيوانات المزودة بمثل تلك الحواس، بيد أنها لا تتعدى الاهتداء الغريزي. كما أن من غير المفهوم ما حاول به باحث آخر أن يردّ على هذا الرأي فراح يستشهد بقول الله تعالى: ﴿لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ﴾ [الشورى: ١١/٤٢] ليستدل من خلاله على أن وسيلتي السمع والبصر من الكمال، ولذلك فالمعارف الآتية من قبلهما بالنسبة للإنسان معارف يقينية مؤكدة. ولست أدري كيف تكون يقينية مؤكدة لمجرد أنها من صفات الكمال عند الإنسان؟ فهل يرفع هذا التشريف معارفها إلى مقام المعارف اليقينية المؤكدة؟ وأين نذهب - إذن - بحقيقة خداع الحواس الذي قد يحصل أحياناً؟ وهل كانت ترقى هذه المعارف إلى اليقين - أحياناً - إن لم يكن العقل قد استقبلها وتفاعل معها؟

والقول بمنح العقل مزية جوهرية على الحواس إلى الحد الذي يشعرك بالميل نحو المذهب العقلاني لا يخلو من غلو. ذلك أن الوظيفة تكاملية بينهما، والعلاقة عضوية تبادلية بحيث نقول: إنه وإن صح تميّز الإنسان عن غيره بالعقل، لكنه لن يحيل أي معرفة يدركها العقل بقوانينه الأولية - عدا ما سواها - إلى معارف حقيقية ذات قيمة لو لم تكن الحواس ومعطياتها قد منحت له منافذ الإدراك وإحداث عمليات التعقل العليا.
Chapter Three, Section Two: The Intellect
And Allah created man equipped with both senses and intellect, therefore his responsibility is contingent upon both: {And Allah brought you out from the wombs of your mothers not knowing anything, and He made for you hearing, sight, and hearts that you might be grateful} [An-Nahl 16:78]. {And He it is who produced for you hearing, sight, and hearts; little do you give thanks} [Al-Mu'minun 23:78]. {Then He proportioned him and breathed into him of His spirit and made for you hearing, sight, and hearts; little do you give thanks} [As-Sajdah 32:9]. {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge; indeed, the hearing, the sight, and the heart – all of those will be questioned} [Al-Isra 17:36]. It is worth noting in these verses that mentioning the hearts (af'idah) refers to the meaning of intellect, because it is the seat of all perception, to which the senses convey their perceptions, and it is knowledge of simple conceptions. And the indication is clear that acquired sciences cannot be obtained except through primary and necessary intuitive sciences. And the attainment of intuitive sciences is realized upon conceiving their subjects and fields. And the occurrence of these conceptions is only due to the assistance of the senses regarding their particulars. Thus the five senses become the original cause of the occurrence of these sciences. And hearing and sight are the first of the senses in acquiring conceptions and the most important of them.

It is true that the verses distinguished man from animal by intellect, since the latter has no heart despite possessing senses, but perhaps it is imprecise what one researcher concluded from this fact – that the real active role belongs only to the intellect which stands behind the senses and makes of their sensations true perceptions and knowledge, transferring them from the instincts and reflexes shared by all animals equipped with such senses, except that they do not exceed instinctual guidance. Likewise, it is incomprehensible what another researcher attempted in refuting this opinion, as he cited the saying of Allah the Exalted: {There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing} [Ash-Shura 42:11] to deduce from it that the two means of hearing and sight are perfections, and therefore the knowledge coming from them for man is certain and confirmed knowledge. And I do not know how they can be certain and confirmed merely because they are attributes of perfection in man? Does this honor elevate their knowledge to the rank of certain and confirmed knowledge? Where then do we go with the reality of sensory deception that may sometimes occur? And would this knowledge reach certainty – sometimes – if the intellect had not received it and interacted with it?

And the claim of granting the intellect an essential superiority over the senses to the extent that it makes you incline toward the rationalist school is not without exaggeration. That is because the function is complementary between them, and the relationship is organic and reciprocal such that we say: Even if it is correct that man is distinguished from others by intellect, it will not convert any knowledge that the intellect grasps by its primary laws – except what is beyond that – into true knowledge of value unless the senses and their data have granted him the channels of perception and the initiation of higher intellectual processes.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a modern Quranic study, examining the relationship between the senses and the intellect in the acquisition of knowledge. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that mention hearing, sight, and the heart (fu'ad), noting that the heart refers to the intellect as the seat of all perception. The senses convey their perceptions to the intellect, which then forms simple conceptions (tasawwurat). The author then explains that acquired sciences (ulum kasbiyya) depend on intuitive sciences (ulum badihiyya), which themselves become actualized only when their subjects are conceived—and these conceptions arise with the assistance of the senses regarding particulars. Thus the five senses are the original cause of these sciences, with hearing and sight being the most important. 

Next, the author critiques two extreme positions. The first researcher claims that the intellect is the real active agent behind the senses, turning raw sensations into true knowledge and distinguishing human knowledge from animal instinct. The author finds this imprecise. The second researcher argues that since hearing and sight are attributes of perfection in Allah, their knowledge in humans is certain and confirmed. The author rejects this as incomprehensible, questioning how sensory certainty can be guaranteed when sensory deception occurs, and whether such knowledge would attain certainty without the intellect's reception and interaction. 

Finally, the author concludes that granting the intellect a fundamental superiority over the senses is an exaggeration characteristic of rationalism. The relationship is complementary and organic: even if the intellect distinguishes humans, it cannot convert any knowledge into true valuable knowledge without the senses providing the channels of perception and initiating higher intellectual processes. Thus, both senses and intellect are necessary and work together.

العقل

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the claim that sensory knowledge is certain and confirmed merely because hearing and sight are divine perfections problematic?
A) Because divine perfections cannot be compared to human faculties.
B) Because sensory deception can occur, and certainty requires intellectual processing.
C) Because the intellect is the only source of certainty.
D) Because the Quran does not mention hearing and sight as perfections.

Key Takeaway
The author rejects both rationalist overemphasis on intellect and naïve sensory certainty, advocating for a complementary and reciprocal relationship between senses and intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Quranic Integration of Senses and Intellect
Author discusses Quranic verses linking senses, heart, and intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Quranic verses cited by the author demonstrate the connection between sensory perception and intellectual reasoning.

Core Idea
The Quran sees senses and intellect as complementary, not contradictory.

In this passage, the author explores several Quranic verses to show that the senses (hearing, sight) and the intellect (reason) are not at odds but work together. The heart (qalb) is presented as the connecting center. Understanding this integration is crucial for Islamic epistemology, as it shapes how we approach knowledge from revelation and observation.

Guided Path
1
Locate the key Quranic verses
Read the verses from Surah an-Nahl, al-Isra, al-Anfal, al-Furqan, and al-A'raf that mention hearts, hearing, and sight. Notice how they are grouped together.
The author uses these verses to show that the disbelievers' hearts, ears, and eyes are sealed or unresponsive.
2
Identify the common theme
In each verse, the failure to use sensory and intellectual faculties leads to a state of heedlessness. The author points out that the Quran likens such people to cattle or says they are worse.
The analogy to cattle emphasizes that they are not benefiting from their God-given tools.
3
Analyze the connection between senses and heart
The author states that the verses show a link between the senses and the heart, as if they operate simultaneously. Check the Arabic: لهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِها وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِها...
The heart is the seat of understanding, but it works with the eyes and ears.
4
Understand the author's conclusion
The author concludes that the Quran sees no conflict but rather integration and synergy between the senses and intellect. This is the key epistemological claim.
Saying otherwise is described as a false assumption.
