الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
٤ - اليقينية والعلمية والثبات.
ه - لغة المثال: أي أسلوب ضرب المثال لتقريب المعنى على نحو متميز.
٦ - الواقعية أي إن الوحي يتعامل مع الحقائق الموضوعية، وليس مع التصورات العقلية المجردة أو المثالية.
۷ - الفطرية أي إن المعرفة النبوية لا تحصل بالتعلم والاكتساب، وإنما بالحال وتبدل الصفات.
وعن هذه الصفة الأخيرة يقول ابن حزم (ت: ٤٥٦هـ): ((وهي بعثة قوم قد خصهم الله - تعالى- بالحكمة والفضيلة، والعصمة لا لعلة إلا أنه شاء ذلك، فعلمهم الله تعالى العلم بدون تعلم، ولا تنقل في مراتبه، ولا طلب له)). وحقاً فإننا حين نتفحص آيات القرآن الكريم الواردة بشأن الوحي والنبوة نلفي هذه الحقيقة ماثلة أمامنا، فتؤكد الآيات التالية بمجموعها أن النبوة أمر صادر عن إرادة الله المطلقة، ولا علاقة له بالرياضة أو الكسب: ﴿وَما نَتَنَزَّلُ إلا بِأَمْرِ رَبِّك﴾ [مريم: ٦٤/١٩]، ﴿اللَّهُ يَصْطَفِي مِنَ الْمَلائِكَةِ رُسُلاً وَمِنَ النَّاسِ﴾ [الحج: ٧٥/٢٢]، ﴿وَقُلْ مَا كُنتُ بِدْعاً مِنَ الرُّسُلِ وَمَا أَدْرِي مَا يُفْعَلُ بِي وَلَا بِكُمْ إِنْ أَتَّبِعُ إِلَّا ما يُوحَى إِلَيَّ وَمَا أَنَا إِلَّا نَذِيرٌ مُبِينٌ﴾ [الأحقاف: ٩/٤٦]، ﴿وَإِذَا تُتْلَى عَلَيْهِمْ آيَاتُنَا بَيِّنَاتٍ قَالَ الَّذِينَ لا يَرْجُونَ لِقَاءَنَا الْتِ بِقُرْآن غَيْرِ هَذَا أَوْ بَدِّلْهُ قُلْ مَا يَكُونُ لِي أَنْ أُبَدِّلَهُ مِنْ تِلْقَاءِ نَفْسِي إِنْ أَتَّبِعُ إِلَّا مَا يُوحَى إِلَيَّ إِنِّي أَخَافُ إِنْ عَصَيْتُ رَبِّي عَذَابَ يَوْمٍ عَظِيمٍ، قُلْ لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا تَلَوْتُهُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَلا أَدْراكُمْ بِهِ﴾ [يونس: ١٥/١٠-١٦]، ﴿وَلَئِنْ شِئْنَا لَنَذْهَبَنَّ بِالَّذِي أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ ثُمَّ لَا تَجِدُ لَكَ بِهِ عَلَيْنَا وَكِيلاً، إِلَّا رَحْمَةً مِنْ رَبِّكَ إِنَّ فَضْلَهُ كان عَلَيْكَ كَبِيرا﴾ [الإسراء: ٨٦/١٧-١٨]، ﴿وَمَا نَتَنَزَّلُ إِلَّا بِأَمْرِ رَبِّكَ لَهُ ما بَيْنَ أَيْدِينَا وَمَا خَلْفَنَا وَمَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ وما كانَ رَبُّكَ نَسِياً﴾ [مريم: ١٦٤/١٩]. وبلغة أصولية يمكن تلخيص صفات الوحي (القرآن) من زاوية أخرى - بأنه إلهي المصدر، قطعي الورود، قطعي الدلالة، وظنيها، قد ينسخ بآيات أخرى، وحقائقه مطلقة، غير خاضعة للتعقيب الإنساني، ودور الإنسان فيها يقتصر على الاستجلاء، وذلك لأنها نابعة من العلم الإلهي المطلق. ويتفق الوحي ومبادئ العقل، ولا يمكن حصول خلاف حقيقي بينهما والوحي نص منضبط يجري على أساليب العرب في القول. ومجمل القول فيما يتصل بالتربية الإسلامية إنها تكتسب جانباً كبيراً من خصائصها من خصائص الوحي ذاته، وذلك من حيث شمولها وواقعيتها وعلميتها وفطريتها المؤسسة على الخير في أعماق كل إنسان، وكذا أساليبها.
طبيعة الوحي
يركز القرآن على طبيعة النبوة أو الوحي، حيث يتنزل على رسول من جنس المدعوين، كي يدرأ الشبهات التي يمكن أن تثار لو أن الرسول من غير جنسهم. وكي يكون البلاغ أكبر أثراً، وأقوى حجة: ﴿وَقالُوا لَوْلا أُنزِلَ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكَ وَلَوْ أَنْزَلْنَا مَلَكَا لَقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ ثُمَّ لا يُنظَرُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٨/٦].
Chapter Three: The Third Section - Revelation
4 - Certainty, scientificity, and stability.
5 - Language of example: i.e., the method of giving an example to approximate the meaning in a distinctive manner.
6 - Objectivity: i.e., revelation deals with objective truths, not with abstract mental or ideal perceptions.
7 - Innate nature: i.e., prophetic knowledge is not acquired by learning and acquisition, but by state and change of attributes.
Concerning this last characteristic, Ibn Hazm (d. 456 AH) says: 'It is the sending of a people whom God has distinguished with wisdom, virtue, and infallibility, not for any cause but that He willed it. So God taught them knowledge without learning, without progression through its stages, and without seeking it.' Indeed, when we examine the verses of the Noble Quran concerning revelation and prophethood, we find this fact evident before us. The following verses collectively affirm that prophethood is a matter emanating from God's absolute will, having no relation to spiritual exercise or acquisition: 'We do not descend except by the command of your Lord' [Maryam 19:64], 'Allah chooses from the angels messengers and from the people' [Al-Hajj 22:75], 'Say, I am not something unprecedented among the messengers, nor do I know what will be done with me or with you. I only follow what is revealed to me, and I am not but a clear warner' [Al-Ahqaf 46:9], 'And when Our verses are recited to them as clear signs, those who do not expect the meeting with Us say, Bring a Quran other than this or change it. Say, It is not for me to change it on my own accord. I only follow what is revealed to me. Indeed I fear, if I should disobey my Lord, the punishment of a great Day. Say, If Allah had willed, I would not have recited it to you, nor would He have made it known to you' [Yunus 10:15-16], 'And if We willed, We could surely take away that which We have revealed to you. Then you would not find for yourself concerning it an advocate against Us, except as a mercy from your Lord. Indeed His favor upon you has ever been great' [Al-Isra 17:86-87], 'We do not descend except by the command of your Lord; to Him belongs what is before us and what is behind us and what is between that. And your Lord is not forgetful' [Maryam 19:64]. In Usuli language, the characteristics of revelation (the Quran) can be summarized from another angle: that it is divine in source, definitive in transmission, definitive and conjectural in indication, may be abrogated by other verses, its truths are absolute, not subject to human commentary, and the role of humans in it is limited to elucidation, because it emanates from absolute divine knowledge. Revelation and the principles of reason agree, and no real conflict can occur between them; revelation is a disciplined text that follows the Arabs' styles of speech. In summary, concerning Islamic education, it acquires a large part of its characteristics from the characteristics of revelation itself, in terms of its comprehensiveness, objectivity, scientificity, and innate nature founded on goodness in the depths of every human being, as well as its methods.
The Nature of Revelation
The Quran focuses on the nature of prophethood or revelation: it descends upon a messenger from the same kind as those addressed, in order to repel the doubts that might arise if the messenger were from another kind, and for the communication to have greater impact and be a stronger proof: 'And they say, Why was an angel not sent down to him? If We had sent down an angel, the matter would have been decided; then they would not be reprieved' [Al-An'am 6:8].
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and expository discussion of the characteristics (ṣifāt) and nature of divine revelation (al-waḥy), specifically focusing on the Quran as understood in the Islamic tradition. The author begins by listing four key characteristics: 1) Certainty and scientificity (al-yaqīniyya wa al-ʿilmiyya) and stability (al-thabāt); 2) Use of example language (lughat al-mithāl) as a distinctive method to approximate meanings; 3) Objectivity (al-wāqiʿiyya), meaning revelation deals with objective truths, not abstract mental constructs; 4) Innateness (al-fiṭriyya), which the author explains as prophetic knowledge not being acquired through learning but bestowed by God. The author then cites Ibn Ḥazm to elaborate on innateness: prophethood is a divine gift, not earned. To support this, the author quotes several Quranic verses emphasizing that revelation and prophethood are solely by God's will, not through human effort. Then, using the language of uṣūl (principles of jurisprudence), the author summarizes the attributes of revelation from another angle: divine source, definitive transmission (qaṭʿī al-wurūd), definitive and conjectural indication (qaṭʿī al-dalāla wa ẓannīhā), possibility of abrogation, absolute truths not subject to human critique, and its role limited to elucidation. The author also asserts harmony between revelation and reason, and that revelation follows Arabic styles. Finally, the passage discusses the nature of revelation: it is sent to a messenger from among the people to avoid doubts and increase impact, citing the Quranic verse about the demand for an angel. Throughout, the author explains these points in a flowing prose, with the enumeration of characteristics providing a loose structure.

Key Terms

اليقينية
الفطرية
قطع الورود

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the characteristic of 'innateness' (al-fiṭriyya) mean regarding prophetic knowledge?
A) Prophetic knowledge is acquired through rigorous study and spiritual training.
B) Prophetic knowledge is obtained spontaneously without learning or acquisition.
C) Prophetic knowledge is developed through repeated practice.
D) Prophetic knowledge is based on analogical reasoning from prior prophets.

Key Takeaway
Revelation's key characteristics – certainty, objectivity, and innateness – establish its unique epistemic authority as divine knowledge, not human acquisition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How does the usuli language reframe the same concepts? Write a short paragraph explaining the connection.

beginner

The Nature of Revelation: Divine Origin and Human Messenger
Author explains why revelation is sent to a human messenger from among the people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why revelation is sent to a human messenger from among the people, using both the reasoning and the Quranic verse provided in the passage.

Core Idea
Prophethood is a divine selection; the messenger is from the same kind to ensure effective communication and stronger proof.

Having discussed the attributes of revelation, the author now turns to its nature: why does God send revelation to a human messenger from among the people? This section addresses potential doubts and provides a rationale grounded in both wisdom and Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the paragraph on the nature of revelation
The author devotes a short paragraph to 'the nature of revelation' (ṭabīʿat al-waḥy). Identify the main claim: revelation descends on a messenger from the same kind as those addressed.
The author uses the word 'nature' to mean the essential characteristic of how revelation is delivered.
2
Find the reason given for this nature
The author gives two reasons: to repel doubts (li yadraʾ al-shubahāt) and for greater impact and stronger proof (yakūn al-balāgh akthar atharan, aqwā ḥujja).
These reasons are practical and theological.
3
Examine the Quranic verse cited
The verse from Al-An'am (6:8) is quoted: the people asked for an angel, but God responds that if an angel were sent, the matter would be decided and they would not be reprieved. This shows why a human messenger is sent.
The verse implies that an angelic messenger would remove the test of faith.
4
Connect to the broader Islamic doctrine of prophethood
Reflect on how this nature aligns with the earlier characteristics: the messenger must be human to be relatable, and the message must be from God to be authoritative.
This explains the consistency between the attributes and the nature of revelation.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
٤ - اليقينية والعلمية والثبات.

٦ - الواقعية أي إن الوحي يتعامل مع الحقائق الموضوعية، وليس مع التصورات العقلية المجردة أو المثالية.

According to the passage, what is the primary reason revelation is sent to a messenger from the same kind as the people?

Nature and Attributes of Revelation (al-Wahy)
Defines the nature and attributes of revelation from a Quranic perspective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the key attributes of revelation derived from the Quranic perspective, including its external nature, divine source, and its implications for Islamic education.

Core Idea
Revelation is an external, divine reality, not inner inspiration, and its attributes shape Islamic education.

In this lesson, we delve into the Quranic understanding of revelation (al-wahy). The passage presents a thorough analysis of what revelation is, listing its attributes such as divine source, definitive transmission, and absolute truths. It also emphasizes that revelation is an external event—a real encounter with the angel Jibreel—not a mere inner feeling. Understanding these attributes is crucial for distinguishing Islamic revelation from other claims of divine knowledge and for grounding Islamic educational principles.

Guided Path
1
Extract the attributes of revelation
Read the passage and list the attributes mentioned, such as divine in source, definitive transmission, absolute truths, and non-subjectability to human critique.
The passage uses usuli language; note that some attributes are paired (e.g., definitive and probable indication).
2
Contrast revelation with inner speech
Identify the argument that revelation is external reception, not inner speech. Look for the example of Jibreel's physical embrace and the command 'Read'.
This is a key polemical point against those who reduce revelation to subjective experience.
3
Explain why prophets are human
The passage cites verses showing that messengers are from among the people. Explain the reason: to prevent doubt and make communication effective.
This reinforces the realism of revelation.
4
Connect to Islamic education
Notice the claim that Islamic education derives its characteristics (comprehensiveness, realism, etc.) from revelation. How does each attribute of revelation translate into an educational principle?
This is an applied step bridging theology and pedagogy.

وَأُمِرَ جبريل - عليه السلام - أن يقول للنبي - - حين تأخر نزول الوحي: ﴿وَما نَتَنَزَّلُ إِلَّا بِأَمْرِ رَبِّكَ لَهُ ما بَيْنَ أَيْدِينَا وَمَا خَلْفَنَا وَمَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ وما كانَ رَبُّكَ نَسِيا﴾ [مريم: ١٦٤/١٩]. وبلغة أصولية يمكن تلخيص صفات الوحي (القرآن) من زاوية أخرى - بأنه إلهي المصدر، قطعي الورود، قطعي الدلالة ،وظنيها، قد ينسخ بآيات أخرى، وحقائقه مطلقة، غير خاضعة للتعقيب الإنساني، ودور الإنسان فيها يقتصر على الاستجلاء، وذلك لأنها نابعة من العلم الإلهي المطلق. ويتفق الوحي ومبادئ العقل، ولا يمكن حصول خلاف حقيقي بينهما والوحي نص منضبط يجري على أساليب العرب في القول. ومجمل القول فيما يتصل بالتربية الإسلامية إنها تكتسب جانباً كبيراً من خصائصها من خصائص الوحي ذاته، وذلك من حيث شمولها وواقعيتها وعلميتها وفطريتها المؤسسة على الخير في أعماق كل إنسان، وكذا أساليبها. طبيعة الوحي يركز القرآن على طبيعة النبوة أو الوحي، حيث يتنزل على رسـول مـن جنس المدعوين، كي يدرأ الشبهات التي يمكن أن تثار فيما لو أن الرسول من غير جنسهم. وكي يكون البلاغ أكبر أثراً، وأقوى حجة: ﴿وَقالُوا لَوْلا أُنزِلَ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكَ وَلَوْ أَنْزَلْنَا مَلَكَا لَقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ ثُمَّ لا يُنظَرُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٨/٦]. ﴿وَما أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ قَبْلِكَ إِلا رِجَالاً نُوحِي إِلَيْهِمْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى﴾ [يوسف: ١٠٩/١٢]. ﴿وَما أَرْسَلْنَا قَبْلَكَ مِنَ الْمُرْسَلِينَ إِلَّا إِنَّهُمْ لَيَأْكُلُونَ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشُونَ فِي الأَسْواقِ وَجَعَلْنَا بَعْضَكُمْ لِبَعْضٍ فِسَةٌ أَتَصْبِرُونَ وَكَانَ رَبُّكَ بَصِيراً﴾ [الفرقان: ٢٠/٢٥]. وإذا كانت طبيعة الشيء ما يميزه عن غيره؛ فإن طبيعة الوحي أنه يتعامل مع الإنسان متميزاً عن المناهج البشرية والقوانين الوضعية كافة. فسمة الواقعية تقتضي أن يتعامل الإنسان (النبي) مع الإنسان (المدعو) بلغته، وطبيعته، وسمات الشخصية الإنسانية المشتركة، كي يصل خطاب الوحي إلى المدعو ناصعاً أبلج. ويؤكد هذا المعنى أن عملية تلقي الوحي حقيقة خارجية لا علاقة لهـا بحديث نفسي مجرد، ولكنها استقبال لذات أخرى مباينة هي جبريل - عليه السلام . وذلك أن ضمه للنبي - - حال تلقيه للوحي في أول عهده به - ثم إرساله ثلاث مرات، قائلاً في كل مرة اقرأ ) بمثابة تأكيد على أن هذا التلقي خارجي خالص. وذلك يعني أن التربية الإسلامية بصفتها واقعية تتعامل مع الإنسان منطلقة من جميع تلك الاعتبارات، وأهمها الإقرار بالطبيعة الإنسانية وتعقيداتها.
And Jibreel - peace be upon him - was commanded to say to the Prophet - - when the revelation was delayed: 'And we do not descend except by the command of your Lord; to Him belongs what is before us and what is behind us and what is between that; and your Lord is not forgetful' [Maryam: 19:64]. In usuli language, the attributes of revelation (the Quran) can be summarized from another angle as: divine in source, definitively transmitted, definitively indicative and probabilistically so, may be abrogated by other verses, its truths are absolute, not subject to human critique, and the role of man in them is limited to elucidation, because they emanate from absolute divine knowledge. Revelation and the principles of reason agree, and no real conflict can occur between them. Revelation is a disciplined text that follows Arab styles of speech. In summary, regarding Islamic education: it acquires a great part of its characteristics from the characteristics of revelation itself, in terms of its comprehensiveness, realism, scientific nature, and its innate foundation on good in the depths of every human, as well as its methods. The nature of revelation: The Quran focuses on the nature of prophethood or revelation, that it descends upon a messenger from the same kind as those called, to ward off suspicions that could arise if the messenger were not of their kind, and so that the message has greater impact and stronger proof: 'And they said, Why was an angel not sent down to him? And if We had sent down an angel, the matter would have been decided; then they would not be reprieved' [Al-An'am 6:8]. 'And We sent not before you any but men to whom We revealed from among the people of the towns' [Yusuf 12:109]. 'And We sent not before you any of the messengers except that they ate food and walked in the markets. And We have made some of you a trial for others. Will you be patient? And your Lord is ever Seeing' [Al-Furqan 25:20]. And if the nature of a thing is what distinguishes it from others, then the nature of revelation is that it deals with man distinguished from all human methodologies and positive laws. The characteristic of realism requires that man (the prophet) deal with man (the called) in his language, nature, and common human personality traits, so that the discourse of revelation reaches the called clear and bright. This meaning is emphasized by the fact that the process of receiving revelation is an external reality, having no connection to mere inner speech, but rather it is a reception of another distinct entity, Jibreel - peace be upon him. And that is because his embracing the Prophet - - at the time of his receiving revelation in its first period, then releasing him three times, each time saying 'Read', is like an affirmation that this reception is purely external. This means that Islamic education, being realistic, deals with man proceeding from all those considerations, most importantly acknowledging human nature and its complexities.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the nature and characteristics of revelation (al-wahy) from a Quranic perspective. It begins by citing a verse where Jibreel is commanded to clarify that descent of angels is only by God's command. Then it summarizes the attributes of revelation in usuli (foundational) terms: divine source, definitive transmission, definitive and probable indication, possibility of abrogation, absolute truths not subject to human critique, and man's role limited to elucidation. It affirms that revelation and reason cannot contradict. Revelation follows Arab linguistic styles. Next, it discusses the nature of prophethood: messengers are human to avoid suspicion and to make the message more effective, citing verses from al-An'am, Yusuf, and al-Furqan. It defines the nature of revelation as what distinguishes it from human methodologies. The realism of revelation requires a human prophet addressing humans in their language and nature. Finally, it emphasizes that receiving revelation is an external reality, not inner speech, exemplified by Jibreel's physical embrace and commanding 'Read'. This external quality ensures that Islamic education is realistic and acknowledges human nature.

Four Commonalities of Prophetic Revelation
Author lists shared traits of prophetic messages from Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the four common traits of prophetic messages from the Quranic verses cited in the passage.

Core Idea
The Quran emphasizes the unity of divine revelation across all prophets through shared traits.

This passage from a modern work on Quranic themes lists four commonalities that all prophetic messages share, supported by numerous Quranic verses. Recognizing these commonalities helps us understand the coherence of the Quranic narrative and the universal principles of Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first commonality: Revelation-based call
Find the Quranic verses that show all prophets received revelation (wahy). The passage cites 4:163-164 and 57:25. Notice that the call is derived from revelation, not personal opinion.
This establishes the divine origin of prophetic messages.
2
Identify the second commonality: Facing harm and denial
Look at the verses listing past nations that denied their prophets (38:12-14, 22:42-44, 51:52-53). Note that rejection and persecution are recurring experiences for prophets.
This commonality teaches patience and perseverance.
3
Identify the third commonality: Unity of knowledge (tawheed)
Observe how the call to worship one God is repeated across prophets. The passage gives examples from Surat al-A'raf and Hud, and cites 21:108 for Prophet Muhammad. All prophets taught tawheed.
This shows the core theological principle is consistent.
4
Identify the fourth commonality: Function of tabligh and ittiba'
Understand that prophets only convey the message; they have no absolute power. The passage emphasizes that this breaks the dominance of power centers.
This commonality reinforces the role of prophets as messengers, not rulers.

- فحسب، وهو ما يؤكد سمات الأصالة والتجديد والعالمية في هذه التربية. ٢- تعرضهم للإيذاء بمختلف الصور: ومن أبرز صور ذلك التكذيب كَذَّبَتْ قَبْلَهُمْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ وَعَادٌ وَفِرْعَوْهُ ذُو الْأَوْتَادِ، وَثَمُودُ وَقَوْمُ لُوطٍ وَأَصْحابُ الأَيْكَةِ أُولَئِكَ الأَحْرَابُ إِن كُلّ إِلا كَذَّبَ الرُّسُلَ فَحَقِّ عِقابِ) [ص: ١٢/٣٨-١٤]. ﴿وَإِن يُكَذِّبُوكَ فَقَدْ كَذَّبَتْ قَبْلَهُمْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ وَعَادٌ وَثَمُودُ، وَقَوْمُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَقَوْمُ لُوطٍ، وَأَصْحَابُ مَدينَ وَكُذَّبَ مُوسَى فَأَمْلَيْتُ لِلْكَافِرِينَ ثُمَّ أَخَذْتُهُمْ فَكَيْفَ كَانَ نَكِيرِ ﴾ [الحج: ٤٢/٢٢-٤٤]. كَذَلِكَ ما أَتَى الَّذِينَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِمْ مِنْ رَسُولٍ إِلَّا قَالُوا سَاحِرٌ أَوْ مَجْنُونٌ أَتَواصَوْا بِهِ بَلْ هُمْ قَوْمٌ طَاغُونَ ﴾ [الذاريات: ٥٢/٥١-٥٣]. وينعكس ذلك على التربية بمزيد من حث الناشئة على الصبر والمثابرة في سبيل بلوغها أهدافها الغائيّة أياً ما كانت العوائق والتحديات التي تبغي الحيلولة دون بلوغ ذلك. ٣- وحدة المعرفة: تبرز وحدة المعرفة في دعوة فريق المعرفة من الأنبياء والرسل في أصول الاعتقاد والأخلاق ولكنها تبرز أكثر من ما تكون في قضية وحدانية الله - تعالى. وقد تكررت في غير آية من القرآن. فقوله سبحانه: يا قَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ ما لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهِ غَيْرُهُ ﴾ وردت في الآيات ٨٥،٧٣،٦٥،٥٩ مـن سـورة الأعراف و ٢٦ ، ٨٤،٦١،٥٠ من سورة هود. > و على لسان محمد - Indeed, We have revealed to you as We revealed to Noah and the prophets after him. And We revealed to Abraham, Ishmael, Isaac, Jacob, the Descendants, Jesus, Job, Jonah, Aaron, and Solomon, and We gave David the Psalms. And [We sent] messengers We have narrated to you before and messengers We have not narrated to you. And Allah spoke to Moses directly [Quran 4:163-164]. Their call derived from revelation is distinguished by proofs and miracles, to establish the argument upon people: 'We have certainly sent Our messengers with clear proofs and sent down with them the Scripture and the balance that people may maintain justice; and We sent down iron, wherein is great might and benefits for the people, and so that Allah may make evident those who support Him and His messengers unseen. Indeed, Allah is Powerful and Exalted in Might.' [Quran 57:25]. This common denominator among all heavenly calls gives Islamic education originality and deep historical depth in its reliance on revelation as a source and method, for it is derived from all knowledge of revelation, not only the revelation specific to Muhammad, which emphasizes the characteristics of originality, renewal, and universality in this education. 2. Their exposure to harm in various forms: Among the most prominent forms of that is denial: 'The people of Noah denied before them, and [the tribes of] 'Aad and Pharaoh, the owner of stakes, and Thamud, and the people of Lot, and the companions of the thicket; those are the parties. Each denied the messengers, so My punishment was justified.' [Quran 38:12-14]. 'And if they deny you, so have denied before them the people of Noah, 'Aad, and Thamud, and the people of Abraham, and the people of Lot, and the inhabitants of Madyan. And Moses was denied, so I gave respite to the disbelievers; then I seized them, and how [terrible] was My rejection.' [Quran 22:42-44]. 'Similarly, there did not come to those before them any messenger except that they said, 'A sorcerer or a madman.' Did they advise each other? Rather, they are a transgressing people.' [Quran 51:52-53]. This is reflected in education by further urging the young to patience and perseverance in achieving their ultimate goals whatever the obstacles and challenges that seek to prevent that. 3. Unity of knowledge: The unity of knowledge appears in the call of the group of knowledge from the prophets and messengers in the principles of belief and morals, but it appears more than that in the issue of the oneness of Allah. It has been repeated in more than one verse of the Quran. So His saying: 'O my people, worship Allah; you have no deity other than Him' appears in verses 59,65,73,85 of Surat al-A'raf and 50,61,84 of Surat Hud. And on the tongue of Muhammad came the saying of Allah: 'Say, 'It is only revealed to me that your god is one God; so will you be Muslims?' [Quran 21:108]. That is an acknowledgment by Islamic education of the importance of the processes of accumulation and cognitive communication between civilizations, especially those with which it shares common foundations of knowledge like tawheed for example. 4. The function of conveying and following: The mission of a messenger – any messenger – is nothing but conveying and following, without having authority to benefit or harm, for the messenger does not have absolute authority. In this is breaking the barrier of dominance of centers of power and their dictates under the claim of prophethood.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from a modern work on Quranic themes discusses the common characteristics of prophetic revelation. It begins by citing Quran 4:163-164, which affirms that revelation to Muhammad is similar to that given to earlier prophets, listing many of them. Then it notes that their calls are supported by proofs and miracles, citing Quran 57:25 about sending messengers with clear proofs, scripture, and the balance. The author emphasizes that this shared foundation gives Islamic education authenticity and depth, since it derives from all revelation, not just the Quran. The passage then lists four commonalities: (1) the call is based on revelation, (2) prophets face harm and denial, citing several verses about past nations, (3) unity of knowledge, especially tawheed, with multiple Quranic examples, and (4) the function of tabligh (conveying) and ittiba' (following), meaning prophets only convey the message and must be followed, without having absolute power. The author argues this breaks the dominance of power centers claiming prophethood. All examples are from the Quran, consistent with the book's theme.

Key Terms
الوحي (al-wahy): Divine revelation sent to prophets as a source of knowledge and guidance. [Note: In classical Mantiq, wahy is not a technical term; here it is used in a theological context.]
الرسل (al-rusul): Messengers sent by God with revelation, proofs, and miracles. [Note: Stable term in Islamic theology; no significant shift.]
التبليغ (al-tabligh): The function of conveying the divine message without personal authority. [Note: Common in Usul al-Fiqh; here used in a general sense.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is one common element in the calls of all prophets?
A) They all performed the same miracles.

C) They each brought a new religion.
D) They all had political power.

Key Takeaway
The Quran shows that all prophetic messages share four commonalities: revelation-based call, facing opposition, unity of tawheed, and the function of conveying without authority.

Civilizational Witnessing of the Ummah
Author explains the concept of civilizational witnessing based on Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of civilizational witnessing (al-shuhood al-hadari) and identify its Quranic foundations.

Core Idea
The ummah is tasked to be a civilizational witness, guiding humanity through reformative action.

This passage from 'Nazariyyat al-Quran' introduces the concept of civilizational witnessing as a natural outflow of the Islamic call's universality and perpetuity. The author grounds this role in two key Quranic verses, establishing the ummah as a witness over nations. Let's explore how this witnessing is understood as active guidance rather than passive observation.

Guided Path
1
Identify key terms
Note the term 'shuhood hadari' (civilizational witnessing) and 'ummah wasat' (middle/justly balanced nation). Understand that 'wasat' here implies justice and qualification for witnessing.
2
Locate Quranic evidence
Find the two verses cited: al-Baqarah 2:143 and al-Hajj 22:78. Notice how both establish a dual witness relationship: the Prophet over the ummah, and the ummah over humanity.
3
Analyze the logical flow
Trace the author's argument: universality and perpetuity of the call → the caller is a witness over the ummah → the ummah is a witness over other nations. This witnessing manifests through civilizational interaction and reformative guidance.
4
Distinguish active vs passive witnessing
Recognize that civilizational witnessing is not passive observation but active engagement—presenting the fruits of Islamic education as 'reformative guidance' and 'Allah's proof over humanity'.
This counters a common misunderstanding that witnessing is merely observational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشهود الحضاري: وذلك انبثاق من عالمية الدعوة وخلودها فإن الرائد لا يكذب أهله، ولذلك فهو - أي صاحب الدعوة - يكون شاهده على أمة الشهود الحضاري، كما أن هذه الأمة - أمة الإجابة - شاهدة على بقية الأمم: وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطًا لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ وَيَكُونَ الرَّسُولُ عَلَيْكُمْ شَهِيداً [البقرة: ١٤٣/٢]. وَجاهِدُوا فِي اللَّهِ حَقَّ جِهَادِهِ هُوَ اجْتَباكُمْ وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَجٍ مِلَّةَ أَبِيكُمْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ هُوَ سَمَاكُمُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَفِي هَذَا لِيَكُونَ الرَّسُولُ شَهِيداً عَلَيْكُمْ وَتَكُونُوا شُهَداءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ فَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ وَاعْتَصِمُوا بِاللهِ هُوَ مَوْلاكُمْ فَنِعْمَ الْمَوْلَى وَنِعْمَ النّصيرُ [الحج: ٧٨/٢٢]. إن من الطبيعي في ظل الإقرار بعالمية التربية الإسلامية وخلودها أن تنزع هذه التربية منزعاً حضارياً في تفاعلها مع العالم من حولنا، فتقدم ثمار هذه التربية في صورة هداية إصلاحية تمثل حجة الله على الإنسانية.
Civilizational witnessing: And that is an emanation from the universality of the call and its perpetuity, for the guide does not lie to his people. Therefore, he - the caller - is a witness over the nation of civilizational witnessing, just as this nation - the nation of response - is a witness over the rest of the nations: 'And thus we have made you a middle nation that you may be witnesses over the people and the Messenger may be a witness over you' [Al-Baqarah 2:143]. 'And strive for Allah with the striving due to Him. He has chosen you and has not placed upon you in the religion any difficulty. [It is] the religion of your father, Ibrahim. He named you Muslims before [in former scriptures] and in this [revelation] that the Messenger may be a witness over you and you may be witnesses over the people. So establish prayer, give zakah, and hold fast to Allah. He is your protector, and excellent is the protector, and excellent is the helper' [Al-Hajj 22:78]. It is natural, in light of acknowledging the universality and perpetuity of Islamic education, that this education takes a civilizational direction in its interaction with the world around us, presenting the fruits of this education in the form of reformative guidance that represents Allah's proof over humanity.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'civilizational witnessing' (shuhood hadari). It begins by stating that the universality and perpetuity of the Islamic call necessitate that the caller (the Prophet) is a witness over the ummah, and the ummah is a witness over other nations. Two Quranic verses are cited to support this: first, that Allah made the ummah a 'middle nation' (ummatan wasatan) to be witnesses over people, and the Messenger a witness over them; second, the verse from Surah Al-Hajj emphasizing the same witness relationship. The author then explains that this witnessing is a natural outcome of Islamic education's universality, whereby it interacts with the world in a civilizational manner, offering reformative guidance as Allah's proof. The passage highlights the role of the ummah as a model and witness for humanity.

Key Terms
الشهود الحضاري (al-shuhood al-hadari): The role of the Islamic ummah as a witness over other nations through its civilizational and educational interaction, based on Quranic mandate.
الأمة الوسط (al-ummah al-wasat): The middle (justly balanced) nation, a designation for the Muslim ummah as witnesses over humanity. [Note: In traditional tafsir, 'wasat' means 'just' or 'moderate'; here it emphasizes the witnessing function.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) To be a witness through civilizational interaction and reformative guidance
C) To engage in trade and economic exchange
D) To isolate themselves from non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
Civilizational witnessing means the ummah actively guides and reforms humanity through the fruits of Islamic education, fulfilling its Quranic mandate as a witness over nations.

The Prophetic Educational Sequence: Tilawah, Tazkiyah, Ta'leem
Author describes the educational and tarbiyyah nature of Muhammad's prophethood with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three-step prophetic educational sequence and explain its methodological rationale using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The Quranic sequence of recitation, purification, teaching is a deliberate methodological key for true education.

In this passage, the author draws from three Quranic verses to uncover the balanced order of the Prophet's mission. Understanding this sequence is essential for grasping how Islamic education integrates knowledge, ethics, and spirituality. We will examine the verses, extract the sequence, and analyze why recitation must precede purification, and purification must precede teaching.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Quranic verses
Locate the verses cited: Al-Baqarah 2:151, Al-Jumu'ah 62:2, and Aal-e-Imran 3:164. Each verse describes the Prophet's functions.
All three verses share a similar structure.
2
Extract the common elements
From each verse, isolate the three key actions: recitation (tilawah), purification (tazkiyah), and teaching (ta'leem) of the Book and wisdom.
The order is consistent across all verses.
3
Notice the order and its significance
Observe that tilawah always comes first, then tazkiyah, then ta'leem. The author argues this order is a necessary methodological balance.
The sequence is not arbitrary but reflects a pedagogical principle.
4
Understand the rationale for each step
Recitation provides the key of knowledge (correct concepts). Purification cleanses the learner from corruptions. Teaching then builds on a purified foundation.
This prevents mixing sound concepts with deviant ones.
5
Reflect on the integration of all three
The author emphasizes that education must rely on a philosophical framework that combines recitation, purification, and wisdom together.
All three are needed simultaneously in the educational process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتتميز دعوة محمد - - بأنها تعليمية تربوية في جوهرها، كما تصرح بذلك هذه الآيات: كَما أَرْسَلْنا فِيكُمْ رَسُولاً مِنْكُمْ يَتْلُو عَلَيْكُمْ آيَاتِنَا وَيُزَكِّيكُمْ وَيُعَلِّمُكُمُ الْكِتابَ وَالْحِكْمَةَ وَيُعَلِّمُكُمْ مَا لَمْ تَكُونُوا تَعْلَمُونَ [البقرة: ١٥١/٢]. هُوَ الَّذِي بَعَثَ فِي الأُمِّيِّينَ رَسُولاً مِنْهُمْ يَتْلُو عَلَيْهِمْ آيَاتِهِ وَيُزَكِّيهِمْ وَيُعَلِّمُهُمُ الْكِتابَ وَالْحِكْمَةَ وَإِنْ كَانُوا مِنْ قَبْلُ لَفِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينٍ [الجمعة: ٢/٦٢]. لَقَدْ مَنَّ اللَّهُ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ بَعَثَ فِيهِمْ رَسُولاً مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ يَتْلُو عَلَيْهِمْ آيَاتِهِ وَيُزَكِّيهِمْ وَيُعَلِّمُهُمُ الْكِتابَ وَالْحِكْمَةَ وَإِن كَانُوا مِنْ قَبْلُ لَفِي ضَلالٍ مُبينٍ [آل عمران: ١٦٤/٣]. وهذه السمة تتحدث عن نفسها إذ هي تصرح بغاية الوحي الخاص بالدعوة وكأن ذلك يشير إلى أن جميع مهام الوحي إن هي إلا منضوية تحت قضيتي التعليم والتربية. وهنا ملحظ هام هو أن تقدّم القراءة (التلاوة) على التربية (التزكية)، ثم ورود التعليم بعد التزكية مؤشر على التوازن الذي يمثل ضرورة منهجية في العملية التعليمية التربوية. فحتى لا تختلط المفهومات السليمة بالردئية المنحرفة كان لابد من التزام مفتاح المعرفة وهي (القراءة) قبل عملية التزكية. ثم إن التزكية تسبق التعليم، وذلك يتضمن ضرورة التطهير لنفس المتعلم من دنس المحاذير التربوية التي تتنافى مع أخلاق المعرفة، بل وتفسد العملية التربوية برمتها، فكان الترتيب المتوازن يقتضي الابتداء بالقراءة فالتربية (التزكية) فالتعليم. وفي الأحوال جمعيها يلزم الجمع بين استناد العملية التربوية إلى فلسفة تحدد المفهومات الأساسية والقواعد والمبادئ الكبرى لتنظيم الحياة، ثم الجمع بعد ذلك بين التعليم والتزكية والحكمة في وقت واحد.
The call of Muhammad - - is distinguished by being educational and tarbiyyah in its essence, as these verses declare: 'Just as We have sent among you a messenger from yourselves reciting to you Our verses and purifying you and teaching you the Book and wisdom and teaching you that which you did not know' [Al-Baqarah 2:151]. 'It is He who has sent among the unlettered a messenger from themselves reciting to them His verses and purifying them and teaching them the Book and wisdom, although they were before in manifest error' [Al-Jumu'ah 62:2]. 'Certainly did Allah confer [great] favor upon the believers when He sent among them a messenger from themselves, reciting to them His verses and purifying them and teaching them the Book and wisdom, although they were before in manifest error' [Aal-e-Imran 3:164]. This characteristic speaks for itself, as it declares the purpose of the revelation specific to the call, as if indicating that all tasks of revelation are subsumed under the two issues of education and tarbiyyah. Here an important observation is that the precedence of recitation (qira'ah/tilawah) over tarbiyyah (tazkiyah), and then the appearance of education after tazkiyah, is an indicator of the balance that represents a methodological necessity in the educational-tarbiyyah process. So that sound concepts may not be mixed with deviant ones, it is necessary to adhere to the key of knowledge, which is recitation, before the process of tazkiyah. Then tazkiyah precedes education, and that includes the necessity of purifying the soul of the learner from the filth of educational prohibitions that contradict the ethics of knowledge, and even corrupt the entire educational process. So the balanced order requires beginning with recitation, then tarbiyyah (tazkiyah), then education. And in all cases, it is necessary to combine the educational process's reliance on a philosophy that defines the fundamental concepts and rules and major principles for organizing life, and then combine education, tazkiyah, and wisdom at the same time.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage explains the educational and tarbiyyah nature of the Prophet's mission. It begins by stating that Muhammad's call is inherently educational and tarbiyyah, supported by three Quranic verses (Al-Baqarah 2:151, Al-Jumu'ah 62:2, Aal-e-Imran 3:164) that emphasize the sequence: recitation (tilawah), purification (tazkiyah), and teaching (ta'leem). The author then argues that this sequence is deliberate: recitation must come first to provide correct concepts (key of knowledge), then purification to cleanse the learner, and finally teaching. The passage highlights that all functions of revelation are subsumed under education and tarbiyyah. It also stresses the need for a philosophical foundation that defines basic concepts and principles for organizing life, and the integration of education, purification, and wisdom. The commentary should follow the author's order: first the verses, then the analysis of the sequence, and finally the philosophical integration.

Key Terms
التزكية
التلاوة
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct sequence in the prophetic educational process?
A) Teaching, purification, recitation
B) Recitation, teaching, purification
C) Recitation, purification, teaching
D) Purification, recitation, teaching

Key Takeaway
The prophetic educational model involves a deliberate sequence (tilawah → tazkiyah → ta'leem) that ensures knowledge is grounded in revelation and accompanied by spiritual purification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the same analytical method, examine another Quranic verse that describes prophetic functions (e.g., Surah Al-Imran 3:164 again, or Surah Al-Baqarah 2:129) and identify the sequence. Write a short paragraph explaining the order and its possible rationale.
?

Revelation as Source and Tool in Islamic Epistemology
Author notes the classification of knowledge and the role of revelation as a source and tool.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the tripartite Islamic classification of knowledge from secular classifications and explain the dual role of revelation as both a source and a tool.

Core Idea
Revelation is both a source of knowledge and a method, setting Islamic epistemology apart.

In this passage, the author builds on a prior discussion of knowledge classification, declaring that the tripartite model—sense, reason, and revelation—is the preferred Islamic framework. Revelation is not merely a repository of facts; it also serves as an active tool for acquiring knowledge. This dual nature is what distinguishes the Islamic view from secular epistemologies that exclude revelation entirely.

Guided Path
1
Recall the classification types
The author mentions that a classification of knowledge was previously presented. Think about what categories were discussed. In Islamic epistemology, common classifications include sense (hiss), reason ('aql), and revelation (wahy).
2
Identify the tripartite model
The author favors the 'tripartite classification' (al-tasneef al-thulathi). Identify the three components: sense, reason, and revelation. Note that revelation is placed alongside the other two as an equal source.
3
Analyze the dual role of revelation
The passage explicitly states that revelation is 'a source of knowledge and a tool for it simultaneously' (مصدرا للمعرفة وأداة لها معاً). Distinguish: as a source (مصدر), revelation provides content (e.g., unseen matters); as a tool (أداة), revelation provides a method (e.g., interpreting scripture).
This dual aspect is often misunderstood: revelation is not just a data source but a means of knowing.
4
Contrast with secular classifications
The author contrasts the Islamic classification with 'prevailing secular types' (التصنيف الوضعية الأخرى). Secular classifications typically include only sense and reason, excluding revelation. This exclusion is the key difference.
5
Evaluate the distinguishing feature
The author claims that revelation is 'the distinguishing feature of the Islamic classification.' Reflect on why this matters: including revelation allows knowledge of the unseen (ghayb) and provides a foundation for theological and legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التكامل بين الوحي ومصادر المعرفة الأخرى: سبق إيراد تصنيف المعرفة وتم ترجيح التصنيف الثلاثي منها، والذي يضم إلى جانب الحس والعقل - الوحي، بوصفه مصدرا للمعرفة وأداة لها معاً. وعنصر الوحي هذا هو ميزة التصنيف الإسلامي على غيره من أنواع التصنيف الوضعية الأخرى السائدة.
Integration between revelation and other sources of knowledge: The classification of knowledge was previously presented, and the tripartite classification was favored, which includes, alongside sense and reason, revelation as a source of knowledge and a tool for it simultaneously. This element of revelation is the distinguishing feature of the Islamic classification over other prevailing secular types of classification.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage discusses the integration of revelation with other sources of knowledge. It refers to a prior discussion about knowledge classification and states that a tripartite classification (sense, reason, revelation) is preferred. Revelation is presented not only as a source (mabdun) but also as a tool (adatan) for knowledge. The author emphasizes that the inclusion of revelation is what distinguishes the Islamic classification from secular (wad'iyyah) classifications that only include sense and reason. The passage is short but makes a critical point: revelation is both a source and an instrument, and it is the unique feature of Islamic epistemology.

Key Terms
الوحي
التصنيف الثلاثي
التصنيف الوضعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Islamic classification of knowledge uniquely incorporates revelation as both a source and a tool, setting it apart from secular classifications that exclude it.

The Balanced Order of Revelation: Recitation, Purification, Teaching
Author explains the purpose of revelation and the balanced order of recitation, purification, and teaching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological order of recitation, purification, and teaching in revelation and justify why recitation precedes purification and purification precedes teaching.

Core Idea
Revelation's order is not arbitrary—it is a pedagogical necessity for sound knowledge.

This passage explores the Quranic description of the Prophet's mission: reciting verses, purifying the people, and teaching the Book and Wisdom. The author argues that this order reflects a deliberate educational methodology: first establish correct concepts through recitation, then purify the soul, then impart deeper teaching. Understanding this order helps us see how revelation integrates knowledge and spiritual growth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three tasks of revelation listed in the verse.
The passage explicitly mentions recitation (tilawa), purification (tazkiya), and teaching (ta'lim). In the Quran (Al-Imran 164), these are presented in that order.
2
Observe the author's claim about the order.
The author notes that recitation precedes purification, and purification precedes teaching. This is not accidental but indicates a methodological necessity.
3
Understand the rationale for recitation before purification.
Recitation provides the key of knowledge to establish correct concepts before purification, so that sound concepts are not mixed with deviant ones.
4
Understand why purification precedes teaching.
Purification cleanses the learner from moral and intellectual corruptions that would hinder the educational process and conflict with the ethics of knowledge.
5
Synthesize the overall balanced order.
The balanced order is: reading (recitation) → education/purification → teaching. All must be grounded in a comprehensive philosophy that integrates these elements simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه السمة تتحدث عن نفسها إذ هي تصرح بغاية الوحي الخاص بالدعوة وكأن ذلك يشير إلى أن جميع مهام الوحي إن هي إلا منضوية تحت قضيتي التعليم والتربية. وهنا ملحظ هام هو أن تقدّم القراءة (التلاوة) على التربية (التزكية)، ثم ورود التعليم بعد التزكية مؤشر على التوازن الذي يمثل ضرورة منهجية في العملية التعليمية التربوية. فحتى لا تختلط المفهومات السليمة بالردئية المنحرفة كان لابد من التزام مفتاح المعرفة وهي (القراءة) قبل عملية التزكية. ثم إن التزكية تسبق التعليم، وذلك يتضمن ضرورة التطهير لنفس المتعلم من دنس المحاذير التربوية التي تتنافى مع أخلاق المعرفة، بل وتفسد العملية التربوية برمتها، فكان الترتيب المتوازن يقتضي الابتداء بالقراءة فالتربية التزكية) فالتعليم. وفي الأحوال جمعيها يلزم الجمع بين استناد العملية التربوية إلى فلسفة تحدد المفهومات الأساسية والقواعد والمبادئ الكبرى لتنظيم الحياة، ثم الجمع بعد ذلك بين التعليم والتزكية والحكمة في وقت واحد.
And this characteristic speaks for itself, for it declares the purpose of revelation specific to the call, as if indicating that all tasks of revelation are subsumed under the two issues of teaching and education. And here is an important observation: that the precedence of reading (recitation) over education (purification), then the occurrence of teaching after purification, is an indicator of the balance that represents a methodological necessity in the educational-educational process. So that sound concepts do not mix with deviant corrupt ones, it was necessary to adhere to the key of knowledge, which is reading, before the process of purification. Then purification precedes teaching, and that entails the necessity of purification of the learner's soul from the filth of educational prohibitions that conflict with the ethics of knowledge, indeed spoil the entire educational process. So the balanced order required beginning with reading, then education (purification), then teaching. And in all cases, it is necessary to combine basing the educational process on a philosophy that defines the basic concepts, rules, and major principles for organizing life, then to combine after that between teaching, purification, and wisdom at the same time.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological analysis of the purpose of revelation as stated in the Quranic verse (Al-Imran 164). The author focuses on the order of the three tasks: recitation (tilawa), purification (tazkiya), and teaching (ta'lim). The author argues that this order is intentional and reflects a balanced educational methodology. First, recitation is prioritized to establish correct understanding before any purification, so that sound concepts are not mixed with corrupt ones. Then purification follows to cleanse the learner from moral and intellectual impediments. Finally, teaching imparts deeper knowledge. The author emphasizes that all these must be grounded in a comprehensive philosophy that integrates education, purification, and wisdom simultaneously.

Key Terms
الوحي
التلاوة
التزكية
التعليم

D) Recitation, then teaching, then purification

Key Takeaway
The order of recitation, purification, and teaching in revelation is a deliberately balanced pedagogical sequence essential for sound Islamic education.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

10 min
Three Conditions for Integrating Revelation with Other Sources
Author lists three necessary conditions for integrating revelation with reason and sense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the three conditions for integrating revelation with reason and sense, and apply them to evaluate an Islamic knowledge claim.

Core Idea
Integration of revelation requires deep, comprehensive, and unified knowledge rooted in Tawhid.

The acceptance of revelation as a source of knowledge alongside reason and sense requires not just a theoretical acknowledgment but practical conditions for proper integration. The author presents three objective conditions that must be met for these sources to work together harmoniously. These conditions—soundness, comprehensiveness, and unity—are drawn from Quranic principles and ensure that knowledge is not fragmented or superficial.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the tripartite classification
The passage assumes a classification of knowledge sources into revelation, reason, and sense. Understand that the author is building on this classification to negotiate their integration.
2
Extract the first condition: rasukh
Note the term 'rasukh fī al-ilm' (soundness in knowledge). The author defines it as deep understanding of the subject's history and development, citing Quranic verses praising the knowledgeable and criticizing superficiality.
Rasukh implies moving beyond surface-level acquaintance to historical depth.
3
Extract the second condition: ihata wa shumul
Identify 'al-ihāṭa wa al-shumūl' (comprehensiveness and inclusiveness). This condition demands complete knowledge of the subject's spatial and temporal boundaries, avoiding partial understanding. Quranic verses warn against denying what one does not fully comprehend.
Partial knowledge leads to false denial or rejection.
4
Extract the third condition: wahdat al-ma'rifa
Observe 'riʿāyat waḥdat al-maʿrifa' (observing the unity of knowledge). This condition emphasizes that all knowledge is ultimately unified, rooted in Tawhid (the oneness of God). Integration requires acknowledging this foundational unity.
This condition prevents epistemological fragmentation.
5
Apply the conditions
Given a claim about Islamic knowledge—for example, a ruling derived from the Quran and science—evaluate whether it meets these three conditions. Does the claimant have deep historical understanding? Comprehensive knowledge? Is the knowledge unified under Tawhid?
This prevents shallow or partial integration.

وانطلاقاً من موضوعية هذا التصنيف الثلاثي، فإن حتمية التكامل بين هذه المصادر والطرائق تغدو من مستلزمات القبول به ولكن ثمة شروط موضوعية ثلاثة أحسب ضرورة توفرها، كي يتم التعاون بين هذه المصادر والطرائق، وذلك على النحو التالي:
الشرط الأول: الرسوخ في العلم
والمقصود بالرسوخ هنا التعمق في فهم الموضوع من حيث تاريخه، وتطوراته التي أوصلته إلى المرحلة الراهنة: {وَالرّاسِخُونَ فِي الْعِلْمِ يَقُولُونَ آمَنَا بِهِ كُلِّ مِنْ عِنْدِ رَبِّنَا} [آل عمران: ٧/٣] ويشنع القرآن على ذوي الأفهام السطحية، الذين لا يتجاوز إدراكهم الحالة القائمة لموضوع المعرفة، وكأنها آخر حلقات هذا التطور الزمني: {يَعْلَمُونَ ظَاهِراً مِنَ الْحَياةِ الدُّنْيا} [الروم: ٧/٣٠].
الشرط الثاني: الإحاطة والشمول
ونعني بالإحاطة والشمول الإحاطة الكلية والتفصيلية المتشعبة بحدود الموضوع المكاني والزماني، والحذر من المعرفة الجزئية: {بَلْ كَذَّبُوا بِما لَمْ يُحِيطُوا بِعِلْمِهِ} [يونس: ٣٩/١٠]. {قالَ أَكَذَّبْتُمْ بِآيَاتِي وَلَمْ تُحِيطُوا بِها عِلْماً} [النمل: ٢٨٤/٢٧].
الشرط الثالث: مراعاة وحدة المعرفة
أي إنه باسترجاع الذهن لمصادر المعرفة وطرائقها، وميادينها، ووحـــدة المعرفة والتي تجسدت هذه الأخيرة أكثر ما تجسّدت في أساس الوحدانية لله
And based on the objectivity of this tripartite classification, the inevitability of integration between these sources and methods becomes a requirement of accepting it, but there are three objective conditions that I consider necessary to be fulfilled for cooperation between these sources and methods, as follows:
The first condition: Soundness in knowledge (rasukh fī al-ilm). By soundness here is meant deep understanding of the subject in terms of its history and developments that brought it to the current stage: {And those firmly grounded in knowledge say, 'We believe in it; all is from our Lord'} [Al-Imran 7/3]. And the Quran criticizes those with superficial understandings, whose perception does not go beyond the current state of the subject of knowledge, as if it were the last link in this temporal development: {They know only the outward appearance of the life of this world} [Ar-Rum 30/7].
The second condition: Comprehensiveness and inclusiveness (al-ihāṭa wa al-shumūl). By comprehensiveness and inclusiveness we mean the total and detailed knowledge of the spatial and temporal boundaries of the subject, and caution against partial knowledge: {But they denied that which they did not encompass in knowledge} [Yunus 10/39]. {He said, 'Did you deny My signs while you did not encompass them in knowledge?'} [An-Naml 27/84].
The third condition: Observing the unity of knowledge (riʿāyat waḥdat al-maʿrifa). That is, by recalling in the mind the sources of knowledge, its methods, and fields, and the unity of knowledge which is embodied most in the foundation of the oneness of God.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents the three conditions necessary for integrating revelation (wahy) with other sources of knowledge (reason and sense). The author begins by stating that acceptance of the tripartite classification (which includes revelation alongside sense and reason) necessitates integration, but integration requires three objective conditions. The first condition is 'rasukh fī al-ilm' (soundness in knowledge), meaning deep historical and developmental understanding of the subject, as opposed to superficial knowledge. The author supports this with Quranic verses praising those firmly grounded in knowledge and criticizing those who only know the outward appearance. The second condition is 'al-ihāṭa wa al-shumūl' (comprehensiveness and inclusiveness), which demands thorough knowledge of the subject's spatial and temporal dimensions, avoiding partial understanding. The third condition is 'riʿāyat waḥdat al-maʿrifa' (observing the unity of knowledge), which refers to the fundamental unity of all knowledge rooted in Tawhid (the oneness of God). These conditions ensure that revelation, reason, and sense work together harmoniously.

Key Terms
الرسوخ في العلم (al-rasukh fī al-ilm): Deeply rooted understanding that encompasses the historical development and current state of a subject, contrasted with superficial knowledge.
الإحاطة والشمول (al-ihāṭa wa al-shumūl): Comprehensive and inclusive knowledge of a subject's spatial and temporal boundaries, avoiding partial or fragmented understanding.
وحدة المعرفة (waḥdat al-maʿrifa): The unity of all knowledge, ultimately grounded in the oneness of God (Tawhid), which integrates different sources and fields.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, which of the following is NOT one of the three conditions for integrating revelation with other knowledge sources?
A) Soundness in knowledge
B) Comprehensiveness and inclusiveness
C) Independence of each source
D) Observing the unity of knowledge

Key Takeaway
For revelation to properly integrate with reason and sense, one must possess deep historical knowledge, comprehensive scope, and a Tawhid-based unified perspective.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Evaluate the following claim using the three conditions: 'The Quranic account of creation is compatible with the Big Bang theory.' What would a scholar need to check under each condition?
?
Identify which condition is violated when someone interprets a Quranic verse on riba without studying its historical context and the broader economic principles of Islam.

Integrated Knowledge in Islamic Education
Explains the necessity of integrated knowledge in Islamic education

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why knowledge must be unified and not contradictory, especially in Islamic education.

Core Idea
Knowledge is a unified whole; fragmentation leads to destructive opposition.

The author begins by emphasizing that a teacher should be knowledgeable in multiple fields to ensure integrated knowledge. This is particularly critical in Islamic education because of its direct link to revelation, where error has severe consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim about knowledge integration
Read the first paragraph and notice how the author argues that a teacher's breadth of knowledge leads to unity and avoids contradiction.
2
Distinguish between Islamic and non-Islamic specializations
The author states that the conditions for integration apply more emphatically to Islamic education due to its direct link to revelation.
3
Understand the consequences of error
Error in Islamic education is more severe because it relates to revelation, while other fields allow more ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
يكون المعلم عالماً بكل شيء - ما أمكنه – عن مادته وتخصصه، عالماً أو ملماً بشيء عن سائر المواد ولتخصصات الأخرى. وبذلك تتحد المعرفة وتتكامل ولا تتجزأ أو تتعارض، فيحصل اختلاف التنوع الإيجابي البناء، وينتفي اختلاف التضاد السلبي المدمر .
والحاصل أن هذه الشروط ومتضمناتها التربوية تنطبق على التخصصات جميعها، مثلما تنطبق على فروع التربية الإسلامية جميعها، بل هي في حق هذه الأخيرة أشد وأكد لأن النتائج المترتبة على الخطأ أو التقصير فيها ليست كالتقصير أو الخطأ في غيرها من التخصصات، إذ التربية الإسلامية على علاقة مباشرة بالوحي، في حين يتسع نطاق الاجتهاد وإعمال النظر الإنساني، ومصادر المعرفة الرئيسة والتبعية الأخرى في التخصصات غير الشرعية.
ومن إبداع البيان القرآني تلخيصه لعضوية العلاقة بين كل من الوحي والعقل والحس بقول الله تعالى:
وَقَدْ جاءَكُمْ بَصَائِرُ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ فَلِنَفْسِهِ وَمَنْ عَمِيَ فَعَلَيْهَا وَمَا أَنَا عَلَيْكُمْ بِحَفِيظٍ [الأنعام: ١٠٤/٦].
إن هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال - تشير إلى القرآن الكريم باعتباره بصائر حسية وعقلية بآن واحد. وحقاً فإن هذا أبلغ تعبير وأوجزه في تحديد المراد. وقد فَطِن إلى تلك الحقيقة ونبه عليها بعض أئمة المدارس الإسلامية الأقدمين فالإمام الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤هـ) من أئمة المتكلمين يقف عند تفسير الآية السابقة قائلا: (بصائر جمع البصيرة، وكما أن البصر اسم للإدراك التام الكامل الحاصل بالعين التي في الرأس، فالبصيرة للإدراك التام الحاصل في القلب. قال تعالى: بَلِ الإِنسانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةً [القيامة: ١٤/٧٥] أي له نفسه معرفة تامة).
وعن عضوية العلاقة بين العقل والوحي يقول الغزالي – من مدرسة التصوف - اعلم أن العقل لن يهتدي إلا بالشرع، والشرع لم يتبين إلا بالعقل فالأس والشرع كالبناء، ولن يغني أس ما لم يكن بناء. ولن يثبت بناء ما لم يكن أس.
وأيضا فالعقل كالبصر والشرع كالشعاع ولن يغني البصر ما لم يكن شعاع من خارج، ولن يغني الشعاع ما لم يكن بصر ، لهذا قال تعالى: ﴿قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ مِنَ اللهِ نُورٌ وَكِتابٌ مُبِينٌ يَهْدِي بِهِ اللهُ مَنِ اتَّبَعَ رِضْوَانَهُ سُبُلَ السَّلامِ وَيُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُماتِ إِلَى النُّورِ... (المائدة: ١٥/٥-١٦].
وأيضاً: فالعقل كالسراج، والشرع كالزيت الذي يمده، فما لم يكن زيت لم يحصل السراج، وما لم يكن سراج لم يضئ الزيت وعلى هذا نبه الله سبحانه بقوله تعالى: واللهُ نُورُ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ مَثَلُ نُورِهِ كَمِشْكَاةٍ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ الْمِصْبَاحُ فِي زُجَاجَةٍ الزُّجاجَةُ كَأَنها كَوْكَبٌ دُرِّيٌ يُوقَدُ مِنْ شَجَرَةٍ مُبَارَكَةٍ زَيْتُونَةٍ لا شَرْقِيَّةِ وَلا غَرْبِيَّةٍ يَكادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِيءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌ نُورٌ عَلَى نور [النور: ٣٥/٢٤]. فالشرع عقل خارج، والعقـل شـرع من داخـل، وهمـا متعاضدان بل متحدان ...)).
وفي سبيل إثبات عدم التعارض بين السمع والعقل أيضا ألف شيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية (ت: ٧٢٨هـ). كتابه الشهير : (درء تعارض العقل والنقل أو موافقة صحيح المنقول لصريح المعقول.
وابن تيمية إمام معتبر في المدرسة السلفية، وقد كشف وهم التعارض المزعوم في هذا الكتاب ومما قال إذا قيل تعارض دليلان سواء كانا سمعيين أو
Chapter Three: The Third Section – Revelation
The teacher must be knowledgeable about everything – as much as possible – regarding his subject and specialization, and knowledgeable or familiar with something about the other subjects and specializations. Thereby knowledge is unified and integrated, not fragmented or contradictory, resulting in positive constructive diversity, and eliminating destructive negative opposition.
The conclusion is that these conditions and their educational implications apply to all specializations, just as they apply to all branches of Islamic education. Indeed, they are more severe and emphatic in the latter because the consequences of error or shortcoming in them are not like error or shortcoming in other specializations, since Islamic education is directly related to revelation, while the scope of ijtihad and human reasoning expands, along with the primary and secondary sources of knowledge in non-Shar'i specializations.
Among the creative expressions of the Qur'anic discourse is its summary of the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense in the words of Allah Almighty:
"And there have come to you insights (basa'ir) from your Lord; whoever sees clearly does so for himself, and whoever is blind does so against himself, and I am not a keeper over you." [Al-An'am 6:104]
This verse – for example – indicates that the Qur'an is insights that are both sensory and rational at the same time. Truly, this is the most eloquent and concise expression in determining the intent. Some of the early imams of Islamic schools were aware of this fact and alerted to it. Imam al-Razi (d. 604 AH), one of the imams of the theologians, pauses at the interpretation of the previous verse, saying: "Basa'ir is the plural of basirah, and just as 'basar' is the name for complete perfect perception obtained through the eye in the head, so 'basirah' is for complete perception obtained in the heart. Allah Almighty said: 'Rather, man is a witness against himself' [Al-Qiyamah 75:14], meaning he has complete knowledge of himself."
Regarding the organic relationship between reason and revelation, al-Ghazali – from the school of Sufism – says: "Know that reason is not guided except by the Shari'ah, and the Shari'ah is not clarified except by reason. So reason is like the foundation and the Shari'ah is like the building; a foundation is of no use without a building, and a building cannot stand without a foundation.
Also, reason is like eyesight and the Shari'ah is like light; eyesight is of no use without external light, and light is of no use without eyesight. For this, Allah Almighty said: 'There has come to you from Allah a light and a clear Book. By it Allah guides those who follow His pleasure to the ways of peace and brings them out of darkness into the light...' [Al-Ma'idah 5:15-16].
Also: reason is like a lamp, and the Shari'ah is like the oil that fuels it; without oil, the lamp does not exist, and without a lamp, the oil does not illuminate. And Allah Almighty indicated this in His saying: 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth. The example of His light is like a niche within which is a lamp, the lamp is within glass, the glass as if it were a pearly star, lit from a blessed olive tree, neither of the east nor of the west, whose oil would almost glow even if no fire touched it. Light upon light.' [An-Nur 24:35]. So the Shari'ah is external reason, and reason is internal Shari'ah, and they are mutually supportive, indeed united..."
And in order to prove that there is no contradiction between transmitted revelation (sam') and reason, Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya (d. 728 AH) authored his famous book: "Dar' Ta'arud al-'Aql wa al-Naql aw Muwafaqat Sahih al-Manqul li Sarih al-Ma'qul" (Refutation of the Contradiction between Reason and Revelation or Agreement of Sound Transmission with Clear Reason).
Ibn Taymiyya is a respected imam in the Salafi school, and he exposed the alleged illusion of contradiction in this book. Among what he said: "If it is said that two proofs contradict, whether they are transmitted (sam'iyyan) or..."
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the relationship between revelation (wahy), reason ('aql), and sense (hiss) in Islamic thought. The author begins by emphasizing the necessity of integrated knowledge, where a teacher must be knowledgeable in his specialization and familiar with others, leading to unified knowledge free from contradiction. This applies especially to Islamic education because of its direct link to revelation, while other fields allow more room for human reasoning.
The author then presents a Qur'anic verse (6:104) as a concise summary of the organic relationship between these three sources: the Qur'an is described as 'basa'ir' (insights), which are both sensory and rational. Imam al-Razi's commentary clarifies that 'basa'ir' are perceptions of the heart, akin to physical sight ('basar') but for inner understanding, citing another verse (75:14).
Next, the author quotes al-Ghazali, who uses three analogies to illustrate the interdependence of reason and Shari'ah (revelation): they are like foundation and building, eyesight and light, and lamp and oil. Each analogy shows that neither can function without the other; they are mutually supportive and ultimately united. Al-Ghazali supports his analogies with Qur'anic verses from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:15-16) and Surah an-Nur (24:35).
Finally, the author references Ibn Taymiyya's work 'Dar' Ta'arud al-'Aql wa al-Naql', which aims to refute the alleged contradiction between reason and revelation. Ibn Taymiyya is presented as a key figure in the Salafi school who exposed the illusion of contradiction. The passage concludes with an incomplete statement from Ibn Taymiyya about allegedly contradictory proofs.
The overall message is that in the Islamic intellectual tradition, revelation, reason, and sense are not in conflict but are complementary and integrated sources of knowledge.

Key Terms
الوحي
العقل
الشرع

According to the passage, what is the result when knowledge is unified and not contradictory?
A) Fragmentation
B) Positive constructive diversity
C) Destructive opposition
D) Error

Key Takeaway
Integrated knowledge in Islamic education prevents error and contradiction, since it is directly tied to revelation.

Basa'ir: The Sensory-Rational Insights of the Qur'an
Explains the concept of basair as sensory-rational insights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'basa'ir' and explain how it combines sensory and rational elements according to al-Razi.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is described as basair—insights that are both sensory and rational.

The author presents Qur'an 6:104 as evidence that revelation addresses both senses and reason. Al-Razi's commentary clarifies that basirah is complete perception of the heart, analogous to physical sight.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and note the word 'basa'ir'
Verse 6:104 says 'there have come to you basair from your Lord'. Reflect on the plural form and its connotation.
2
Understand al-Razi's definition of basirah
Al-Razi distinguishes basirah from basar: basar is physical sight, basirah is complete perception in the heart. The Qur'an is thus both sensory (as recited) and rational (as understood).
3
Apply the concept to the Qur'an's epistemic role
The Qur'an provides insights that engage both the senses through its linguistic beauty and the intellect through its arguments.

Source Text

إن هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال - تشير إلى القرآن الكريم باعتباره بصائر حسية وعقلية بآن واحد. وحقاً فإن هذا أبلغ تعبير وأوجزه في تحديد المراد. وقد فَطِن إلى تلك الحقيقة ونبه عليها بعض أئمة المدارس الإسلامية الأقدمين فالإمام الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤هـ) من أئمة المتكلمين يقف عند تفسير الآية السابقة قائلا: (بصائر جمع البصيرة، وكما أن البصر اسم للإدراك التام الكامل الحاصل بالعين التي في الرأس، فالبصيرة للإدراك التام الحاصل في القلب. قال تعالى: بَلِ الإِنسانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةً [القيامة: ١٤/٧٥] أي له نفسه معرفة تامة).
وعن عضوية العلاقة بين العقل والوحي يقول الغزالي – من مدرسة التصوف - اعلم أن العقل لن يهتدي إلا بالشرع، والشرع لم يتبين إلا بالعقل فالأس والشرع كالبناء، ولن يغني أس ما لم يكن بناء. ولن يثبت بناء ما لم يكن أس.
وأيضا فالعقل كالبصر والشرع كالشعاع ولن يغني البصر ما لم يكن شعاع من خارج، ولن يغني الشعاع ما لم يكن بصر ، لهذا قال تعالى: ﴿قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ مِنَ اللهِ نُورٌ وَكِتابٌ مُبِينٌ يَهْدِي بِهِ اللهُ مَنِ اتَّبَعَ رِضْوَانَهُ سُبُلَ السَّلامِ وَيُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُماتِ إِلَى النُّورِ... (المائدة: ١٥/٥-١٦].
وأيضاً: فالعقل كالسراج، والشرع كالزيت الذي يمده، فما لم يكن زيت لم يحصل السراج، وما لم يكن سراج لم يضئ الزيت وعلى هذا نبه الله سبحانه بقوله تعالى: واللهُ نُورُ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ مَثَلُ نُورِهِ كَمِشْكَاةٍ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ الْمِصْبَاحُ فِي زُجَاجَةٍ الزُّجاجَةُ كَأَنها كَوْكَبٌ دُرِّيٌ يُوقَدُ مِنْ شَجَرَةٍ مُبَارَكَةٍ زَيْتُونَةٍ لا شَرْقِيَّةِ وَلا غَرْبِيَّةٍ يَكادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِيءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌ نُورٌ عَلَى نور [النور: ٣٥/٢٤]. فالشرع عقل خارج، والعقـل شـرع من داخـل، وهمـا متعاضدان بل متحدان ...)).
وفي سبيل إثبات عدم التعارض بين السمع والعقل أيضا ألف شيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية (ت: ٧٢٨هـ). كتابه الشهير : (درء تعارض العقل والنقل أو موافقة صحيح المنقول لصريح المعقول.
وابن تيمية إمام معتبر في المدرسة السلفية، وقد كشف وهم التعارض المزعوم في هذا الكتاب ومما قال إذا قيل تعارض دليلان سواء كانا سمعيين أو
Chapter Three: The Third Section – Revelation
The teacher must be knowledgeable about everything – as much as possible – regarding his subject and specialization, and knowledgeable or familiar with something about the other subjects and specializations. Thereby knowledge is unified and integrated, not fragmented or contradictory, resulting in positive constructive diversity, and eliminating destructive negative opposition.
The conclusion is that these conditions and their educational implications apply to all specializations, just as they apply to all branches of Islamic education. Indeed, they are more severe and emphatic in the latter because the consequences of error or shortcoming in them are not like error or shortcoming in other specializations, since Islamic education is directly related to revelation, while the scope of ijtihad and human reasoning expands, along with the primary and secondary sources of knowledge in non-Shar'i specializations.
Among the creative expressions of the Qur'anic discourse is its summary of the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense in the words of Allah Almighty:
"And there have come to you insights (basa'ir) from your Lord; whoever sees clearly does so for himself, and whoever is blind does so against himself, and I am not a keeper over you." [Al-An'am 6:104]
This verse – for example – indicates that the Qur'an is insights that are both sensory and rational at the same time. Truly, this is the most eloquent and concise expression in determining the intent. Some of the early imams of Islamic schools were aware of this fact and alerted to it. Imam al-Razi (d. 604 AH), one of the imams of the theologians, pauses at the interpretation of the previous verse, saying: "Basa'ir is the plural of basirah, and just as 'basar' is the name for complete perfect perception obtained through the eye in the head, so 'basirah' is for complete perception obtained in the heart. Allah Almighty said: 'Rather, man is a witness against himself' [Al-Qiyamah 75:14], meaning he has complete knowledge of himself."
Regarding the organic relationship between reason and revelation, al-Ghazali – from the school of Sufism – says: "Know that reason is not guided except by the Shari'ah, and the Shari'ah is not clarified except by reason. So reason is like the foundation and the Shari'ah is like the building; a foundation is of no use without a building, and a building cannot stand without a foundation.
Also, reason is like eyesight and the Shari'ah is like light; eyesight is of no use without external light, and light is of no use without eyesight. For this, Allah Almighty said: 'There has come to you from Allah a light and a clear Book. By it Allah guides those who follow His pleasure to the ways of peace and brings them out of darkness into the light...' [Al-Ma'idah 5:15-16].
Also: reason is like a lamp, and the Shari'ah is like the oil that fuels it; without oil, the lamp does not exist, and without a lamp, the oil does not illuminate. And Allah Almighty indicated this in His saying: 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth. The example of His light is like a niche within which is a lamp, the lamp is within glass, the glass as if it were a pearly star, lit from a blessed olive tree, neither of the east nor of the west, whose oil would almost glow even if no fire touched it. Light upon light.' [An-Nur 24:35]. So the Shari'ah is external reason, and reason is internal Shari'ah, and they are mutually supportive, indeed united..."
And in order to prove that there is no contradiction between transmitted revelation (sam') and reason, Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya (d. 728 AH) authored his famous book: "Dar' Ta'arud al-'Aql wa al-Naql aw Muwafaqat Sahih al-Manqul li Sarih al-Ma'qul" (Refutation of the Contradiction between Reason and Revelation or Agreement of Sound Transmission with Clear Reason).
Ibn Taymiyya is a respected imam in the Salafi school, and he exposed the alleged illusion of contradiction in this book. Among what he said: "If it is said that two proofs contradict, whether they are transmitted (sam'iyyan) or..."
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the relationship between revelation (wahy), reason ('aql), and sense (hiss) in Islamic thought. The author begins by emphasizing the necessity of integrated knowledge, where a teacher must be knowledgeable in his specialization and familiar with others, leading to unified knowledge free from contradiction. This applies especially to Islamic education because of its direct link to revelation, while other fields allow more room for human reasoning.
The author then presents a Qur'anic verse (6:104) as a concise summary of the organic relationship between these three sources: the Qur'an is described as 'basa'ir' (insights), which are both sensory and rational. Imam al-Razi's commentary clarifies that 'basa'ir' are perceptions of the heart, akin to physical sight ('basar') but for inner understanding, citing another verse (75:14).
Next, the author quotes al-Ghazali, who uses three analogies to illustrate the interdependence of reason and Shari'ah (revelation): they are like foundation and building, eyesight and light, and lamp and oil. Each analogy shows that neither can function without the other; they are mutually supportive and ultimately united. Al-Ghazali supports his analogies with Qur'anic verses from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:15-16) and Surah an-Nur (24:35).
Finally, the author references Ibn Taymiyya's work 'Dar' Ta'arud al-'Aql wa al-Naql', which aims to refute the alleged contradiction between reason and revelation. Ibn Taymiyya is presented as a key figure in the Salafi school who exposed the illusion of contradiction. The passage concludes with an incomplete statement from Ibn Taymiyya about allegedly contradictory proofs.
The overall message is that in the Islamic intellectual tradition, revelation, reason, and sense are not in conflict but are complementary and integrated sources of knowledge.

Key Terms
البصائر
الوحي
العقل
الحس

A) Physical sight
B) Complete perception of the heart
C) Rational deduction
D) Sensory experience

Key Takeaway
Basirah is the heart's complete perception, combining sensory and rational insights from revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
