Al-Ghazali's Analogies on Reason and Revelation
Explains the interdependence of reason and revelation via analogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Ghazali's three analogies demonstrating the interdependence of reason and the Shari'ah.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation are mutually dependent; neither functions without the other.

Al-Ghazali uses three vivid analogies: foundation and building, eyesight and light, and lamp and oil. Each illustrates that reason needs revelation for guidance, and revelation needs reason for clarification. The author then supports these analogies with Qur'anic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ghazali's first analogy
Reason is like the foundation, Shari'ah like the building. A foundation without a building is useless, and a building cannot stand without a foundation.
2
Examine the second analogy
Reason is like eyesight, Shari'ah like external light. Eyesight cannot see without light, and light is useless without eyesight.
3
Analyze the third analogy
Reason is like a lamp, Shari'ah like the oil that fuels it. Without oil, the lamp does not exist; without a lamp, oil does not illuminate.
4
Connect with the quoted verses
Al-Ghazali cites verses about light to reinforce the idea that revelation provides guidance that reason needs to function properly.

Source Text

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
يكون المعلم عالماً بكل شيء - ما أمكنه – عن مادته وتخصصه، عالماً أو ملماً بشيء عن سائر المواد ولتخصصات الأخرى. وبذلك تتحد المعرفة وتتكامل ولا تتجزأ أو تتعارض، فيحصل اختلاف التنوع الإيجابي البناء، وينتفي اختلاف التضاد السلبي المدمر .
والحاصل أن هذه الشروط ومتضمناتها التربوية تنطبق على التخصصات جميعها، مثلما تنطبق على فروع التربية الإسلامية جميعها، بل هي في حق هذه الأخيرة أشد وأكد لأن النتائج المترتبة على الخطأ أو التقصير فيها ليست كالتقصير أو الخطأ في غيرها من التخصصات، إذ التربية الإسلامية على علاقة مباشرة بالوحي، في حين يتسع نطاق الاجتهاد وإعمال النظر الإنساني، ومصادر المعرفة الرئيسة والتبعية الأخرى في التخصصات غير الشرعية.
ومن إبداع البيان القرآني تلخيصه لعضوية العلاقة بين كل من الوحي والعقل والحس بقول الله تعالى:

إن هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال - تشير إلى القرآن الكريم باعتباره بصائر حسية وعقلية بآن واحد. وحقاً فإن هذا أبلغ تعبير وأوجزه في تحديد المراد. وقد فَطِن إلى تلك الحقيقة ونبه عليها بعض أئمة المدارس الإسلامية الأقدمين فالإمام الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤هـ) من أئمة المتكلمين يقف عند تفسير الآية السابقة قائلا: (بصائر جمع البصيرة، وكما أن البصر اسم للإدراك التام الكامل الحاصل بالعين التي في الرأس، فالبصيرة للإدراك التام الحاصل في القلب. قال تعالى: بَلِ الإِنسانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةً [القيامة: ١٤/٧٥] أي له نفسه معرفة تامة).
وعن عضوية العلاقة بين العقل والوحي يقول الغزالي – من مدرسة التصوف - اعلم أن العقل لن يهتدي إلا بالشرع، والشرع لم يتبين إلا بالعقل فالأس والشرع كالبناء، ولن يغني أس ما لم يكن بناء. ولن يثبت بناء ما لم يكن أس.

(المائدة: ١٥/٥-١٦].

Ibn Taymiyya's Principle of Non-Contradiction between Definitive Reason and Revelation
Author presents Ibn Taymiyya's argument that definitive revelation cannot be contradicted by definitive reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that definitive revelation and definitive reason cannot genuinely contradict.

Core Idea
Definitive reason and definitive revelation never contradict; apparent contradictions stem from faulty reasoning.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya confronts a key challenge: what happens when reason seems to oppose a clear religious text? His answer is decisive: a genuine definitive rational proof can never overturn a definitive scriptural proof. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis
Find the exact phrase where Ibn Taymiyya states that it is impossible for a definitive rational proof to contradict a definitive scriptural proof.
Look for 'يمتنع أن يقوم عقلي قطعي يناقض هذا'.
2
Understand the consequence
Why does Ibn Taymiyya say that prioritizing reason over revelation leads to disbelief? Trace his reasoning.
He argues that it necessitates accusing the Prophet of falsehood, which is clear disbelief.
3
Extract the justification
How does he support the impossibility of contradiction? What logical or theological basis does he provide?
The basis is that both definitive reason and definitive revelation are sources of truth; they cannot conflict.
4
Distinguish types of arguments
Note the contrast between definitive (قطعي) and non-definitive arguments. Why is this distinction crucial?
Only definitive proofs are considered; non-definitive ones do not carry conclusive weight.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قدم العقلي لزم تكذيب الرسول فيما عُلم بالاضطرار أنه جاء به وهـذا هـو الكفر الصريح، فلا بد لهم من جواب عن هذا. والجواب عنه أنه يمتنع أن يقوم عقلي قطعي يناقض هذا. فتبين أن كل ما قام عليه دليل قطعي سمعي يمتنع أن يعارضه قطعي عقلي. وفي موطن آخر يتساءل ابن تيمية: فكيف يجوز أن يقال: إن في كتاب الله وسنة رسوله الصحيحة الثابتة عنه ما يعلم زيد وعمرو بعقله أنه باطل ؟ وأن يكون كل من اشتبه عليه شيء مما أخبر به النبي - صلى الله عليه وسلم - قدم رأيه على نص الرسول - صلى الله عليه وسلم - في أنباء الغيب التي ضل فيها عامة من دخل فيها بمجرد رأيه، من دون الاستهداء بهدي الله، والاستضاءة بنور الله الذي أرسل به رسله وأنزل به كتبه، مع علم كل أحد بقصوره وتقصيره في هذا الباب، وبما وقع فيه من أصحابه وغير أصحابه من الاضطراب. ففي الجملة النصوص الثابتة في الكتاب والسنة لا يعارضها معقول بين قط، ولا يعارضها إلا ما فيه اضطراب واشتباه لم يعلم أنه حق، بل نقول قولاً عاماً كلياً إن النصوص الثابتة عن الرسول - صلى الله عليه وسلم - لم يعارضها قط صريح معقول، فضلاً عن أن يكون مقدَّماً عليها، وإنما الذي يعارضها شبه وخيالات، مبناها على معان متشابهة وألفاظ مجملة فمتى وقع الاستفسار والبيان ظهر أن ما عارضها شبه سوفسطائية، لا براهين عقلية.
If the rational is given precedence, it necessitates accusing the Messenger of falsehood in what is known by necessity that he brought, and this is clear disbelief. So they must have an answer for this. The answer is that it is impossible for a definitive rational proof to contradict this. So it becomes clear that everything for which a definitive scriptural proof stands, it is impossible for a definitive rational proof to oppose it. And in another place Ibn Taymiyya asks: How can it be permitted to say that in the Book of God and the authentic Sunnah of His Messenger there is something that Zayd and Amr know by their reason to be false? And that everyone who is confused about something from what the Prophet - peace be upon him - informed, places his opinion before the text of the Messenger - peace be upon him - concerning the news of the unseen, in which most of those who entered into it went astray by mere opinion, without guidance from God's guidance and illumination from God's light by which He sent His messengers and revealed His books, while everyone knows his own inadequacy and shortcoming in this subject, and the confusion that occurred among his Companions and others? In summary, the confirmed texts from the Book and the Sunnah are never opposed by any clear rational proof, and nothing opposes them except that which contains confusion and ambiguity, not known to be true. Rather, we say as a general universal statement: The confirmed texts from the Messenger - peace be upon him - have never been opposed by any clear rational proof, let alone that it could be given precedence over them. The only things that oppose them are sophistical doubts and fantasies, based on ambiguous meanings and vague expressions. Whenever clarification and explanation occur, it becomes apparent that what opposed them are sophistical doubts, not rational demonstrations.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's critical argument against those who claim a genuine contradiction between definitive rational proofs and definitive scriptural texts. The author first states the consequence of prioritizing reason over revelation: it leads to accusing the Prophet of falsehood in matters known necessarily from him, which is clear disbelief. Therefore, those who make such claims must provide an answer. Ibn Taymiyya's answer is that it is impossible for a definitive rational proof to arise that contradicts a definitive scriptural proof. This implies that whenever a scriptural text is definitive in its transmission and meaning, no rational proof can truly oppose it. To illustrate, Ibn Taymiyya poses a rhetorical question: how can it be allowed to claim that in the Quran and authentic Sunnah there is something that any person can rationally know to be false? He then describes the misguided approach of those who, when confused about prophetic reports concerning the unseen, give precedence to their own opinion over the text, without seeking guidance from God's revelation. He concludes that the confirmed texts are never opposed by any clear rational proof; only confused and ambiguous notions, which are not known to be true, oppose them. These opposing notions are sophistical (sufistā'iyya), not genuine rational demonstrations. Thus, the apparent conflict is resolved through proper investigation and clarification.

Key Terms
عقلي قطعي
سمعي قطعي
شبه سوفسطائية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya as presented in this passage, what is the consequence of prioritizing reason over revelation?
A) It leads to a deeper understanding of the texts.
B) It necessitates accusing the Prophet of falsehood, which is clear disbelief.
C) It is permissible as long as the reason is sound.
D) It results in a synthesis of reason and revelation.

Key Takeaway
For Ibn Taymiyya, definitive revelation and definitive reason are two sources of truth that cannot genuinely oppose each other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a supposed conflict: a rational argument claims the world is eternal, but the Quran says the heavens and earth were created. Using Ibn Taymiyya's principle, explain why this cannot be a genuine contradiction.
?
Identify whether the rational argument in question qualifies as 'definitive' (قطعي عقلي) or merely speculative. What criteria would you use?

Identifying Sophistical Doubts vs. Definitive Reasoning
Author presents Ibn Taymiyya's argument that definitive revelation cannot be contradicted by definitive reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between genuine rational demonstrations and sophistical doubts when assessing supposed contradictions with revelation.

Core Idea
What appears to be a rational contradiction to revelation is actually a sophistical doubt based on ambiguous premises.

Ibn Taymiyya goes a step further: not only is contradiction impossible, but any supposed rational proof against revelation is intrinsically flawed – it is a sophistical doubt (شبه سوفسطائية), not a genuine demonstration. Let's learn how to recognize such fallacious reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about opposition
Find where Ibn Taymiyya says that the texts are never opposed by any clear rational proof.
Look for 'النصوص الثابتة في الكتاب والسنة لا يعارضها معقول بين قط'.
2
Understand the nature of opposition
He says the only things that oppose the texts are 'شبه وخيالات' (doubts and fantasies). What are these based on?
They are based on ambiguous meanings (معان متشابهة) and vague expressions (ألفاظ مجملة).
3
Distinguish between two types
Contrast genuine rational demonstrations (براهين عقلية) with sophistical doubts (شبه سوفسطائية).
Genuine proofs are clear and based on sound premises; sophistical doubts are fallacious and ambiguous.
4
Apply the test
When you encounter a claim that reason contradicts revelation, ask: Is the rational argument truly definitive? Is the scriptural text definitive in transmission and meaning? If both are definitive, the contradiction is illusory.
This is the practical test derived from Ibn Taymiyya's framework.

Ibn Rushd’s Principle of Non-Contradiction between Truths
Author presents Ibn Rushd's harmony argument and ta'wil principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Rushd's principle that demonstrative truth and scriptural truth cannot conflict, and identify when allegorical interpretation (ta'wil) is required.

Core Idea
Truth does not contradict truth; apparent conflict is resolved by allegorical interpretation.

Ibn Rushd (Averroes) wrote 'Fasl al-Maqal' to defend the pursuit of philosophy within Islam. He argues that since the Sharia itself calls for reflection (nazar), and demonstrative reasoning yields truth, there can be no real contradiction between reason and revelation. When an apparent contradiction arises, the scriptural text must be interpreted allegorically according to established linguistic rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim
Find the sentence where Ibn Rushd states that demonstrative reasoning does not lead to contradicting the Sharia. Understand that he asserts a fundamental harmony.
The phrase 'al-ḥaqq lā yuḍādu al-ḥaqq' (truth does not contradict truth) is the core.
2
Understand the diversity of assent
Notice Ibn Rushd's classification of people: those who assent by demonstration, dialectic, or rhetoric. This shows that different people need different methods, but all lead to truth.
This is a key epistemic move: logical methods vary, but truth is one.
3
Locate the principle of allegorical interpretation (ta'wil)
Find the passage where Ibn Rushd says that if a scriptural text's apparent meaning contradicts a demonstrative proof, it must be interpreted allegorically according to 'qānūn al-ta’wīl'.
This principle is analogized from usul al-fiqh, where jurists use ta'wil for legal rulings.
4
Connect to the certainty of demonstration
Ibn Rushd contrasts the jurist's probabilistic reasoning with the demonstrative thinker's certain reasoning. The philosopher has even more justification to apply ta'wil because his reasoning is certain.
This shows that far from subordinating revelation to reason, Ibn Rushd sees reason as a tool to properly understand revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسير على هذا المنوال حتى أساطين الفلسفة الإسلامية الذين اتهموا ظلماً أو عن غير تحقيق بتقديمهم عقولهم على الوحي بالإطلاق. وذلك ما دفع بابن رشد الحفيد - رحمه الله - لأن يكتب فصل المقال فيما بين الحكمة والشريعة من الاتصال. فتراه - بعد أن يورد حججه على أن الاشتغال بالفلسفة مشروع من غير حرج يقول: وإذا تقرر هذا كله وكنا نعتقد – معشر المسلمين – أن شريعتنا هذه الإلهية حق وأنها التي نبهت على هذه السعادة، ودعت إليها، التي هي المعرفة بالله عز وجل و مخلوقاته وأن ذلك متقرر عند كل مسلم من الطريق الذي اقتضته جبلته وطبيعته من التصديق، وذلك أن طباع الناس متفاضلة في التصديق، فمنهم من يصدق بالبرهان ومنهم من يصدق بالأقاويل الجدلية تصديق صاحب البرهان بالبرهان، إذ ليس في طباعه أكثر من ذلك، ومنهم من يصدق بالأقاويل الخطابية كتصديق صاحب البرهان بالأقاويل البرهانية. وقال: وإذا كانت هذه الشريعة داعية إلى النظر المؤدي إلى معرفة الحق، فإنا معشر المسلمين نعلم على القطع أنه لا يؤدي النظر البرهاني إلى مخالفة ما ورد به الشرع، فإن الحق لا يضاد الحق، بل يوافقه ويشهد له. ويؤكد على عدم التعارض بين الحكمة (الفلسفة أو العقل) والشريعة (الوحي) عند حديثه عن قانون التأويل، فيقول: وإذا كان الفقيه يفعل هذا في كثير من الأحكام الشرعية (يقصد إعمال قانون التأويل) فكم بالحري أن يفعل ذلك صاحب علم البرهان فإن الحقيقة إنما عنده قياس ظني، والعارف عنده قياس يقيني. ونحن نقطع قطعاً أن كل ما أدى إليه البرهان وخالفه ظاهر الشرع، أن ذلك الظاهر يقبل التأويل على قانون التأويل العربي. وهذه القضية لا يشك فيها مسلم ولا يرتاب بها مؤمن. وما أعظم اليقين بها عند من زاول هذا المعنى وجربه وقصد هذا المقصد من الجمع بين المعقول والمنقول. بل نقول إنه ما من منطوق به في الشرع مخالف بظاهره لما أدى إليه البرهان إلا إذا اعتبر الشرع وتصفحت
And it proceeds in this manner even to the pillars of Islamic philosophy who were unjustly accused, or without verification, of giving precedence to their intellects over revelation absolutely. This is what drove Ibn Rushd the grandson - may God have mercy on him - to write the Decisive Treatise on the connection between wisdom and the Sharia. So you see him - after presenting his arguments that engagement with philosophy is permissible without difficulty - saying: Once all this is established, and we - the Muslim community - believe that our divine Sharia is true and that it calls attention to this happiness and invites to it, which is knowledge of God Almighty and His creatures, and that this is established for every Muslim by the way required by his innate disposition and nature of assent, for the natures of people vary in assent: among them are those who assent by demonstration, among them are those who assent by dialectical arguments like the assent of the one who possesses demonstration to demonstration, for their nature does not go beyond that, and among them are those who assent by rhetorical arguments like the assent of the one who possesses demonstration to demonstrative arguments. And he said: Since this Sharia invites to reflection that leads to knowledge of truth, we Muslims know with certainty that demonstrative reflection does not lead to contradicting what the Sharia has brought, for truth does not contradict truth, rather it agrees with it and bears witness to it. And he emphasizes the non-contradiction between wisdom (philosophy or reason) and Sharia (revelation) when discussing the law of allegorical interpretation, saying: If the jurist does this in many legal rulings (meaning applying the law of allegorical interpretation), how much more should the one who possesses the science of demonstration do it? For the truth is with him only by probabilistic reasoning, while the gnostic has certain reasoning. And we state with certainty that whatever demonstration leads to and the apparent meaning of the Sharia contradicts it, that apparent meaning is open to allegorical interpretation according to the Arabic law of interpretation. This proposition no Muslim doubts nor any believer is skeptical about. And how great is certainty regarding it for those who have practiced this meaning and experienced it and aimed at this goal of reconciling the rational and the transmitted. Rather we say: There is no utterance in the Sharia whose apparent meaning contradicts what demonstration leads to, unless one considers the Sharia and examines
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents the author's summary of Ibn Rushd's position on the harmony between philosophy (reason) and revelation (Sharia). The author begins by noting that even the great figures of Islamic philosophy, who were sometimes accused of prioritizing reason over revelation, actually held a balanced view. Ibn Rushd wrote his 'Fasl al-Maqal' to argue that philosophy is not only permissible but encouraged by the Sharia. Ibn Rushd is then quoted: He states that people differ in their capacity for assent—some need demonstration, others dialectic or rhetoric—yet all are called to know God. Since the Sharia itself invites to reflection ('nazar'), and demonstrative reflection leads to truth, it cannot contradict scriptural truth, because 'truth does not contradict truth; rather it agrees with it and bears witness to it.' Ibn Rushd further argues that if jurists routinely apply allegorical interpretation (ta'wil) in legal matters to reconcile apparent contradictions, then philosophers—who deal with certain knowledge—are even more justified in applying ta'wil when the apparent meaning of scripture seems to conflict with a demonstrative proof. He asserts that any scriptural text that appears to contradict a demonstrative proof is open to allegorical interpretation according to the established rules of Arabic hermeneutics. The author ends by emphasizing that this principle is certain for those who have experience in reconciling reason and revelation.

Key Terms
البرهان
التأويل
القياس الظني / اليقيني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Rushd as presented, what should happen when the apparent meaning of a scriptural text contradicts a demonstrative proof?
A) The scriptural text should be rejected.
B) The demonstrative proof must be abandoned.
C) The scriptural text should be interpreted allegorically (ta'wil).
D) The contradiction is accepted as a mystery.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Rushd's principle: truth cannot contradict truth; apparent conflicts between demonstration and scripture are resolved through allegorical interpretation (ta'wil) following established linguistic rules.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Identify a scriptural verse that appears to conflict with a rational truth (e.g., 'God settles on the Throne' and God's immateriality). Explain how ta'wil resolves the apparent contradiction according to the Arabic law of interpretation.
?
Task 2: Construct a brief argument showing that a demonstrative proof (e.g., 'the world is temporally originated and requires a creator') and a scriptural text (e.g., 'Allah is the Creator of everything') are not contradictory, using Ibn Rushd's principle.

The Principle of Non-Contradiction
Author discusses non-contradiction of reason and revelation, cites al-Shatibi, then clarifies Ibn Rushd and Ibn Taymiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply al-Shatibi's principle that legal evidences do not contradict the intellect to identify when an apparent conflict between a rational argument and a revealed text must be reconciled through interpretation.

Core Idea
Revelation and reason, when both certain, cannot genuinely contradict.

This lesson introduces the foundational principle of non-contradiction between reason and revelation, as articulated by al-Shatibi. Understanding this principle is essential for distinguishing genuine conflicts from apparent ones, and for knowing when to seek reconciliation through interpretation (ta'wil) rather than rejecting one source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent conflict
State clearly the rational claim and the revealed text that seem to contradict each other.
For example, a rational proof for eternal causation vs. Qur'anic creation.
2
Assess the certainty of each source
Determine whether each claim is qat'i (definitive) or dhanmi (probable) in its own domain.
A qat'i rational proof must be based on decisive premises; a qat'i text must be clear and authentic.
3
Apply al-Shatibi's principle
If both are qat'i, there can be no contradiction; if one is dhanmi, the qat'i takes precedence and the dhanmi must be interpreted accordingly.
Al-Shatibi's statement 'al-adilla al-shar‘iyya la tunafi al-'uqul' encapsulates this.
4
Seek reconciliation (ta'wil) if needed
If the text is dhanmi and the rational proof is qat'i, employ ta'wil to harmonize the text with reason.
Ta'wil must follow established rules, not caprice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
سائر أجزائه وجد في ألفاظ الشرع ما يشهد بظاهره لذلك التأويل، أو يقارب أن يشهد (1).
ولخص أمر عدم التعارض هذا الشاطبي (ت: 790)(هـ) بعبارة موجزة فقال: الأدلة الشرعية لا تنافي العقول (3).
(3)
ويرى أحد الباحثين في هذا الإطار أن غاية ما يستدل به علماء الكلام لا يخرج - عند التحقيق عن كون القرآن الكريم أقر للعقل بنظرته كمنـزع مشروع في الاجتهاد، بل إنه يشجع على ذلك، بيد أن القرآن الكريم لا يقر دعوی استقلال العقل عن مصدر المعرفة الإلهية وهو الو - وأخال جميع العبارات المتقدمة لأبرز رموز المدارس الفكرية الإسلامية لا تخرج عن هذا المعنى الأخير إلا ما قد يتبادر لأول مرة من الإلباس في قول ابن رشد: ونحن نقطع قطعاً أن كلّ ما أدى إليه البرهان أن ذلك الظاهر يقبل التأويل على قانون التأويل (العربي) فلربما يشعر هذا بأن ابن رشد يقدم العقل على السمع، وذلك - في حقيقة الأمر - مقيد بحالة الظن الظاهري ليس أكثر. وابن تيمية لم ينازع في هذا، وإنما رفض بشدة تقديم القطعي لكونه عقلياً لا لكونه قطعياً، واعتبار العقل أصل السمع.
ومن هنا فإذا اتفق على أن العقلي قطعي فيقدم العقلي القطعي، وكذلك يقال في النقل لقطعيته. ومن جهة أخرى فإن ابن رشد ما زاد على أن أعمل قانون التأويل الذي يهدف إلى الجمع والتوفيق بين النقل والعقل لا أنـه يـردّ النصوص ولا يعترف بصحتها أو نسبتها إلى الشارع بدافع العجز أو الهـوى والتشهي كما يسارع بعض المتعجلين ممن لم ترسخ أقدامهم في معرفة الشريعة إن سلمنا برسوخها في معرفة الحكمة - إلى الرجم بذلك.
-
ولأن الإنسان عدو ما جهل، فإن أقرب شيء يريح العاجز الكسول هو أن يسارع إلى إعلان أحكام الرفض والإنكار، دون أن يكلف نفسه عناء البحث والنقاش وفق الأصول المعتبرة، والقواعد والأسس المرعية عند الراسخين في الشريعة والحكمة على حد سواء.
وعلى هذا الأساس فإن ثمة دوراً للعقل في الوحي، وآخر للوحي في العقل،
ولنبدأ بالأول:
أولاً- دور العقل في الوحي
يقصد بدور العقل في الوحي دور المعرفة العقلية أو المعرفة الفلسفية - كما يحلو لبعض الباحثين أن يرادف بينهما (1) في فهم الدين، فتكون معرفة العقل عبارة عن كسبه الذاتي في المعارف والعلوم المتعلقة بميادين الآفاق والأنفس، ليتحدد دوره في فهم الهَدِي الديني وطبيعة دوره. وسبيل ذلك:
أ. تعيين المدلول النصي.
ب. تقدير المقاصد (2).
وبتعبير أكثر تفصيلاً نقول: إنه بناء على طبيعة دور العقل في فهم الدين، وعلى الأسس التي يقوم عليها ذلك الفهم ينهض العقل بالاجتهاد، بغية تحديد المراد الإلهي من خلال النص، عندما يصاغ بأحكام تتعلق بأفعال الإنسان فيما ينبغي أن تكون عليه.
ويختلف عمل العقل في تفهم النص باختلاف النص ذاته، من حيث وروده، ومن حيث دلالته أي من حيث القطعية والظنية. ولذلك فكلما علت حظوظ القطع سهل دور العقل، وكلما ضعفت عظم ذلك الدور، وحقت به المصاعب.
Chapter Three: Section Three - Revelation. ... The rest of its parts found in the words of the Law what testifies by its apparent meaning to that interpretation, or nearly testifies (1). And al-Shatibi (d. 790 AH) summarized the matter of non-contradiction with a brief expression, saying: The legal evidences do not contradict the intellects (3). (3) And one researcher in this framework holds that the ultimate extent of what the theologians use as evidence does not go beyond — upon verification — that the Noble Qur'an affirmed for the intellect its view as a legitimate approach in ijtihad, rather it encourages that, however the Noble Qur'an does not affirm the claim of the independence of the intellect from the source of divine knowledge, which is Allah — and I think all the preceding statements of the most prominent symbols of Islamic intellectual schools do not depart from this latter meaning except what may initially appear of ambiguity in Ibn Rushd's statement: 'And we are absolutely certain that whatever the proof leads to, that apparent meaning is subject to interpretation according to the law of interpretation (Arabic).' Perhaps this suggests that Ibn Rushd gives precedence to reason over revelation, but this — in reality — is restricted to a case of apparent conjecture, nothing more. And Ibn Taymiyya did not dispute this, but rather strongly rejected giving precedence to the rational certainty because it is rational, not because it is certain, and considering reason as the root of revelation. Hence if it is agreed that the rational is certain, then the rational certain is given precedence, and likewise is said for the transmitted due to its certainty. On the other hand, Ibn Rushd did no more than employ the law of interpretation which aims to reconcile between transmission and reason, not that he rejects the texts nor acknowledges their validity or attribution to the Legislator due to incapacity or whim and caprice, as some hasty ones who have not established their feet in knowledge of the Sharia — even if we grant their establishment in knowledge of wisdom — hasten to charge. — Because man is an enemy of what he is ignorant of, the closest thing that comforts the lazy incapable person is to hasten to pronounce judgments of rejection and denial, without burdening himself with the trouble of research and discussion according to the recognized principles and the rules and foundations adhered to by those firmly rooted in Sharia and wisdom alike. On this basis, there is a role for reason in revelation, and another for revelation in reason. Let us begin with the first: Firstly - The role of reason in revelation. By the role of reason in revelation is meant the role of rational knowledge or philosophical knowledge — as some researchers like to equate them (1) — in understanding religion. Thus rational knowledge is the mind's own acquisition in the fields of knowledge and sciences related to the horizons and the souls, so that its role in understanding religious guidance and the nature of that role is determined. The means of that are: A. Determining the textual meaning. B. Assessing the objectives (2). In more detailed expression we say: Based on the nature of the role of reason in understanding religion, and on the foundations upon which that understanding is built, reason undertakes ijtihad, aiming to determine the divine intent through the text, when it is formulated with rulings concerning human actions as they ought to be. And the work of reason in understanding the text varies according to the text itself, in terms of its transmission and its signification, i.e., in terms of certainty and probability. Therefore, the higher the chances of certainty, the easier the role of reason, and the weaker they are, the greater that role and the more difficulties it is beset with.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the relationship between reason and revelation in Islamic thought. The author begins by stating that the legal texts contain expressions whose apparent meaning supports a particular interpretation. He then references al-Shatibi's concise formulation that legal evidences do not contradict the intellect. The author proceeds to analyze the position of prominent Islamic thinkers: he argues that the Qur'an affirms reason as a legitimate tool for ijtihad but does not grant it independence from divine revelation. He then addresses Ibn Rushd's statement about certainty in interpretation, clarifying that Ibn Rushd does not prioritize reason over revelation absolutely but only in cases of apparent conjecture. The author also explains Ibn Taymiyya's position: Ibn Taymiyya did not reject the use of reason but opposed giving preference to rational certainty simply because it is rational; rather, both rational and revealed certainty should be weighed equally. The passage then transitions to the role of reason in understanding revelation: reason is to determine textual meaning and assess the objectives (maqasid) of the Law. The author notes that the function of reason varies depending on whether the text is definitive (qat'i) or probable (dhanmi) in its transmission and signification. The easier the certainty, the simpler the role of reason; the more ambiguous, the greater the cognitive effort required.

Key Terms
العقل
الوحي
الأدلة الشرعية
التأويل
القطعي
الظني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Shatibi's formulation in the passage, what is the relationship between legal evidences ('adilla shar'iyya) and the intellects ('uqul)?
A) Legal evidences always confirm intellect.
B) Legal evidences do not contradict intellects.
C) Intellects are superior to legal evidences.
D) Legal evidences are independent of intellects.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shatibi's principle that legal evidences do not contradict the intellect forms the foundation for harmonizing reason and revelation in Islamic thought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the claim: 'The Qur'an states that Allah created the heavens and the earth in six days.' A rational argument suggests that the universe is eternal. Identify the certainty level of each (based on the passage's categories). Apply al-Shatibi's principle to determine whether this is a genuine contradiction and what the appropriate response should be.

The Hierarchy of Certainty: Qat'i and Dhanmi
Author discusses how the role of reason varies with the certainty of the text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given piece of evidence as qat'i or dhanmi based on its transmission and signification, and determine which takes precedence in case of conflict.

Core Idea
Certainty trumps probability, regardless of source.

This lesson introduces the critical distinction between definitive (qat'i) and probable (dhanmi) knowledge, both in rational arguments and revealed texts. Understanding this hierarchy allows you to resolve apparent conflicts by giving precedence to the more certain evidence, as taught by the scholars cited in our passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the evidence
Name the rational argument or revealed text under consideration.
Example: the rational argument for divine unity or a Qur'anic verse.
2
Evaluate transmission (thubut)
For a text, check if its chain is mutawatir (qat'i) or ahad (dhanmi).
For rational arguments, check if the premises are necessary or derived.
3
Evaluate signification (dalala)
Check if the meaning is clear (qat'i) or ambiguous (dhanmi).
A verse may be qat'i in transmission but dhanmi in meaning.
4
Apply precedence rule
If both are qat'i, no conflict; if one is qat'i, it overrides the dhanmi; if both dhanmi, scholars may reconcile or prefer based on strength.
As the passage says: the higher the certainty, the easier the role of reason.

Source Text

سائر أجزائه وجد في ألفاظ الشرع ما يشهد بظاهره لذلك التأويل، أو يقارب أن يشهد (1).

Ta'wil: The Method of Reconciliation
Author discusses Ibn Rushd's ta'wil method and clarifies its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules of ta'wil, as described in the passage, to harmonize a rational proof with a revealed text that appears to contradict it.

Core Idea
Ta'wil reconciles reason and revelation by interpreting the text's apparent meaning without rejecting it.

This lesson focuses on Ibn Rushd's method of ta'wil, which aims to achieve harmony between rational proof (burhan) and revealed texts. The passage clarifies that ta'wil is not a rejection of the text but a principled interpretation that follows rules, not whims. Understanding ta'wil is crucial for any scholar dealing with apparent conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rational proof
State the certain rational argument that seems to conflict with the text.
Ibn Rushd says: 'whatever the proof leads to.'
2
Identify the apparent meaning of the text
State the literal or apparent meaning (zahir) of the revealed text.
The passage says: 'that apparent meaning is subject to interpretation.'
3
Check the status of the text
Determine if the text's apparent meaning is qat'i or dhanmi. Ta'wil is only valid when the text is dhanmi.
The passage implies Ibn Rushd's case is restricted to apparent conjecture.
4
Apply ta'wil according to the law of interpretation
Find a valid interpretation that aligns the text with the rational proof, following the rules of Arabic language and legal theory.
Ta'wil must not violate the consensus or definitive texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولنبدأ بالأول:
أولاً- دور العقل في الوحي
يقصد بدور العقل في الوحي دور المعرفة العقلية أو المعرفة الفلسفية - كما يحلو لبعض الباحثين أن يرادف بينهما (1) في فهم الدين، فتكون معرفة العقل عبارة عن كسبه الذاتي في المعارف والعلوم المتعلقة بميادين الآفاق والأنفس، ليتحدد دوره في فهم الهَدِي الديني وطبيعة دوره. وسبيل ذلك:
أ. تعيين المدلول النصي.
ب. تقدير المقاصد (2).
وبتعبير أكثر تفصيلاً نقول: إنه بناء على طبيعة دور العقل في فهم الدين، وعلى الأسس التي يقوم عليها ذلك الفهم ينهض العقل بالاجتهاد، بغية تحديد المراد الإلهي من خلال النص، عندما يصاغ بأحكام تتعلق بأفعال الإنسان فيما ينبغي أن تكون عليه.
ويختلف عمل العقل في تفهم النص باختلاف النص ذاته، من حيث وروده، ومن حيث دلالته أي من حيث القطعية والظنية. ولذلك فكلما علت حظوظ القطع سهل دور العقل، وكلما ضعفت عظم ذلك الدور، وحقت به المصاعب.
Chapter Three: Section Three - Revelation. ... The rest of its parts found in the words of the Law what testifies by its apparent meaning to that interpretation, or nearly testifies (1). And al-Shatibi (d. 790 AH) summarized the matter of non-contradiction with a brief expression, saying: The legal evidences do not contradict the intellects (3). (3) And one researcher in this framework holds that the ultimate extent of what the theologians use as evidence does not go beyond — upon verification — that the Noble Qur'an affirmed for the intellect its view as a legitimate approach in ijtihad, rather it encourages that, however the Noble Qur'an does not affirm the claim of the independence of the intellect from the source of divine knowledge, which is Allah — and I think all the preceding statements of the most prominent symbols of Islamic intellectual schools do not depart from this latter meaning except what may initially appear of ambiguity in Ibn Rushd's statement: 'And we are absolutely certain that whatever the proof leads to, that apparent meaning is subject to interpretation according to the law of interpretation (Arabic).' Perhaps this suggests that Ibn Rushd gives precedence to reason over revelation, but this — in reality — is restricted to a case of apparent conjecture, nothing more. And Ibn Taymiyya did not dispute this, but rather strongly rejected giving precedence to the rational certainty because it is rational, not because it is certain, and considering reason as the root of revelation. Hence if it is agreed that the rational is certain, then the rational certain is given precedence, and likewise is said for the transmitted due to its certainty. On the other hand, Ibn Rushd did no more than employ the law of interpretation which aims to reconcile between transmission and reason, not that he rejects the texts nor acknowledges their validity or attribution to the Legislator due to incapacity or whim and caprice, as some hasty ones who have not established their feet in knowledge of the Sharia — even if we grant their establishment in knowledge of wisdom — hasten to charge. — Because man is an enemy of what he is ignorant of, the closest thing that comforts the lazy incapable person is to hasten to pronounce judgments of rejection and denial, without burdening himself with the trouble of research and discussion according to the recognized principles and the rules and foundations adhered to by those firmly rooted in Sharia and wisdom alike. On this basis, there is a role for reason in revelation, and another for revelation in reason. Let us begin with the first: Firstly - The role of reason in revelation. By the role of reason in revelation is meant the role of rational knowledge or philosophical knowledge — as some researchers like to equate them (1) — in understanding religion. Thus rational knowledge is the mind's own acquisition in the fields of knowledge and sciences related to the horizons and the souls, so that its role in understanding religious guidance and the nature of that role is determined. The means of that are: A. Determining the textual meaning. B. Assessing the objectives (2). In more detailed expression we say: Based on the nature of the role of reason in understanding religion, and on the foundations upon which that understanding is built, reason undertakes ijtihad, aiming to determine the divine intent through the text, when it is formulated with rulings concerning human actions as they ought to be. And the work of reason in understanding the text varies according to the text itself, in terms of its transmission and its signification, i.e., in terms of certainty and probability. Therefore, the higher the chances of certainty, the easier the role of reason, and the weaker they are, the greater that role and the more difficulties it is beset with.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the relationship between reason and revelation in Islamic thought. The author begins by stating that the legal texts contain expressions whose apparent meaning supports a particular interpretation. He then references al-Shatibi's concise formulation that legal evidences do not contradict the intellect. The author proceeds to analyze the position of prominent Islamic thinkers: he argues that the Qur'an affirms reason as a legitimate tool for ijtihad but does not grant it independence from divine revelation. He then addresses Ibn Rushd's statement about certainty in interpretation, clarifying that Ibn Rushd does not prioritize reason over revelation absolutely but only in cases of apparent conjecture. The author also explains Ibn Taymiyya's position: Ibn Taymiyya did not reject the use of reason but opposed giving preference to rational certainty simply because it is rational; rather, both rational and revealed certainty should be weighed equally. The passage then transitions to the role of reason in understanding revelation: reason is to determine textual meaning and assess the objectives (maqasid) of the Law. The author notes that the function of reason varies depending on whether the text is definitive (qat'i) or probable (dhanmi) in its transmission and signification. The easier the certainty, the simpler the role of reason; the more ambiguous, the greater the cognitive effort required.

Key Terms
التأويل
العقل
النقل
البرهان
الشريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Ibn Rushd's statement about ta'wil not entail?
A) That he rejects the texts.
B) That he gives precedence to reason in all cases.
C) That he follows the law of interpretation.
D) That he considers reason as the root.

Key Takeaway
Ta'wil is a legitimate and necessary tool for reconciling certain rational proofs with revealed texts when the latter are open to interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the rational proof that God is not a body. The Qur'an says: 'The Most Merciful is established upon the Throne' (istawa). Explain how ta'wil can be applied to reconcile these, stating the apparent meaning and the intended interpretation according to the rules of ta'wil.

intermediate
8 min
The Role of Reason in Understanding Revelation
Author outlines the role of reason in revelation and lists its two functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the two main functions of reason in understanding revelation: determining textual meaning (dalala) and assessing the objectives (maqasid) of the Law.

Core Idea
Reason serves revelation by clarifying what is certain and what is probable, and by uncovering the higher purposes of the Law.

This lesson explores the two fundamental roles of reason in interpreting revelation: first, to determine the meaning of the text (ta'yin al-madlul al-nassi), and second, to assess the objectives of the Law (taqdir al-maqasid). The passage explains that the degree of reason's involvement depends on the text's certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text's level of certainty
Determine whether the text is qat'i or dhanmi in transmission and signification.
The passage says: 'يختلف عمل العقل باختلاف النص ذاته'.
2
Apply reason to determine meaning
For texts with clear meaning, reason's role is minimal; for ambiguous texts, reason engages in ijtihad to clarify.
This is part of 'تعيين المدلول النصي'.
3
Apply reason to assess objectives
Beyond literal meaning, reason infers the purposes (maqasid) of the rulings, such as preserving religion, life, intellect, lineage, property.
This is 'تقدير المقاصد'.
4
Perform ijtihad accordingly
Based on the certainty and objectives, reason formulates new rulings or interprets existing ones.
Ijtihad is the effort of reasoning to determine the divine intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
سائر أجزائه وجد في ألفاظ الشرع ما يشهد بظاهره لذلك التأويل، أو يقارب أن يشهد (1).
ولخص أمر عدم التعارض هذا الشاطبي (ت: 790)(هـ) بعبارة موجزة فقال: الأدلة الشرعية لا تنافي العقول (3).
(3)
ويرى أحد الباحثين في هذا الإطار أن غاية ما يستدل به علماء الكلام لا يخرج - عند التحقيق عن كون القرآن الكريم أقر للعقل بنظرته كمنـزع مشروع في الاجتهاد، بل إنه يشجع على ذلك، بيد أن القرآن الكريم لا يقر دعوی استقلال العقل عن مصدر المعرفة الإلهية وهو الو - وأخال جميع العبارات المتقدمة لأبرز رموز المدارس الفكرية الإسلامية لا تخرج عن هذا المعنى الأخير إلا ما قد يتبادر لأول مرة من الإلباس في قول ابن رشد: ونحن نقطع قطعاً أن كلّ ما أدى إليه البرهان أن ذلك الظاهر يقبل التأويل على قانون التأويل (العربي) فلربما يشعر هذا بأن ابن رشد يقدم العقل على السمع، وذلك - في حقيقة الأمر - مقيد بحالة الظن الظاهري ليس أكثر. وابن تيمية لم ينازع في هذا، وإنما رفض بشدة تقديم القطعي لكونه عقلياً لا لكونه قطعياً، واعتبار العقل أصل السمع.
ومن هنا فإذا اتفق على أن العقلي قطعي فيقدم العقلي القطعي، وكذلك يقال في النقل لقطعيته. ومن جهة أخرى فإن ابن رشد ما زاد على أن أعمل قانون التأويل الذي يهدف إلى الجمع والتوفيق بين النقل والعقل لا أنـه يـردّ النصوص ولا يعترف بصحتها أو نسبتها إلى الشارع بدافع العجز أو الهـوى والتشهي كما يسارع بعض المتعجلين ممن لم ترسخ أقدامهم في معرفة الشريعة إن سلمنا برسوخها في معرفة الحكمة - إلى الرجم بذلك.
-
ولأن الإنسان عدو ما جهل، فإن أقرب شيء يريح العاجز الكسول هو أن يسارع إلى إعلان أحكام الرفض والإنكار، دون أن يكلف نفسه عناء البحث والنقاش وفق الأصول المعتبرة، والقواعد والأسس المرعية عند الراسخين في الشريعة والحكمة على حد سواء.
وعلى هذا الأساس فإن ثمة دوراً للعقل في الوحي، وآخر للوحي في العقل،

The Integration of Reason and Revelation
Author explains the integration of reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the complementary relationship between reason and revelation as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation are partners, not rivals.

This lesson introduces the central thesis of the passage: reason and revelation work together in harmony. The author argues that there is no contradiction between rational and transmitted sciences. Understanding this integration is essential for a correct approach to Islamic knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main claim
Read the first part of the passage where the author states that the role of reason is realized from the standpoint of integration between reason and revelation. Note the claim that there is no contradiction.
Focus on the sentence: 'وَبِاخْتِصَارٍ فَإِنَّ مَظَاهِرَ أَدْوَارِ الْعَقْلِ فِي الْوَحْيِ تَتَجَلَّى... لَا تَعَارُضَ بَيْنَ عُلُومِ النَّقْلِ وَعُلُومِ الْعَقْلِ'.
2
Locate evidence for integration
Find where the author describes reason as 'free in movement but bound by revelation' and revelation as a 'safety valve'. This shows the mutual dependence.
3
Summarize the two categories of reason's efforts
The passage divides reason's work into definitive texts (قطعي وروداً ودلالة) and probable texts (ظني وروداً ودلالة). This shows reason's role in interpretation.
This categorization is foundational for usul al-fiqh.
4
Explain revelation's role as a safeguard
The author says revelation restrains reason from extremism and warns at danger points. This clarifies why revelation is necessary for sound reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
وبصيغة أكثر تحديداً يمكن تلخيص اجتهاد العقل في فهم الدين من خلال:
أ. اجتهاد العقل في النص القطعي وروداً ودلالة.
ب. اجتهاد العقل في النص الظني وروداً ودلالة.
إن هذا الدور للمعرفة العقلية إنما يتحقق من منطلق التكامل القائم بين العقل والوحي، وفي ضوء ذلك يقوم العقل بما يلي:
١ - تصديق الوحي: أي إن القرآن الكريم إنما حث العقل على التفكر والتدبر والتأمل..إلخ. لأنه يثق بقدرة العقل الصحيح على تمييز الوحي الصادق عن الادعاء الزائف للوحي. ومن جانب آخر فإنه لما كان الوحي مسؤولية والتزاماً بالواجبات وانتهاء عن المحرمات فإن تصديق العقل للوحي ضروري ليقوم بمهمته التزاماً وانتهاء، إذ هو مناط التكليف.
۲- فقه الشرائع أي إن معرفة أصول الأحكام وتشريعها عملية عقلية تتم من خلال إعمال العقل في النصوص، إذ نجد في القرآن الكريم كلمات من مثل من أجل ذلك أو (كذلك) أو (( لكي لا ، لتدل على ضرورة فقه الشرائع ومقاصدها، ولا يتم ذلك إلا عن طريق العقل.
٣- العقل والمناهج التطبيقية ونقصد بذلك جوانب الثبات والتطور في الشريعة الإسلامية. فعنصر الثبات هو تأسيس أصل المبدأ أما عنصر التطور فقابل لتطبيق المبدأ وفق شروط التطبيق المتغير من حين لآخر. ومن هنا جاء النص به كمبدأ يلتزم ولكن لم يرد النص بتفصيلاته، ليقوم العقل باختيار الصيغة الأنسب من زمان لآخر ومن بيئة اجتماعية إلى بيئة أخرى.
وباختصار فإن مظاهر أدوار العقل في الوحي تتجلى من خلال وظيفتين هامتين هما:
الأولى: إرشادنا إلى الوحي والتصديق بالنبوة.
الثانية: القيام بإدراك الموحى به وتفهمه.
وهذا كفيل ببيان أن لا تعارض بين علوم النقل وعلوم العقل
وهنا نلاحظ أن العقل بالنسبة إلى التربية الإسلامية طليق في حركته منضبط بالوحي، فيكبح جماحه عن الشطط أو الذهاب بعيداً خارج دائرة حركته فالوحي للعقل بمثابة صمام أمان يصونه عن الانزلاق فيما لا يعنيه، وينذره بنقطة الخطر. إذا ما تجاوز حدود المناطق الآمنة.
ثانياً - دور الوحي في العقل
ويمكن تلخيص دور الوحي في العقل بالأدوار التالية:
1 - إيقاظ العقل: وهذا يتضح من خلال الآيات التي جاءت تحث العقل على القيام بعملياته العليا وهي كثيرة جداً (سبق إيراد جانب كبير منها عند الحديث عن العقل).
٢- تزكية العقل: حيث إن الإنسان مكون من عقل وجهل وشهوات تفد إليه من بيئته الخارجية فلا بد أن يقوم مصدر معصوم بعمل تقويم وتزكية لهذا العقل غير المعصوم نتيجة اختلاطه بهذه المؤثرات البيئية. ومثال ذلك قول الله سبحانه: ﴿وَلا تَتَّبِعِ الْهَوَى فَيُضِلَّكَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ.. ﴾ [ص: ٢٦/٣٨].
- تنمية العقل وتتم هذه التنمية العقلية من خلال النظر في منظومة الإسلام المتكاملة تشريعات وأحكاماً وأخلاقاً وقيماً ومبادئ عملية تعمل على تنمية وإنهاض العقل باتجاه اكتشاف السنن وتسخير الطبيعة وإعمار الحياة
Chapter Three, Section Three: Revelation
In more specific terms, the effort of reason in understanding religion can be summarized through:
a. The effort of reason regarding definitive texts in transmission and meaning.
b. The effort of reason regarding probable texts in transmission and meaning.
This role of rational knowledge is realized from the standpoint of the integration between reason and revelation. In light of that, reason undertakes the following:
1. Confirming revelation: That the Noble Qur'an urged reason to think, ponder, reflect... etc., because it trusts the ability of sound reason to distinguish true revelation from false claims of revelation. On the other hand, since revelation is responsibility and commitment to duties and abstention from prohibitions, the confirmation of revelation by reason is necessary for it to fulfill its role of commitment and abstention, as it is the basis of obligation.
2. Understanding the laws: That knowledge of the principles of rulings and their legislation is a rational process carried out through engaging reason in texts. We find in the Noble Qur'an words like 'because of that' or 'thus' or 'so that not', indicating the necessity of understanding the laws and their objectives, and that is only achieved through reason.
3. Reason and applied methodologies: By this we mean aspects of stability and development in Islamic law. The element of stability is establishing the principle's origin, while the element of development is open to applying the principle according to changing application conditions from time to time. Hence the text came as a principle to be adhered to, but the text did not provide its details, so that reason may choose the most suitable form from time to time and from one social environment to another.
In summary, the manifestations of the roles of reason in revelation appear through two important functions:
First: Guiding us to revelation and confirming prophethood.
Second: Undertaking to comprehend the revealed content and understand it.
This suffices to show that there is no contradiction between transmitted sciences and rational sciences.
Here we note that reason, in relation to Islamic education, is free in its movement but bound by revelation, which restrains it from extremism or going far outside its sphere of movement. Revelation is for reason like a safety valve that protects it from slipping into what does not concern it and warns it at the point of danger if it exceeds the boundaries of safe zones.
Second: The role of revelation in reason
The role of revelation in reason can be summarized in the following roles:
1. Awakening reason: This is clear from the verses that urge reason to undertake its higher operations, which are very many (a large part of them was previously mentioned when discussing reason).
2. Purification of reason: Since man is composed of reason, ignorance, and desires that come to him from his external environment, there must be an infallible source to correct and purify this non-infallible reason as a result of its mixing with these environmental influences. An example of that is the saying of God Almighty: 'And do not follow desire, lest it lead you astray from the path of God...' [Sad 38:26].
3. Development of reason: This rational development takes place through contemplation of the integrated system of Islam, its legislations, rulings, ethics, values, and practical principles that work to develop and uplift reason towards discovering natural laws, harnessing nature, and building civilization.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage explains the mutual relationship between reason and revelation in Islamic thought, arguing for their integration rather than contradiction. The author first summarizes the efforts of reason in understanding religion, distinguishing between definitive and probable texts. Then he enumerates three roles of reason in relation to revelation: first, confirming revelation by recognizing its truth through intellectual reflection; second, understanding the laws by deriving principles and objectives from texts; third, applying principles flexibly across time and context, with reason choosing appropriate forms. The author summarizes these as guiding to revelation and comprehending revelation. Then he shifts to the role of revelation in relation to reason: awakening reason through divine exhortation, purifying reason from the influence of desires and environment, and developing reason by studying the comprehensive Islamic system. The passage emphasizes that reason is free but bound by revelation, which acts as a safeguard. This is an epistemological discussion about the sources of knowledge and their harmony.

Key Terms
العقل
الوحي

According to the passage, what is the relationship between reason and revelation?
A) They are in constant conflict
B) Reason is independent and revelation is secondary
C) They are integrated and complementary
D) Revelation replaces reason completely

Key Takeaway
Reason and revelation are integrated: reason confirms and applies revelation, while revelation guides and safeguards reason.

Reason's Three Roles in Relation to Revelation
Author lists and explains the three roles of reason in relation to revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and describe the three roles of reason in relation to revelation as outlined in the passage.

Core Idea
Reason confirms, understands, and applies revelation.

The passage details three specific functions of reason in engaging with revelation: confirming its truth, understanding its laws, and applying its principles flexibly. These roles show how reason is an active partner in the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three roles
Look for the numbered list (١-٣) in the Arabic after 'يقوم العقل بما يلي'. The three roles are: 1) تصديق الوحي, 2) فقه الشرائع, 3) العقل والمناهج التطبيقية.
These correspond to tasdiq, fiqh, and applied methodologies.
2
Examine the first role: confirming revelation
Read the explanation under role 1. The author says the Qur'an encourages reflection because it trusts reason to distinguish true revelation from false claims. Also, confirmation is necessary for responsibility.
Tasdiq al-wahy is a rational act that establishes the authenticity of prophecy.
3
Examine the second role: understanding the laws
Under role 2, the author mentions rational engagement with texts to derive principles and objectives (فقه الشرائع ومقاصدها). Examples from the Qur'an (من أجل ذلك, لكي لا) show that reason is needed to understand the purposes behind rulings.
This role is central to usul al-fiqh and maqasid al-shari'ah.
4
Examine the third role: applied methodologies
Role 3 discusses stability (ثبات) and development (تطور). The text provides the principle, but reason chooses the appropriate form over time and social context. This shows reason's flexibility.
This allows Islamic law to adapt while preserving core principles.
5
Summarize the two overarching functions
The author later summarizes the roles into two functions: guiding to revelation/confirming prophethood, and comprehending the revealed content. These functions encapsulate all three roles.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
وبصيغة أكثر تحديداً يمكن تلخيص اجتهاد العقل في فهم الدين من خلال:
أ. اجتهاد العقل في النص القطعي وروداً ودلالة.
ب. اجتهاد العقل في النص الظني وروداً ودلالة.
إن هذا الدور للمعرفة العقلية إنما يتحقق من منطلق التكامل القائم بين العقل والوحي، وفي ضوء ذلك يقوم العقل بما يلي:
١ - تصديق الوحي: أي إن القرآن الكريم إنما حث العقل على التفكر والتدبر والتأمل..إلخ. لأنه يثق بقدرة العقل الصحيح على تمييز الوحي الصادق عن الادعاء الزائف للوحي. ومن جانب آخر فإنه لما كان الوحي مسؤولية والتزاماً بالواجبات وانتهاء عن المحرمات فإن تصديق العقل للوحي ضروري ليقوم بمهمته التزاماً وانتهاء، إذ هو مناط التكليف.
۲- فقه الشرائع أي إن معرفة أصول الأحكام وتشريعها عملية عقلية تتم من خلال إعمال العقل في النصوص، إذ نجد في القرآن الكريم كلمات من مثل من أجل ذلك أو (كذلك) أو (( لكي لا ، لتدل على ضرورة فقه الشرائع ومقاصدها، ولا يتم ذلك إلا عن طريق العقل.
٣- العقل والمناهج التطبيقية ونقصد بذلك جوانب الثبات والتطور في الشريعة الإسلامية. فعنصر الثبات هو تأسيس أصل المبدأ أما عنصر التطور فقابل لتطبيق المبدأ وفق شروط التطبيق المتغير من حين لآخر. ومن هنا جاء النص به كمبدأ يلتزم ولكن لم يرد النص بتفصيلاته، ليقوم العقل باختيار الصيغة الأنسب من زمان لآخر ومن بيئة اجتماعية إلى بيئة أخرى.
وباختصار فإن مظاهر أدوار العقل في الوحي تتجلى من خلال وظيفتين هامتين هما:
الأولى: إرشادنا إلى الوحي والتصديق بالنبوة.
الثانية: القيام بإدراك الموحى به وتفهمه.
وهذا كفيل ببيان أن لا تعارض بين علوم النقل وعلوم العقل
وهنا نلاحظ أن العقل بالنسبة إلى التربية الإسلامية طليق في حركته منضبط بالوحي، فيكبح جماحه عن الشطط أو الذهاب بعيداً خارج دائرة حركته فالوحي للعقل بمثابة صمام أمان يصونه عن الانزلاق فيما لا يعنيه، وينذره بنقطة الخطر. إذا ما تجاوز حدود المناطق الآمنة.
ثانياً - دور الوحي في العقل
ويمكن تلخيص دور الوحي في العقل بالأدوار التالية:
1 - إيقاظ العقل: وهذا يتضح من خلال الآيات التي جاءت تحث العقل على القيام بعملياته العليا وهي كثيرة جداً (سبق إيراد جانب كبير منها عند الحديث عن العقل).
٢- تزكية العقل: حيث إن الإنسان مكون من عقل وجهل وشهوات تفد إليه من بيئته الخارجية فلا بد أن يقوم مصدر معصوم بعمل تقويم وتزكية لهذا العقل غير المعصوم نتيجة اختلاطه بهذه المؤثرات البيئية. ومثال ذلك قول الله سبحانه: ﴿وَلا تَتَّبِعِ الْهَوَى فَيُضِلَّكَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ.. ﴾ [ص: ٢٦/٣٨].
- تنمية العقل وتتم هذه التنمية العقلية من خلال النظر في منظومة الإسلام المتكاملة تشريعات وأحكاماً وأخلاقاً وقيماً ومبادئ عملية تعمل على تنمية وإنهاض العقل باتجاه اكتشاف السنن وتسخير الطبيعة وإعمار الحياة
Chapter Three, Section Three: Revelation
In more specific terms, the effort of reason in understanding religion can be summarized through:
a. The effort of reason regarding definitive texts in transmission and meaning.
b. The effort of reason regarding probable texts in transmission and meaning.
This role of rational knowledge is realized from the standpoint of the integration between reason and revelation. In light of that, reason undertakes the following:
1. Confirming revelation: That the Noble Qur'an urged reason to think, ponder, reflect... etc., because it trusts the ability of sound reason to distinguish true revelation from false claims of revelation. On the other hand, since revelation is responsibility and commitment to duties and abstention from prohibitions, the confirmation of revelation by reason is necessary for it to fulfill its role of commitment and abstention, as it is the basis of obligation.
2. Understanding the laws: That knowledge of the principles of rulings and their legislation is a rational process carried out through engaging reason in texts. We find in the Noble Qur'an words like 'because of that' or 'thus' or 'so that not', indicating the necessity of understanding the laws and their objectives, and that is only achieved through reason.
3. Reason and applied methodologies: By this we mean aspects of stability and development in Islamic law. The element of stability is establishing the principle's origin, while the element of development is open to applying the principle according to changing application conditions from time to time. Hence the text came as a principle to be adhered to, but the text did not provide its details, so that reason may choose the most suitable form from time to time and from one social environment to another.
In summary, the manifestations of the roles of reason in revelation appear through two important functions:
First: Guiding us to revelation and confirming prophethood.
Second: Undertaking to comprehend the revealed content and understand it.
This suffices to show that there is no contradiction between transmitted sciences and rational sciences.
Here we note that reason, in relation to Islamic education, is free in its movement but bound by revelation, which restrains it from extremism or going far outside its sphere of movement. Revelation is for reason like a safety valve that protects it from slipping into what does not concern it and warns it at the point of danger if it exceeds the boundaries of safe zones.
Second: The role of revelation in reason
The role of revelation in reason can be summarized in the following roles:
1. Awakening reason: This is clear from the verses that urge reason to undertake its higher operations, which are very many (a large part of them was previously mentioned when discussing reason).
2. Purification of reason: Since man is composed of reason, ignorance, and desires that come to him from his external environment, there must be an infallible source to correct and purify this non-infallible reason as a result of its mixing with these environmental influences. An example of that is the saying of God Almighty: 'And do not follow desire, lest it lead you astray from the path of God...' [Sad 38:26].
3. Development of reason: This rational development takes place through contemplation of the integrated system of Islam, its legislations, rulings, ethics, values, and practical principles that work to develop and uplift reason towards discovering natural laws, harnessing nature, and building civilization.

This passage explains the mutual relationship between reason and revelation in Islamic thought, arguing for their integration rather than contradiction. The author first summarizes the efforts of reason in understanding religion, distinguishing between definitive and probable texts. Revelation's Three Roles in Relation to Reason
Author lists and explains the three roles of revelation in relation to reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and describe the three roles of revelation in relation to reason as outlined in the passage.

Core Idea
Revelation awakens, purifies, and develops reason.

Just as reason serves revelation, revelation also serves reason by awakening it from neglect, purifying it from corrupting influences, and developing it through the comprehensive Islamic system. This lesson explores the three functions of revelation vis-à-vis reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three roles of revelation
After the heading 'دور الوحي في العقل', the author lists three roles: 1) إيقاظ العقل, 2) تزكية العقل, 3) تنمية العقل. Translate these as awakening, purification, and development.
These are presented with supporting evidence.
2
Examine the first role: awakening reason
The author mentions many verses that urge reason to undertake higher operations. This shows that revelation stimulates rational activity. The Qur'an repeatedly calls for reflection (ولم يتفكروا, etc.).
This role is about motivation and initiation.
3
Examine the second role: purification of reason
The author explains that humans are composed of reason, ignorance, and desires from the environment. Revelation corrects and purifies reason from these influences. The example verse (ولا تتبع الهوى) shows how revelation guides reason away from desires.
Purification is necessary because reason is not infallible.
4
Examine the third role: development of reason
Development occurs through contemplating the integrated system of Islam: its legislations, ethics, values, and practical principles. This leads to discovering natural laws, harnessing nature, and building civilization.
This shows revelation as a source of intellectual growth.

Five Roles of Revelation in Guiding the Intellect
Author enumerates five functions of revelation regarding the intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the five roles revelation plays in relation to the intellect and explain how each role contributes to Islamic education.

Core Idea
Revelation awakens, purifies, develops, protects, and liberates the human intellect.

How does revelation interact with human reason? The author introduces a comprehensive framework: revelation is not opposed to intellect but rather fulfills five essential functions that enable the intellect to operate correctly within Islamic education. This lesson walks through each role and its practical meaning.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the first role: Awakening the intellect
Find where the author mentions 'إيقاظ العقل' (awakening). This refers to Qur'anic verses that energize and stimulate the intellect to perform its higher operations. Note that the author says these verses are 'كثيرة جداً' (very many).
2
Identify the second role: Purification of the intellect
Locate 'تزكية العقل' (purification). The author states that humans are composed of intellect, ignorance, and desires; revelation, being infallible, corrects and cleanses the intellect from environmental corruptions. The example given is the prohibition of following desire (Qur'an 38:26).
3
Understand the third role: Development of the intellect
Find 'تنمية العقل' (development). This intellectual growth occurs through studying the integrated system of Islam—laws, morals, values—which leads to discovering natural laws (sunan), harnessing nature, and building civilization. The word 'Iqra'' (Read) symbolizes this scientific civilization.
4
Pinpoint the fourth role: Protection of the intellect
Look for 'حماية العقل' (protection). Since intellect is one of the five necessities (al-daruriyyat al-khams), Islam safeguards it by prohibiting alcohol and anything that leads to its loss.
5
Isolate the fifth role: Liberation of the intellect
Find 'تحرير العقل' (liberation). This derives from the philosophy of tawhid: the Qur'an instructs Muslims not to be influenced by erroneous societal norms, thereby fostering both liberation and creativity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
الأولى إرشادنا إلى الوحي والتصديق بالنبوة.
الثانية: القيام بإدراك الموحى به وتفهمه.
وهذا كفيل ببيان أن لا تعارض بين علوم النقل وعلوم العقل
وهنا نلاحظ أن العقل بالنسبة إلى التربية الإسلامية طليق في حركته منضبط بالوحي، فيكبح جماحه عن الشطط أو الذهاب بعيداً خارج دائرة حركته فالوحي للعقل بمثابة صمام أمان يصونه عن الانزلاق فيما لا يعنيه، وينذره بنقطة الخطر. إذا ما تجازو حدود المناطق الآمنة.
ثانياً - دور الوحي في العقل
ويمكن تلخيص دور الوحي في العقل بالأدوار التالية:
1 - إيقاظ العقل: وهذا يتضح من خلال الآيات التي جاءت تحث العقل على القيام بعملياته العليا وهي كثيرة جداً (سبق إيراد جانب كبير منهـا عنـد الحديث عن العقل).
٢- تزكية العقل: حيث إن الإنسان مكون من عقل و جهل وشهوات تفد إليه من بيئته الخارجية فلا بد أن يقوم مصدر معصوم بعمل تقويم وتزكية لهذا العقل غير المعصوم نتيجة اختلاطه بهذه المؤثرات البيئية. ومثال ذلك قول الله سبحانه: ﴿وَلا تَتَّبِعِ الْهَوَى فَيُضِلَّكَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ.. ﴾ [ص: ٢٦/٣٨].
تزكية العقل وتتم هذه التنمية العقلية من خلال النظر في منظومة الإسلام المتكاملة تشريعات وأحكاماً وأخلاقاً وقيماً ومبادئ عملية تعمل على تنمية وإنهاض العقل باتجاه اكتشاف السنن وتسخير الطبيعة وإعمار الحياة وبناء الحضارة. ولذلك فمن الطبيعي أن تلي عملية التنمية عمليتا التذكير والتزكية، عن طريق العلم الذي أولاه القرآن خاصة اهتماماً متميزاً، ترمز إليـه كلمة (اقرأ) كإيذان بافتتاح حضارة علمية شاملة، فيها البناء والإعمار، ،والإحياء، والإصلاح، والتجديد.
- حماية العقل ولما كان العقل أحد الضروريات الخمس فإن الإسلام قد صانه حين حَرَّم الخمر، وكذلك حَرَّم كل أمر من شأنه أن يؤدي إلى ذهاب العقل وفقدانه.
-٥ تحرير العقل وذلك انبثاق من فلسفة تحرير الإنسان جذرياً تمهيداً لتوحيد الله - تعالى - وعبوديته والقرآن مليء بالآيات التي تبين عدم تأثر المسلم بأعمال المجتمع الخاطئة فلا يخشاها ولا يحاكيها، مما يبعث على التحرير والإبداع معاً(۱) (سبق إيراد جملة من الآيات).
وحاصل القول: إن ركيزة الثوابت الوحي، وركيزة المتغيرات العقل. فالأهداف والغايات يمثلها محور الثوابت، أما المرونة والمتغيرات فتمثلها الوسائل والأساليب المتغيرة تبعاً للزمان والمكان. ولذا كان هذا منطقة عمل العقل. ومن ناحية أخرى يشتغل الوحي في قضايا الأصول والكليات، في حين يشتغل العقل في قضايا الفروع والجزئيات وذلك على نحو عام.
وينعكس ذلك عملياً في ميدان التربية الإسلامية على النحو التالي: يقوم العقل الإنساني بالتفاعل مع الكون بشتى صور التفاعل الإيجابي كالتأمل والتجريب لمحتوياته الحسية والإفادة من ذلك في أداء أدوار الإنسان الاستخلافية على الأرض، في ضوء توجيهات الوحي وإرشاداته.
Chapter Three, Section Three: Revelation
First: Guiding us to revelation and affirming prophethood.
Second: Undertaking the perception and understanding of what is revealed.
This suffices to show that there is no contradiction between transmitted sciences and rational sciences.
Here we note that intellect in relation to Islamic education is free in its movement but regulated by revelation, which restrains its excesses or going far outside its circle of movement. So revelation for the intellect is like a safety valve that protects it from slipping into what does not concern it and warns it at the point of danger if it exceeds the boundaries of safe zones.
Secondly: The Role of Revelation in the Intellect
The role of revelation in the intellect can be summarized in the following roles:
1 - Awakening the intellect: This is evident from the many verses that urge the intellect to perform its higher operations (a large part of which was previously cited when discussing the intellect).
2 - Purification of the intellect: Since man is composed of intellect, ignorance, and desires that come to him from his external environment, an infallible source must perform a process of correction and purification for this non-infallible intellect as a result of its mixing with these environmental influences. An example of that is the saying of God Almighty: "And do not follow desire, for it will lead you astray from the way of God..." [Sad: 38:26].
Development of the intellect: This intellectual development occurs through consideration of the integrated system of Islam: legislations, rulings, morals, values, and practical principles that work to develop and raise the intellect towards discovering the sunan (natural laws), harnessing nature, building civilization. Therefore, it is natural that the processes of reminder and purification follow the process of development, through knowledge to which the Qur'an gave special attention, symbolized by the word "Iqra'" (Read) as an announcement of the opening of a comprehensive scientific civilization, in which there is building, construction, revival, reform, and renewal.
- Protection of the intellect: Since the intellect is one of the five necessities, Islam protected it when it prohibited alcohol, and also prohibited everything that might lead to the loss and disappearance of the intellect.
-5 Liberation of the intellect: This emanates from the philosophy of radically liberating man as a prelude to the tawhid of God Almighty and His worship. The Qur'an is full of verses that show that the Muslim is not affected by the wrong deeds of society, not fearing them nor imitating them, which leads to liberation and creativity together (a number of verses were previously cited).
The conclusion: The pillar of constants is revelation, and the pillar of variables is the intellect. The goals and ends are represented by the axis of constants, while flexibility and variables are represented by the means and methods that change according to time and place. Hence, this is the field of the intellect's work. On the other hand, revelation operates in issues of principles and universals, while the intellect operates in issues of branches and particulars, in a general manner.
This is practically reflected in the field of Islamic education as follows: The human intellect interacts with the universe in various forms of positive interaction, such as contemplation and experimentation of its sensory contents, and benefiting from that in performing man's vicegerent roles on earth, in light of the guidance and directives of revelation.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the relationship between divine revelation (al-wahy) and the human intellect (al-‘aql) within the framework of Islamic education. The author begins by stating two preliminary matters: first, that revelation guides us to itself and to the affirmation of prophethood; second, that we must undertake to perceive and understand what is revealed. This establishes that there is no contradiction between transmitted and rational sciences. Then, the author introduces the central point: the intellect in Islamic education is free in its movement but regulated by revelation, which acts as a safety valve, restraining excess and warning of danger.

Next, the author enumerates five specific roles of revelation regarding the intellect:
1. Awakening the intellect: Revelation contains verses that urge the intellect to perform its higher operations, energizing it.
2. Purification of the intellect: Because humans are composed of intellect, ignorance, and desires influenced by environment, revelation, being infallible, corrects and purifies the non-infallible intellect. The example is the verse forbidding following desire.
3. Development of the intellect: This occurs through the integrated system of Islam—its laws, morals, and values—which develop the intellect towards discovering natural laws, harnessing nature, and building civilization. The word "Iqra'" (Read) symbolizes this scientific civilization.
4. Protection of the intellect: Since intellect is one of the five essential necessities (al-daruriyyat al-khams), Islam protects it by prohibiting alcohol and anything that leads to its loss.
5. Liberation of the intellect: This stems from the philosophy of liberating man for tawhid. The Qur'an shows that Muslims should not be influenced by erroneous societal norms, fostering liberation and creativity.

Finally, the author concludes with a key principle: revelation is the basis of constants (thawabit), while the intellect is the basis of variables (mutaghayyirat). Goals and ends are constants, while means and methods are variables that change with time and place. Thus, revelation deals with universals and principles, while the intellect deals with particulars and branches. In practice, in Islamic education, the human intellect interacts with the universe through contemplation and experimentation, using sensory content, to fulfill man's role as vicegerent on earth, all within the guidance of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which role of revelation is directly linked to the prohibition of alcohol?
A) Awakening the intellect
B) Purification of the intellect
C) Development of the intellect
D) Protection of the intellect

Key Takeaway
Revelation plays five fundamental roles in relation to intellect: awakening, purification, development, protection, and liberation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
List the five roles of revelation from memory and for each, provide one Qur'anic verse or example from the passage that illustrates it.
?
Choose one role (e.g., protection of intellect) and explain how it is applied in Islamic law beyond the prohibition of alcohol—think of other rulings that safeguard reason.
